(2) After dropping the prompt literal, the leak class shifted to `70` / `80` — the model reaching for canonical RSI overbought/oversold thresholds when the report didn't print them (NVDA's report cites "above 70 threshold" so it passed; GOOGL's report says "approaching overbought" with no number, so the model leaked "70" from prior knowledge). The category error was on the scorer's side: `RSI > 70 = overbought` is canonical TA convention, not a fact-claim about a specific company — but the hallucination scorer can't tell those apart without help. ADR-012 picks Option B (surface conventions in the report layer, not loosen the prompt or the scorer) and parameterises `_rsi_label` so every bucket prints both 70 and 30 in the report body. Empirical: pre-fix run `20260426T082316Z-d8d42e` showed leak set `{70, 80}` on TA records; post-fix canonical baseline `20260426T091357Z-625e57` shows all `*-technical` records clean and residual leakage on the fundamental/news side (tracked as QNT-137). New baseline retires the QNT-128 16/16 mark — the QNT-133 prompt's mandatory Action line raises the numeric-claim surface area on every thesis, so 12-14/16 with TA-class clean is the honest floor. Side guards: a regression test pins "no multi-digit literals in `SYSTEM_PROMPT`"; a sibling pins the same on every `Thesis.model_fields` description (because `with_structured_output` injects descriptions into the LLM's schema, making them a parallel bleed surface to the prompt body itself). Calibration note: the over-tightened prompt iteration (run `20260426T083425Z-f50e0f` adding "do not write canonical thresholds" rules) collapsed judge from 6.5 → 2.94 with no hallucination improvement — confirming the right layer for the fix is the report, not more rules at the prompt layer.
- [x] Restructure thesis output to Setup / Bull Case / Bear Case / Verdict — QNT-133
    - **Triggered by**: Phase 6 design v2 (TERMINAL/NINE) thesis card. The QNT-58 prompt produced a 5-section narrative (Overview / Technical / Fundamental / News / Conclusion) that read like a checkbox-completed report rather than a research note with a stance. QNT-133 swaps the prompt + state contract: synthesize now uses `with_structured_output(Thesis)` (a Pydantic model with `setup: str`, `bull_case: list[str]`, `bear_case: list[str]`, `verdict_stance: Literal[constructive|cautious|negative|mixed]`, `verdict_action: str`), so the four sections reach the API as typed JSON instead of prose the frontend has to regex. Two design-side risks were locked into the prompt rather than left for the model: (1) **forced symmetry** — bull and bear sections explicitly allow EMPTY when the supplied reports don't argue for that side (verified live: TSLA produced 0 bull / 3 bear, stance=negative, action="no action level supported by current data"); (2) **hallucinated action levels** — verdict guidance must reference numbers verbatim from the technical/fundamental reports, never invented price targets (verified live: V cites SMA-20 307.32 + RSI-14 49.7, UNH cites SMA-50 292.81, AAPL cites SMA-50 260.15 — all from the technical-report body the agent gathered). The CLI keeps its markdown contract via `Thesis.to_markdown()`; the eval harness renders the same way so QNT-67's hallucination scorer keeps pattern-matching numbers without changes. Side fix: the `test_no_raw_llm_invoke_in_agent_package` AST scanner only walked the top-level RHS for `get_llm()`, so a chained `structured = get_llm().with_structured_output(...)` binding would have let `structured.invoke(...)` slip past CI; reviewer-agent caught the gap, scanner now `ast.walk`s the full RHS and two regression fixtures pin the new pattern. Calibration note: when `traced_invoke`'s output handling was widened to JSON-dump pydantic responses, the naive `isinstance(response, BaseModel)` matched `AIMessage` first (langchain messages ARE pydantic BaseModels) and broke an existing tracing assertion — order matters: check `BaseMessage` first, then `BaseModel` for the schema-instance fallback.
- [x] Agent evaluation framework — QNT-67 **[highest-priority Phase 5 item — the single biggest AI-Engineer hiring signal]**
    - Lives under `packages/agent/evals/`. Three eval types — all required, not optional:
    - **(a) Numeric-claim hallucination detector** (`evals/hallucination.py`): regex every number out of the agent's thesis; assert each appears verbatim in one of the report strings the agent received as tool output. Any mismatch = test failure. Operationalises the ADR-003 contract.
    - **(b) Golden set** (`evals/golden_set.py` + `evals/goldens/questions.yaml`): 15–20 curated `(ticker, question, reference_thesis, expected_tools)` pairs. **Coverage invariant: at least one question per ticker in `shared.tickers.TICKERS`** — thin, heavy, volatile, and quiet tickers all exercise the pipeline. Phase 2 retro lesson (`feedback_sample_ac_broadly.md`): a golden set that skews to NVDA/AAPL leaves bugs in UNH/V/JPM invisible to regression. Per run, track LLM-as-judge score + cosine similarity of generated thesis vs reference thesis. Commit `evals/history.csv` so prompt-version quality is visible in `git log -p`.
    - **(c) Tool-call correctness** (`evals/tool_calls.py`): for each golden-set question, assert the expected tool was called — e.g., valuation questions MUST call `get_fundamental_report`, technical questions MUST call `get_technical_report`.
    - Design goal: harness is reusable enough to extract as a standalone repo later.
- [x] Investigate + fix the 3 hallucination findings the QNT-67 baseline flagged — QNT-128
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-67 baseline (commit 1b66e7b, run 20260425T092008Z) flagged 3 records emitting numbers absent from any tool-output report — `amzn-fundamental` (16.09), `unh-fundamental` (89.02 + 99.82), `unh-news` (same UNH numbers). The framework was doing exactly what it should; per the issue body the next step was to classify each finding as (a) rounding / (b) cross-pollination / (c) pretraining leakage / (d) regex false-positive, then apply the matching lever. Replay of all 3 records showed every "hallucinated" number was actually present in the reports as the negative form (`-16.09`, `-89.02`, `-99.82`) — the reports template YoY changes with explicit signs while the model naturally moves the sign into English verbs ("free cash flow declined 16.09%"). Class (d): regex false-positive. Fix: support comparison strips the leading sign before lookup; canonical form (and the `unsupported` listing for `--explain`) keeps it for explainability. Trade-off documented in `hallucination.py`'s "Sign-magnitude support" section and pinned by an `xfail(strict=True)` tripwire (`test_inverted_sign_thesis_should_be_flagged_but_is_not`) — if a future change re-introduces asymmetric sign comparison without a deliberate decision to remove the trade-off, the suite fails loud. Verifying live sweep (run 20260425T142759Z): 16/16 hallucination_ok, 16/16 tool_call_ok, exit 0. Side effect: `litellm_config.yaml` adds Qwen3-32B as auto-fallback for the default Llama-3.3-70B alias (Groq's free-tier daily TPD on Llama is 100K, ~2 sweeps' worth; Qwen-fallback adds 5× more headroom). Llama stays default — Qwen-as-default was tested first and regressed 15/16 → 11/16 hallucination_ok because Qwen rounds numbers and leaks `<think>` reasoning into the thesis content.
- [x] Re-run Llama-3.3-70B bench on a fresh TPD bucket — QNT-138
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-129 follow-up — the production-default `bench-llama3-70b` row in the bench was anchored on a partially-throttled TPD bucket (Groq daily token-per-day cap was already mid-burn from prep sweeps when the canonical run fired), so the reference line carries 7 zero-cosine records from failed syntheses. The bench doc footnotes this as "0.336 (clean) / 0.189 (raw)" — fine for the first publish, but every future model decision references back to that row and a clean reference is worth the rerun. Empirical: clean re-run on `equity-agent/bench-llama3-70b` (run_id `20260427T122411Z-8ebb34`) lands 16/16 hallucination_ok, 16/16 tool_call_ok, judge 4.69, **cosine 0.364** — the highest cosine in the bench, ahead of Scout's 0.342. The pre-registered decision rule (Scout cosine lead ≥ 0.02 OR judge lead ≥ 2.0 → promote) fires on neither: cosine lead is **negative** (-0.022, Llama leads), judge lead is +0.25. Outcome: keep Llama-3.3-70B as default, leave the QNT-129-shipped chain (`equity-agent/default` → `equity-agent/fallback-llama4scout`) intact. The `Two weeks after this PR ships` Scout-promotion gate is removed from the doc's revisit cadence — the question is closed on data, not waited out. Side product: aggregate + token-summary scripts promoted from `/tmp/` into `scripts/evals/` (the doc's "second re-run" trigger fired); aggregate now defaults to latest-sweep-per-alias so the original TPD-truncated sweep + the QNT-138 NVDA probe are both retained in `history.csv` as audit trail without contaminating the doc-publishable numbers. Calibration note: the wall-clock p50 of 8 398 ms looks bad next to Scout's 836 ms but is mostly the per-alias bench TPM cap (5 K TPM on `bench-llama3-70b`) queueing late-record plan calls — per-call Langfuse latency was 311 ms, ~2× Scout's 169 ms (real but not the 10× the wall-clock implies); the production default has no such cap, so the 2× per-call edge is the only signal that survives a clean comparison and isn't enough to disrupt months of production track record.
- [x] Bench free-tier candidate models against QNT-67 goldens (portfolio artifact) — QNT-129
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-128 retro lesson — the Qwen3-32B fallback was promoted on a *capacity* signal (5× the default's TPD) without checking quality first; only after the fact did a re-run on the goldens find Qwen had regressed 15/16 → 11/16 hallucination_ok. Wrong sequence (capacity-then-quality instead of quality-then-capacity) and exactly the gap a portfolio reader of `litellm_config.yaml` would notice on inspection. This ticket establishes a repeatable bench whose output is the artifact every future model-selection decision references back to. Plumbing: 7 dedicated `equity-agent/bench-<model>` aliases in `litellm_config.yaml` plus an 8th `bench-llama3-70b` reference alias added during the run (so the production model gets a fair within-bench comparison line on the same prompt_version as every candidate — the QNT-128 baseline `f1aa25` was on a pre-QNT-133/QNT-136/QNT-137 prompt and re-using it would have anchored every candidate to the wrong target). Per-bench-alias `rpm` and `tpm` set at ~80% of each provider's published cap so the proxy queues over-cap requests instead of returning 429 — the eval sees latency, not failures. Harness: a single `--model` flag on `python -m agent.evals` plumbs the alias through a module-level `set_model_override()` in `agent.llm` so plan, synthesize, and the LLM-as-judge call all hit the model under test in one process; the alias suffix encodes into the run_id so per-model aggregates over `evals/history.csv` work without a schema column. Empirical: 8 sweeps × 16 records = 128 new history rows; Llama-4-Scout-17B wins every comparable measure (16/16 hallucination_ok, judge 4.94, cosine 0.342, p50 elapsed 836 ms) versus Qwen3-32B's 12/16 hallucination_ok and Llama-3.3-70B's 9-clean-records 0.336 cosine / 1 110 ms p50. Qwen confirmed unsafe (4 records with invented magnitudes for AAPL P/E, JPM EPS, UNH headlines, plus a Groq function-call collapse on META synthesize). Two candidates self-disqualified through the harness: gemma-3-27b-it has no JSON-mode support so every synthesize call 400'd into an empty thesis (cosine 0.000 across all 16 — the unambiguous tell that `hallucination_ok=16/16` was vacuous), and gemini-3.1-flash-lite-preview hit upstream 429s on 3/16 records despite a `rpm: 12` cap below the published 15. Recommendation landed in same PR: `equity-agent/fallback-qwen3` → `equity-agent/fallback-llama4scout` (same provider/key, 5× the default's TPD, strictly better than Qwen on every measure). Holding off on Scout-as-default — its lead over Llama on cosine is sub-noise (+0.006), the lead on judge is biased by self-judging, and Llama has months of production track record vs Scout's zero. Two bench-surfaced follow-ups filed in the doc but out of scope for the ship: (1) `traced_invoke` drops `model_name`/`usage_details` for `with_structured_output` responses since they aren't `AIMessage`, so reported "total tokens" is a lower bound on every Langfuse trace today, not just bench; (2) the prose references in `goldens/questions.yaml` underestimate cosine for the post-QNT-133 four-section thesis structure and should be re-shaped at next bench cycle. Calibration note for next time: I should have caught the reference TPD truncation before publishing the doc — the reference row's raw cosine 0.189 was 7/16 zeros from failed syntheses, not pure format drift; reviewer-ediff flagged this and the fix-commit's "0.336 (clean) / 0.189 (raw)" framing makes it audit-trail-visible. Output artifact: `docs/model-bench-2026-04.md` is the doc, structured so "why this model" is answerable in <30s; README link from QNT-66 captured in the doc's Follow-ups section.

### Phase 6 — Frontend
**Scope**: Next.js terminal-style dashboard (TERMINAL/NINE design v2), ticker detail with TradingView charts, persistent agent chat panel. Deployed on Vercel.
**Dependencies**: Requires Phase 3. Requires Phase 5 for agent chat panel (depends on QNT-133 structured thesis output). News card gracefully degrades if Phase 4 not complete.
**Design reference**: `docs/design-frontend-plan.md` is the canonical UI spec — locks the three-pane layout (watchlist / detail / analyst), the elements each pane owns, the EOD framing (no live-tick chrome), and the field substitutions (EBITDA margin for op margin, ROE/ROA for ROIC, Quarterly/Annual/TTM tabs, no FWD).

- [x] Phase 6 frontend design assessment + canonical mocks — QNT-135 **[lands BEFORE any architecture or page work]**
    - **Triggered by**: Phase 5 → Phase 6 hand-off — design intent was scattered across `project-requirement.md`, ad-hoc mocks, and Slack-style notes; without a single canonical artifact every Phase 6 ticket would have re-litigated the layout. Shipped `docs/design-frontend-plan.md` as the locked spec (three-pane layout: watchlist / detail / analyst, EOD framing, field substitutions: EBITDA margin for op margin, ROE/ROA for ROIC, Quarterly/Annual/TTM tabs, no FWD) plus the canonical mock set. Every subsequent Phase 6 ticket references this doc by section instead of re-deriving the design; QNT-121's rendering-mode ADR, QNT-72's watchlist, QNT-73's detail page, and QNT-74's chat panel all consume it as input.
- [x] ADR-014: Next.js rendering mode per page (SSG / SSR / CSR) + cache strategy — QNT-121 **[written BEFORE any page code]**
    - **Slot drift fixed 2026-04-27 (Phase 5 retro)**: original ticket title was ADR-012, but ADR-012 went to QNT-136/137 (domain conventions in reports) and ADR-013 to QNT-104 (no Coolify); next free slot is ADR-014.
- [x] ADR-015: News-source + sentiment topology — QNT-140 **[written BEFORE QNT-72/73 consumer pages; gates QNT-131 / QNT-132]**
    - **Triggered by**: Phase 5 retro Phase 6 review — QNT-131 (`pending` sentiment state) and QNT-132 (subsystem provenance via `/health`) both carry "blocked on news-source decision" disclaimers. Decision is binary on two axes (news source: Finnhub vs AV `NEWS_SENTIMENT` vs current RSS; sentiment topology: async downstream asset vs in-line dep vs ships-with-news payload). Land before any consumer page so the provenance strip + news cards are wired against the real shape, not an assumed one.
    - Phase 4 retro carry-over: the Dagster quickstart-topology arc (QNT-100 → QNT-116, 17h across 4 incidents) and Qdrant point-ID arc (QNT-54 → QNT-120) both burned hours because the prod-vs-tutorial gap surfaced at deploy, not design. Next.js app-router has the same shape — SSR-by-default + RSC boundaries + SSE streaming don't all compose.
    - Each page/panel names: rendering mode, data-fetch location (RSC vs client vs API route), cache / revalidate strategy, and failure-mode rendering. Watchlist sidebar likely RSC + ISR; ticker detail middle pane SSR with client-side toggles; chat panel CSR + `fetch`/`ReadableStream`. **Also decides**: persistent right-pane chat (per design v2) vs `/chat` route — recommend persistent panel.
    - Output: `docs/decisions/014-nextjs-rendering-mode-per-page.md` — every subsequent Phase 6 ticket references it by section.
- [x] Initialize Next.js app in `frontend/` with Tailwind CSS — QNT-71
- [x] **Phase 6 backend support: indicators + fundamentals + sparkline + SPY** — QNT-134 **[gates QNT-72 + QNT-73]**
    - New indicators: SMA200, ADX(14), ATR(14), OBV, Bollinger %B, MACD bullish-cross flag.
    - Fundamental additions: EBITDA margin (substitutes op margin), gross/net margin bps deltas, TTM rollup asset (rolling-4Q sums of revenue / net income / FCF / EPS).
    - Sparkline field on `GET /api/v1/dashboard/summary` (60 daily closes per ticker — server-side, no N+1 client calls).
    - SPY benchmark ingest as a `BENCHMARK_TICKERS` constant — OHLCV-only, skipped from fundamentals/news/sentiment assets.
- [x] **News ingest migration: Yahoo RSS → Finnhub `/company-news`** — QNT-141 **[gates QNT-72 + QNT-73 news cards; per ADR-015]**
    - Schema migration 012 adds `publisher_name` + `image_url` + `sentiment_label` columns to `equity_raw.news_raw` (existing dedup key `(ticker, published_at, id)` unchanged).
    - Ingest rewrite: replace Yahoo RSS with Finnhub `/company-news` per partition; map `source` → ingest provenance, `publisher_name` → originating outlet, `image_url` → `image`, `sentiment_label` → `'pending'` (column exists per QNT-141 schema; QNT-131 classifier deferred — values stay `'pending'` indefinitely).
    - One-time 1y backfill on first run (Finnhub free tier explicitly allows 1y history per `freeTier: "1 year of historical news and new updates"` in the docs JSON).
    - `FINNHUB_API_KEY` added to `Settings` + `.env.example` + SOPS prod (per QNT-102).
    - Side-by-side density check (Finnhub vs RSS for one ticker, one week) before cutover; verify `news_embeddings` re-runs cleanly on Finnhub rows (point-id formula from QNT-120 is source-agnostic).
- [x] **Bound `news_embeddings` to recent + delta-only upsert — protect Qdrant free tier post-QNT-141** — QNT-142 **[durable fix for the QNT-141 backfill blast radius; calibration multiplier surfaced via `feedback_full_refresh_multiplier.md`]**
    - Switch `_FRESH_WINDOW_SQL` from `fetched_at >= now() - INTERVAL 7 DAY` to `published_at >= now() - INTERVAL 7 DAY` so the 28k-row Finnhub backfill (all `fetched_at = today`, 1y of `published_at` history) drops out of Qdrant scope. Pre-fix projection: 168k inferences/day, ~93x the calibrated free-tier budget.
    - Add delta-only upsert: scroll existing point IDs per ticker via `qdrant.scroll_ids` and skip rows whose `point_id(ticker, url_id)` is already indexed. Steady-state ticks now embed only new articles since the last tick.
    - Symmetric-window count check: both sides of `news_embeddings_vector_count_matches_source` scope to the same 7-day `published_at` window so neither the 1y CH backfill nor aged-out Qdrant points (no GC) lock the tolerance check into permanent WARN. Adversarial review (QNT-142) caught the Qdrant-side asymmetry that would have started false-failing within ~9 days otherwise.
    - Out of scope: Qdrant garbage-collection of points whose `published_at` aged past the window (the orphan check has the same monotonic-growth shape; needs a follow-up if `equity_news` storage starts tracking toward the 4 GB free-tier cap). News ingest schedule resume happens in Dagster UI post-deploy.
- [x] **Shift `news_raw_schedule` from 4h cadence to daily (02:00 ET)** — QNT-143 **[aligns ingest cadence with design v2 EOD framing; cleans the only sub-daily schedule in the project]**
    - `cron_schedule` flips from `0 */4 * * *` to `0 2 * * *` in `packages/dagster-pipelines/src/dagster_pipelines/schedules.py`. 7-day-per-week (no weekday filter) — news happens on weekends too (after-hours announcements, weekend macro, earnings warnings).
    - Aligns with `docs/design-frontend-plan.md` push-back #1 ("Drop the 'LIVE / 8ms / 5s refresh' framing") and the QNT-72 bottom-left status `EOD · 02:00 ET`. Post-QNT-142 the 4h cadence was functionally cheap (delta-only upsert), but cheap-and-aligned beats cheap-and-vestigial.
    - Inference token budget drops from ~270k/mo (5% of free tier) to ~70k/mo (1.4%); Dagster runs/day from 60 to 10; clean of overlap with ohlcv_daily (17:00 ET) and fundamentals_weekly (Sun 22:00 ET).
    - QNT-93 freshness check `_MAX_INGESTION_LAG_HOURS` bumped from 24h to 48h (2× cadence) — tighter would flap right before each next tick now that cadence equals the prior threshold.
- [x] **`dagster.yaml` env_vars drifted from Settings post-QNT-141 — bidirectional CI guard** — QNT-144 **[durable fix for the silent run-drop discovered while verifying QNT-143's first manual tick]**
    - Adds `FINNHUB_API_KEY` to `dagster.yaml` `run_launcher.config.env_vars` (QNT-141 added the key to `Settings` + `.env` + SOPS but skipped the DockerRunLauncher passthrough; per-run containers spawned by the cron started without the key and silently dropped at launch). Run history confirms 60 queued news_raw runs were dropped between 2026-04-27 16:00 UTC and discovery on 2026-04-29.
    - Strengthens `tests/dagster/test_run_launcher_env_vars.py` with the inverse-direction invariant: an explicit `ASSET_REQUIRED_SETTINGS` allowlist of Settings keys read inside DockerRunLauncher-spawned containers must be a subset of `env_vars`. QNT-125's existing forward direction (`env_vars ⊆ Settings`) caught QNT-59's drift but missed QNT-141's because it only checked one direction. Sweep clean today: `FINNHUB_API_KEY`, `QDRANT_URL`, `QDRANT_API_KEY`, `CLICKHOUSE_HOST`, `CLICKHOUSE_PORT`.
    - Unblocks QNT-143 AC-5 + AC-6 live verification on the next news_raw tick post-deploy.
- [x] **Qdrant GC: delete `news_embeddings` points whose `published_at` aged past the 7-day window** — QNT-145 **[converges Qdrant on ADR-009's literal rolling-7d definition; closes the QNT-142 out-of-scope advisory before it could trip the orphan check]**
    - Adds `QdrantResource.delete_points_by_filter(collection, query_filter)` with the same retry semantics as `upsert_points` (transient 5xx / 429 / transport errors retry up to `_MAX_RETRIES`; everything else fails loud).
    - At the tail of `news_embeddings`, derives a single Python-side `cutoff_ts = now - WINDOW_DAYS` and issues a ticker-scoped delete on `published_at < cutoff_ts`. GC runs unconditionally (even on quiet tickers with no fresh CH rows in the window) so a quiet feed cannot keep aged points alive.
    - `aged_ticker_filter(ticker, cutoff_ts)` (Range `lt`) and the QNT-142 count check's `_ticker_within_window_filter` (Range `gte`) form an exact partition at the same anchor: every Qdrant point is either kept or deleted, never both, never neither.
    - Tightens `news_embeddings_no_orphaned_vectors` (QNT-93) to scroll within the same 7-day window — without it the orphan check would silently become a no-op once GC ships, the same monotonic-growth asymmetry that broke QNT-142's count check before symmetrising.
    - `WINDOW_DAYS` promoted to a module-level constant in `news_embeddings.py` so the CH SQL window, GC filter, count check, and orphan check all reference one value (no risk of one drifting).
    - Pre-deploy verification (2026-04-29 per QNT-142's bucketed-distribution query): 5933 total points across 10 tickers, 923 in the 7-30d bucket. Post-deploy AC: every ticker has 0 points with `published_at < now() - INTERVAL 7 DAY` after the first scheduled tick.
- [x] **News pill: resolve true outlet beyond Finnhub redirect labels** — QNT-148 **[corrects ~78% of weekly news pills mislabelled "Yahoo"/"Benzinga"/"CNBC" by Finnhub redirect; ADR-016 commits the cross-ticker storage + dedup contract]**
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-73 ticker detail shipped with publisher pills reading whatever Finnhub put in `publisher_name` (often "Yahoo" / "Benzinga" / "CNBC" / generic feed-source labels) for `finnhub.io/api/news?id=...` redirect URLs — 4113 of the last week's 5135 news rows. The label can't tell us who actually wrote the article: "Yahoo" routinely covers republished Reuters / Bloomberg / Fool. QNT-73 partially patched the ~22% direct-outlet bucket via `domain(url)`; this ticket honestly resolves the redirect bucket at ingest.
    - Migration `024_alter_news_raw_add_resolved_host.sql` adds `resolved_host LowCardinality(String) DEFAULT ''` to `equity_raw.news_raw`. CD auto-applies on merge (per QNT-146).
    - `news_feeds.py` adds `resolve_publisher_host(url, client)` — HEAD with redirect-follow (5s deadline / 5 hops), GET fallback for 405/501 outlets that reject HEAD (`http.stream("GET", ...)` exits without `.read()` so the body is never fetched), short-circuit for non-finnhub.io hosts. Soft-fails to `''` on any error (timeout, non-2xx, redirect loop). `make_resolver_client()` factory centralises the timeout / redirect-budget config so the asset's pooled client and the resolver's own self-constructed client share one source of truth.
    - `news_raw` asset takes one pooled `httpx.Client` per partition (warm-pool ~30ms vs cold-connect ~150ms per article) and threads it through `_article_to_row`. ~210 calls per ticker per day in steady state, ~80% short-circuit on direct outlets — well under the 2-3 min per-partition budget.
    - `/api/v1/news/{ticker}` returns a single canonical `publisher` field via SQL `multiIf(resolved_host != '', resolved_host, domain(url) NOT IN ('finnhub.io', ''), replaceRegexpOne(domain(url), '^www\\.', ''), trim(publisher_name) != '', trim(publisher_name), '')`. Frontend `news-card.tsx` collapses to `item.publisher || "—"` with no further fallback.
    - **Intra-ticker dedup at API**: `WITH deduped AS (SELECT id, argMax(field, published_at) ... GROUP BY id)` — Finnhub returns same URL across ticks with drifted `datetime` epochs (3 NVDA rows for one article observed in pre-deploy data), and ReplacingMergeTree keys on `(ticker, published_at, id)` so timestamp drift can't be merged at storage. URL-hash equality on `id` is strictly stronger than `(host, headline)` and reuses the existing dedup column.
    - **Cross-ticker storage stays per-mention**: same URL under AAPL and MSFT lands as two rows by design (one per Finnhub `/company-news?symbol=X` mention). Cross-ticker dedup deferred to a future "Related across portfolio" surface — collapsing under one ticker would silently drop the article from the other ticker's feed.
    - **AC #10 (cross-ticker peer-news) deferred** with rationale in ADR-016 §4: Qdrant infra exists (`equity_news` collection + payload `ticker` filter), shipping it well needs a UI design pass against the recently-shipped watchlist + ticker-detail layouts, and marginal value is unclear without first observing how readers use the de-duplicated single-ticker feed shipped here. Revisit trigger: one week post-deploy usage data.
    - Pre-deploy data via tunnel: 7-day window had 5135 rows / 3360 distinct ids → fanout factor 1.528 (cross-ticker mention multiplier); ~78% finnhub.io redirects, ~22% direct outlets. Documented in ADR-016 §Context table.
    - **ADR-016**: cross-store identity table (Finnhub URL → news_raw composite key → Qdrant point ID), per-ticker attribution semantics (Finnhub matches on string-equality of `related[]`, not relevance), dedup contract (URL hash within ticker, no cross-ticker collapse), peer-news deferral. Extends ADR-015's table.
    - Adversarial review caught the GET-fallback `.read()` bug (would have downloaded full article bodies) before merge — refactored to `_fetch_head_or_get` helper that exits the stream context without consuming the body.
- [x] **Ticker detail: responsive labels at narrow viewports + period-aware P/E + simplified quote header** — QNT-153 **[third polish round on top of QNT-151/QNT-152; closed the 14" MacBook layout gap and surfaced one data-quality bug (QNT-154 filed)]**
    - **Triggered by**: After QNT-151 (text overflow) and QNT-152 (chart height + internal card scroll) shipped, the user reported the ticker detail page was still awkward at narrow viewports — TECHNICALS' `Daily/Weekly/Monthly` and FUNDAMENTALS' `Quarterly/Annual/TTM` tab labels overflowed the ~178 px card headers (TTM was being clipped off-screen on the FUND card), and the 5-stat quote-header `dl` was wrapping into 5 vertical rows because `flex-wrap + gap-x-6` was too generous for the ~560 px center pane.
    - **Original plan was abbreviation-only**: `D / W / M` for TECH tabs, `Q / A / T` for FUND tabs (two-span Tailwind pattern with `2xl:hidden` / `hidden 2xl:inline`), `Tech` / `Fund` for card titles below 2xl, `flex-nowrap + overflow-hidden` for the dl. Two-span pattern keeps the diff JS-free (just Tailwind class toggling) and the breakpoint at `2xl:` (1536 px) cleanly separates "external monitor" (full labels) from "MacBook 14"" (1512 px → abbreviated).
    - **Redirected mid-implementation by browser screenshots** (3 rounds):
        - Round 1 shipped, but `justify-center + overflow-hidden` clipped both edges of the dl at narrow widths (Open + Mkt cap + P/E TTM all cropped, only "0 - 210.30 VOL 223.74M" visible) and at 1920 px the 5 stats still overflowed → `flex-wrap` dropped P/E TTM to row 2 (awkward 4+1 split).
        - Round 2 fixed `justify-start` + tightened `gap-x-4` at 2xl+ + dropped Mkt cap/P/E below 2xl. Layout no longer broken but P/E still got clipped at 1920 px on borderline displays.
        - Round 3 (final): user redirected: the OHLCV strip below the chart already shows Open / Day range (= H/L) / Volume — header dl was a redundant duplicate. P/E is a valuation ratio that belongs in the Fundamentals card, not the quote header. Mkt cap is the same axis as the cap-tier chip, can ride alongside as the precise number. Quote header simplified to just identity (left) + price (right); `Stat` component deleted; `dl` removed entirely.
    - **Period-aware P/E in FUND card** — first row of the dl, label travels with the displayed period: `P/E` (Annual = price / annual EPS), `P/E annualised` (Quarterly = price / (Q EPS × 4) — single-quarter extrapolation, label flags it explicitly), `P/E TTM` (TTM = price / TTM EPS). Replaced the original "render `pe_ratio_ttm` regardless of tab" stub. New `peCell(row, price)` helper at the bottom of the file mirrors the existing `roeRoaCell` pattern but returns `{ label, value }` because the label varies, not just the value. Edge cases handled: null price → `—`, null EPS → `—`, denom (after × 4 if quarterly) === 0 → `—`, negative EPS → negative P/E (correct financial convention).
    - **Cap chip absorbs Mkt cap precision**: `<span>{capTier}<span className="ml-1 normal-case text-zinc-400">· {capValue}</span></span>` reads as `MEGA-CAP · 5.06T` — the `uppercase tracking-wider` outer chrome carries the chip identity while the inner `normal-case` span keeps the number readable.
    - **Surfaced QNT-154** (Backlog, no milestone): JPM quarterly + TTM rows ingest as zeros (revenue=0, net_income=0, ebitda=0) because yfinance returns banks' P&L in a Net-Interest-Income shape rather than the conventional Revenue/COGS/EBITDA tree. Annual is fine. Out of scope for this ticket (frontend renders what API returns); ADR-style triage decision (sector-aware empty-state vs bank-field mapping vs drop bank tickers) deferred to whoever picks up QNT-154.
    - **AC scope evolution noted on the Linear issue**: original AC #4 (`flex-nowrap dl`) and AC #5 (`Stat shortLabel + 'vs 30d' suffix`) were superseded by the redesign. AC #1-3 (tab/title abbreviations) shipped as planned. AC #6 (tsc clean) green. AC #7-9 (browser viewport tests at 1280/1920) verified by user across 3 review rounds.
- [x] **Price chart: 1M/3M/6M/YTD buttons zoom (not filter), older candles stay accessible** — QNT-155 **[surfaced 2026-05-01 during QNT-153 testing; TradingView-convention fix]**
    - **Triggered by**: clicking a range preset (1M / 3M / 6M / YTD) on `/ticker/{ticker}` was sliced data via `filterByRange` and passed the slice to `series.setData(...)`. Older candles were physically absent from the chart's internal dataset, so panning left hit a white void — broke the standard TradingView interaction model.
    - **Fix shape**: dataset and viewport are now decoupled. The full back-adjusted candles + volume + indicators reach `setData(...)` on every render; range presets resolve to a `[from, to]` window and call `chart.timeScale().setVisibleRange(...)` (or `fitContent()` for MAX) inside a separate effect. YTD anchors at `Date.UTC(year(latestBar), 0, 1)` per the issue spec. `filterByRange` deleted; replaced by `computeVisibleRange` which returns viewport bounds, not slices.
    - **Effect ordering**: data-push effect declared before viewport effect, both depend on `[candles]`; React commits them in declaration order so `setData` always runs before `setVisibleRange` within a single flush. Manual pan/pinch persists across renders because nothing in the viewport effect's deps changes when the user drags — only a preset click or a data refresh re-applies the viewport.
    - **SPY anchor tradeoff**: pre-fix SPY normalised against the first bar of the visible *slice* (re-anchored on range change — TradingView "Compare" convention). Post-fix anchors at full-extent first bar — simpler, line stable across zoom. If per-window 0% baseline is wanted back it's a separate ticket; comment in the file points there.
    - **Cross-ticker range persistence kept intentional** (AC #8): the `range` state lives on `PriceChart` and survives ticker swaps. A user comparing two stocks at the same window shouldn't have to re-click the preset on every watchlist hop. The viewport re-applies to the new dataset via the same range effect.
    - Adversarial reviewer (code-reviewer-ediff) returned SHIP with five non-blocking advisories; the only one I acted on was a misleading SPY-anchor comment I had written (claimed re-anchoring "defeats the comparison" — false; re-anchoring is the TradingView convention). Re-worded.
    - Author-verified all four [dev exec] AC in browser at /ticker/NVDA: 1M zoom + pan-left reveals older candles, MAX no refetch, ticker-switch preserves range, crosshair + indicator overlays render on older bars.
- [x] **Price chart: per-pane legends so sub-panes are self-identifying** — QNT-157 **[surfaced 2026-05-01 alongside QNT-155 testing; TradingView-convention follow-on]**
    - **Triggered by**: with the chart now showing up to 4 sub-panes (RSI / MACD / ATR / OBV) the panes were unlabeled — user had to remember which colored line was which, and 3 of the 4 indicators (RSI / ATR / OBV) had no value readout anywhere on the page (the header `indParts` block only covered SMA / BB / MACD). Standard TradingView convention is a small per-pane legend in the top-left that names the indicator and shows its current value at the hovered bar.
    - **Fix shape**: lightweight-charts ships no built-in legend (per the v5 docs page the issue links), so the implementation follows the documented HTML-overlay recipe — append a `<div>` to the chart container, position absolute, write `textContent` on every `subscribeCrosshairMove` tick. Pure formatters (`mainLegendText` / `rsiLegendText` / `macdLegendText` / `atrLegendText` / `obvLegendText`) live in their own `price-chart-legend.ts` module so they can be tested without spinning up a canvas. The chart-side effect owns DOM lifecycle: tear down on every dep change, build legends per current overlay set, re-pin Y offsets via `pane.getHeight()` summation, expose an updater closure through `updateLegendsRef` so the mount-time crosshair handler reads the latest per-bar lookup without re-subscribing.
    - **Anchoring tradeoff** (caught one-screenshot-into-impl-review): pane elements from `IPaneApi.getHTMLElement()` don't establish a positioning context (lightweight-charts lays panes out as `<tr>`/`<td>` children of an internal `<table>` — `position:absolute` on a child of an unstyled row falls through to the viewport, which is exactly what the first paint did — every legend stacked at the page top-left over the watchlist sidebar). Fix: anchor all legends to `containerRef` (the React-managed wrapper, which we explicitly set to `position: relative`) and compute pane Y offsets from `pane.getHeight()` accumulation. ResizeObserver on the container catches the responsive 300px↔400px breakpoint; the indicator-effect's `setStretchFactor` reflow is caught via the shared `overlays` dep on this effect.
    - **Design iteration during impl review**: shipped four UI revisions in the same impl session as the user eyeballed each candidate — (1) one-line crowded legend → (2) two-row wrap (ticker+SMA / BB+SPY) → (3) four-row split (ticker / SMA / BB / SPY) → (4) ticker + Vol dropped from the chart legend entirely (both already shown in the quote header above and the OHLCV crosshair readout, respectively). Final layout: main pane shows one row per toggled-on overlay group only; sub-panes (RSI / MACD / ATR / OBV) carry their own dedicated legend; OhlcReadout simplified from two rows to one (header now owns ticker + OHLCV + Vol + change; per-pane legends own SMA / BB / SPY / RSI / MACD / ATR / OBV).
    - **Test infra (new)**: added `npm test` script using Node 24's built-in `node --test` runner with native `.ts` support (type-stripping) and `node:test` + `node:assert/strict` — no vitest / jest / tsx dependency added. Tradeoff: ESM forces explicit `.ts` extensions on relative imports, so `tsconfig.json` gained `allowImportingTsExtensions: true` (safe pairing with the existing `noEmit: true`). 6 tests exercise every formatter (RSI / MACD / ATR / OBV / Main) plus the main-legend toggle matrix; satisfies AC #7 and gives future frontend tickets a zero-config path to add unit tests on pure modules.
    - **Adversarial-reviewer fixes**: code-reviewer-ediff agent flagged one BLOCKING (SPY%-anchor consistency between `spyOverlayLine` and the legend's % calc) and two ADVISORY (cleanup leak risk on parent-route unmount; `pane.getHeight()` returning stale 0 on the first frame after a `setStretchFactor` reflow). All three fixed: SPY anchor switched to `spyLine[0].value` so the legend tracks whatever convention `spyOverlayLine` uses; first `repositionAll()` wrapped in `requestAnimationFrame` so it reads post-layout heights; cleanup explicitly `el.remove()`s legend divs and nulls `updateLegendsRef.current` on unmount. (The "blocking" was technically equivalent in current shape because `backAdjusted` copies `adj_close` into `close`; the fix is defensive against a future change to either side.)
    - User-verified all four [dev exec] visual AC at /ticker/UNH and /ticker/NVDA: each sub-pane carries its labelled legend, main pane shows toggled-overlay groups only, crosshair-off falls back to most-recent bar, no candle overlap at any of 1/2/3/4 sub-pane stretch ratios.
- [x] **Price chart polish round (post-QNT-157 user-test bundle)** — QNT-158 **[surfaced 2026-05-01 during QNT-157 user-testing; one-PR bundle of five chart-correctness fixes]**
    - **Triggered by**: five small chart-correctness items the user flagged in quick succession after QNT-157 shipped — bundled into one ticket per the "don't split trivial follow-ups" pattern (every change touches the same `frontend/src/components/ticker/` files). Filed under QNT-158 mid-session once the change-set crossed the "trivial cosmetic" threshold; the user's "lump sum into one ticket" call confirmed the bundling.
    - **MACD histogram bars**: standard TradingView MACD pane is line + signal + histogram of `(macd - macd_signal)`. We were already surfacing the Hist value in the per-pane legend (added by QNT-157), but the bars themselves were missing — visually inconsistent. Adds a `HistogramSeries` on the MACD pane coloured green when the value is positive (bullish momentum) and red when negative; same pane index as the line + signal so they reflow together. New `MACD_HIST` key in the sub-pane teardown set so it gets cleaned up on overlay toggle.
    - **RSI 70 / 30 reference lines**: ADR-012 calls 70 / 30 the canonical RSI thresholds, but the pane had no visual cue for them — the user had to trust the right-axis scale. Adds two `series.createPriceLine(...)` calls on the RSI series itself (not the pane) — red dashed at 70, green dashed at 30, axis labels disabled per user preference. Lifecycle is automatic: lines disappear with the series when RSI is toggled off.
    - **Pane-drag legend tracking**: when the user dragged a divider between panes the heights changed but the container didn't, so the single `ResizeObserver` on the container missed the event and legends stayed at their pre-drag Y positions. Fix: in addition to the container, also `resizeObs.observe(p.getHTMLElement())` for every pane. ResizeObserver collapses duplicate notifications, so observing both surfaces is cheap and catches both the responsive 300px↔400px container breakpoint AND user-dragged pane reflows.
    - **Coloured legend (SMA / BB / SPY) + SPY label, no %**: the legend was monochrome zinc-300 — user couldn't visually link a number to its line on the chart. Each indicator name+value is now wrapped in a `<span style="color:..."> ` matching its series colour (SMA20 amber-400, SMA50 amber-500, SMA200 amber-600, BB↑/·/↓ all violet-400, SPY sky-400). The previous `SPY +44.33%` was anchored to the first loaded bar so the absolute % swung whenever the user changed the range preset (1M vs 5Y vs MAX) — misleading; replaced with a bare `SPY` label only (right-axis price label still carries the live value). Required switching `mainLegendText` → `mainLegendHtml` and the renderer from `textContent` to `innerHTML` so spans can be coloured; values all controlled (`toFixed` numbers + constant hex strings) so XSS surface is nil.
    - **Compact OBV right-axis**: OBV magnitudes commonly run into the billions (NVDA OBV ~5.9B); the default plain-number axis label showed "5918115640.22" which overran the right-axis gutter. Custom `priceFormat` via `fmtBigNum` (re-exported from `price-chart-legend.ts`) compacts to "5.9B" / "-2.1M" / etc. Other indicator panes keep default formatting (RSI 0-100, MACD small ±N, ATR small +N) — only OBV has the axis-overflow problem.
    - **Per-pane axis interaction (clarification, no code)**: user discovered that `wheel-only` doesn't scale a pane's price axis. Confirmed this is by-design: lightweight-charts' `mouseWheel` is bound to time-axis zoom; per-pane price scaling is via `axisPressedMouseMove.price` (click+drag on the right-axis), which is enabled by default. Same gesture model as the full TradingView app.
    - **Reviewer's wager paid**: QNT-157's adversarial-reviewer pre-empted exactly the pane-drag concern with an ADVISORY ("ResizeObserver fires when the container resizes but not when internal pane heights settle"). I ignored it on the QNT-157 ship because user-dragging a divider isn't a typical interaction — the user demonstrated otherwise within an hour. Confirmed pattern: reviewer-flagged advisories on UI ergonomics deserve a tighter triage even when not blocking.
    - User-verified all five [dev exec] visual AC at /ticker/NVDA: histogram bars render under MACD line/signal, 70/30 dashes appear on RSI pane with no axis labels, dragging a pane divider shifts every legend in real time, SMA/BB/SPY legend rows render in their respective line colours with no SPY %, OBV right-axis compacts to K/M/B notation.
- [x] **Watchlist polish: terminal title block + per-ticker logos + middle-pane logo + data: URL inlining** — QNT-162 **[surfaced 2026-05-02 cosmetic + perf round on the watchlist column]**
    - **Triggered by**: Lift the watchlist from "homework project" to "finance tool" framing without functional changes. Adds a Bloomberg-style stacked `Equity Data Agent` / `TERMINAL` title above the rail, Finnhub `/stock/profile2` logos per row with an initials-in-colored-circle fallback for missing logos (deterministic palette hashed on ticker, `<img onError>` swap), the same logo to the left of the big ticker in the quote header, drops the long company name from watchlist rows since the logo IS the recognition cue, and inlines the bytes as base64 `data:` URLs so the browser never round-trips to `static.finnhub.io` — all 10 watchlist logos + the quote-header logo arrive in one ~70-130 KB JSON response (gzipped: ~50 KB), amortised by a 24h Next Data Cache TTL. Backend caches in-process, pre-warms at FastAPI lifespan in a daemon thread. Code-reviewer-ediff caught two BLOCKING concurrency bugs pre-merge (lock held across HTTP I/O during cold-start; sync route inline-populated under that lock, starving uvicorn workers) — fixed by separating populate-only `_populate_lock` from lockless GIL-safe dict reads and bounding the request handler on a `threading.Event` set by the prewarm thread (30s ceiling, no Finnhub I/O on the request path); also caught SSRF via attacker-controlled logo URL, pinned to `https://static.finnhub.io` before the second GET. AC #6 ("no regression in scroll/click/selection") verified interactively during dev — user navigated AAPL → MSFT → TSLA and confirmed selection/hover/overflow scroll intact.
- [x] **Logos broken in prod: Finnhub now returns static2.finnhub.io, SSRF allowlist only permits static.finnhub.io** — QNT-163 **[surfaced 2026-05-02 from QNT-161 dev API logs spam — every ticker logged "host mismatch"]**
    - **Triggered by**: After QNT-161 shipped, dev API logs surfaced `finnhub logo URL host mismatch for <TICKER>: 'static2.finnhub.io'` for all 10 watchlist tickers + quote header. Finnhub had sharded their CDN; QNT-162's strict equality SSRF allowlist (`hostname == "static.finnhub.io"`) rejected every URL → cache stored `None` for every ticker → frontend served the colored-initials fallback instead of the real logo. Fix: replaced the constant with a `^static\d*\.finnhub\.io$` regex using `fullmatch`, accepting `static.finnhub.io`, `static2.finnhub.io`, and any future `staticN.finnhub.io` shard while still rejecting subdomain spoofs (`static.finnhub.io.evil.com`), suffix tricks (`static.finnhub.io2`), tld swaps (`static.finnhub.com`), non-numeric variants (`staticx.finnhub.io`), and non-https URLs. 13 new regression tests in `tests/api/test_logos.py` (4 accepted shards × parametrised, 9 rejected look-alikes × parametrised) lock the SSRF guard so a future "let's just allow ``*.finnhub.io``" sweep doesn't silently widen the surface. Pattern-not-example fix per `feedback_fix_pattern_not_example.md`: regex anticipates Finnhub's next shard rather than playing whack-a-mole on `static3`, `static4`, etc. **Follow-up in PR #181 (same ticket per "don't split trivial follow-ups")**: post-deploy verification surfaced JPM still returning null because its logo (83 KB) exceeded QNT-162's `_MAX_LOGO_BYTES = 64 * 1024` cap. The cap was set on a "real Finnhub PNGs come in around 5-15 KB" assumption that didn't hold for the larger-cap-icon brands (banks, healthcare). Bumped to 128 KB; added a regression test that pins the cap at >= 1.5× the largest observed legitimate logo (currently JPM at 83 KB) so a future tightening sweep can't silently re-break the same ticker class.

Date-range toggle 1M / 3M / 6M / YTD / 1Y / 5Y / MAX (no 1D/5D — EOD only). Indicator overlay chips: SMA / BB / RSI / ATR / OBV (no VWAP). SPY benchmark overlay (default off).

- [x] **Analyst chat (right pane)** — QNT-74
    - Persistent right-rail panel that follows the active `/ticker/[symbol]` route (per ADR-014 §4 + Anti-pattern §6: chat is part of `app/layout.tsx`, not a `/chat` route — a route would tear down in-flight SSE on every ticker navigation).
    - `POST /api/v1/agent/chat` SSE endpoint streams `tool_call` / `tool_result` / `prose_chunk` / `thesis` / `done` events. **No Vercel AI SDK** — native `fetch` + `ReadableStream` + optional `eventsource-parser` (~2KB).

    - Inline data chips in agent prose (`+2.45% · close 4/24` style).

- [x] **Agent chat SSE: production-hardening follow-up (disconnect cleanup, LLM timeout, error sanitization)** — QNT-150 **[QNT-74 adversarial-review punch list — six advisories that didn't block ship, bundled because they share an operational concern: the SSE path can hang or leak under failure modes the happy-path tests don't exercise]**
    - **Triggered by**: Adversarial review of QNT-74 surfaced six production-hardening advisories that did not block ship at the time. Filing them together because they share an operational concern: the chat SSE path can hang or leak resources under failure modes the happy-path tests don't exercise. (1) Client-disconnect cleanup — the `_stream` drain loop ran without a `try/finally`, so a browser disconnect mid-stream (FastAPI raises GeneratorExit) left `runner_task` running, burning LLM quota and a thread-pool slot until the graph naturally finished. Fix: wrap the entire drain + post-graph phase in `try/finally`; cancel `runner_task` and `await asyncio.shield(runner_task)` with `contextlib.suppress(CancelledError)` on every exit path. `asyncio.to_thread` can't actually kill the thread, but cancelling the asyncio task releases the queue + emitter so no further frames pile up after the SSE consumer is gone. (2) Top-level LLM timeout — `agent.llm.get_llm()` returned a `ChatOpenAI` with no `timeout`, so a hung LiteLLM proxy stalled the SSE connection forever. Fix: `LLM_REQUEST_TIMEOUT` (60s, free-tier-shaped) bounds every per-LLM call; `CHAT_RUN_TIMEOUT` (240s, ~4x per-call) bounds the whole run via a deadline check inside the drain loop and surfaces an explicit `agent-timeout` SSE error code. (3) Error sanitization — emitting `f"agent error: {type(exc).__name__}: {exc}"` to the client could leak LiteLLM auth-token strings, internal URLs, and stack context. Fix: stable user-facing constants (`_ERROR_DETAIL_AGENT_FAILED`, `_ERROR_DETAIL_AGENT_TIMEOUT`); raw exception detail only via `logger.exception`. Same treatment for the per-tool-failed event — graph-recorded `errors[name]` strings (which can carry `[error] http: 500 ... at http://api.internal:8000/...` from `agent.tools._format_error`) are now logged at WARNING and replaced with a stable `"<Tool> failed."` payload. (4) Stance-pill fallback — `STANCE_PILL[thesis.verdict_stance]` had no default; an unknown stance from a provider hallucination would render a pill with `undefined` className. Fix: `stancePillClass()` helper with `?? STANCE_PILL.mixed` so the runtime guard fires at the JSON.parse boundary even when a hallucinated stance slips past TS narrowing. (5) `done` event contract — module docstring listed `errors` in the payload but the emitted event omitted it (the TypeScript `DoneEvent` already did). Fix: docstring rewritten to match the actually-emitted shape (`{tools_count, citations_count, confidence}` plus `intent` once classify has run; pre-classify failures emit done without `intent`, matching the TS optional). (6) Streaming-race coverage — existing tests used a synchronous fake `invoke` that returned immediately, so the race between `runner_task.done()` and pending `call_soon_threadsafe` callbacks wasn't covered. Added `test_streaming_race_async_worker_drains_cleanly` (50ms tool delay) plus `test_client_disconnect_cancels_runner_task` (drives `_stream` directly, asserts the captured runner_task transitions to cancelled after `gen.aclose()`) and `test_run_timeout_emits_agent_timeout_error` (1s budget, asserts `agent-timeout` code + sanitized detail). Reviewer-agent (code-reviewer-ediff) caught two issues mid-pass: (a) the per-tool-failed error path bypassed the sanitization constants — fixed in the same PR with a `caplog`-based regression test; (b) the success-vs-failure `done` payload diverged silently on `intent` — fixed by clarifying the docstring contract so all three (TS type, docstring, emitted payload) agree on intent being optional.
- [x] **Agent chat SSE: emit intent event from classify_node so streaming label is correct from frame 0** — QNT-159 **[QNT-156 follow-up surfaced during user testing the same day; one-line user-visible bug, two-line root-cause]**
    - **Triggered by**: User testing QNT-156 noticed the chat panel's per-intent streaming label always read "streaming thesis…" regardless of which question they asked, even on comparison and conversational runs. Root-cause: `agent_chat.py:_stream` was only yielding the `intent` event AFTER `graph.invoke` returned (i.e., after every tool_call/tool_result event had already streamed), so `run.intent` was null in the panel for the entire tool-gathering phase and the label fell back to its default. The classify node runs FIRST in the LangGraph state machine and is fast (under 200 ms heuristic, under 800 ms with LLM) — its output was just being held back. The fix is option-1 from the QNT-159 ticket scope: add an optional `event_emitter: Callable[[str, dict], None] | None = None` kwarg to `build_graph`; the classify node calls it the moment intent resolves; the SSE wrapper provides an emitter that posts onto the existing asyncio queue via `loop.call_soon_threadsafe` (mirroring the QNT-74 tool-instrumentation pattern — same queue, same drain loop, same thread-safety primitive). Post-graph yield kept as an idempotent safety net for stubbed test graphs that bypass classify_node. CLI / eval harness pass no emitter; default None means zero behaviour change for those callers. Reviewer-flagged regression guard: the SSE-side ordering test is structurally tautological because the stubbed `_fake_build` calls the emitter itself, so a regression where production `classify_node` stops calling the emitter would leave the test green — added three direct unit tests on `build_graph` (pin emit-on-success, pin BLE001 swallow on a broken emitter, pin no-op behaviour when emitter is None) so the production code path is the thing under test. Verified end-to-end against live LiteLLM with one golden per intent: thesis judge=7, quick_fact judge=9, comparison judge=8, conversational judge=8, all hallucination + tool_call clean — additive change, evals path is untouched.
- [x] **Agent: extend intent set with comparison + conversational + domain-redirect fallback** — QNT-156 **[follow-on to QNT-149; closes the two visible gaps the two-intent baseline left]**
    - **Triggered by**: Two visible failure modes still in the chat panel after QNT-149 shipped — (1) open-ended asks like "Tell me about UNH" got the heavy four-section thesis even when the user wanted a quick read; (2) off-domain asks ("hi", "what can you do?", "what's the weather?") returned a thesis built from whatever reports the agent could fetch — noise, not a redirect, and zero guidance about what the agent CAN answer. QNT-156 extends the two-intent classifier to four shapes: adds `comparison` (multi-ticker side-by-side via a new `ComparisonAnswer` Pydantic schema with per-ticker sections + a qualitative differences paragraph; ADR-003 enforced — the LLM never computes a synthetic ratio or delta the reports don't already state) and `conversational` (greetings / capability asks / off-domain via a new `ConversationalAnswer` schema with short prose + an optional list of three example questions drawn from the agent's actual capabilities). Heuristic extended (multi-ticker + comparison phrase → comparison; greeting / capability / clearly-off-domain phrase → conversational; safety net: a conversational phrase paired with a covered ticker mention defers to the LLM, blocking false positives like "help me understand NVDA's RSI"); LLM classifier prompt + IntentDecision schema cover all four. Synthesize node now branches on intent and — critically — every failure surface (no reports gathered, structured-output crash, comparison parse failed) routes through a deterministic `domain_redirect` helper that builds a `ConversationalAnswer` listing covered tickers + biased suggestions, so the panel never sees a stack trace or blank state again. Conversational hard rule: NO digits in the answer body (the hallucination scorer treats one as a regression since there are no reports to cite); the helper guards `reason` at construction time so a future caller can't accidentally embed a status code or year. Two new SSE events (`comparison`, `conversational`) and two new chat-panel cards (`ComparisonCard` side-by-side; `ConversationalCard` with click-to-resubmit suggestion buttons); thesis + quick-fact cards stay hidden when their respective payloads are absent (same conditional pattern proven in QNT-149). Eval harness extended to render any of the four `to_markdown()` shapes; `prompt_version` hash widened to cover all four system prompts so a regression on any path is observable in `evals/history.csv`. Two new goldens (one comparison, one off-domain conversational) — live run against LiteLLM produced 2/2 hallucination_ok, 2/2 tool_call_ok, judge=8/10 each. Reviewer-agent caught two structural issues pre-merge: (1) `_hint_from_intent("quick_fact")` returned a label that didn't exist in the suggestion bank, silently degrading every quick-fact-failure redirect to the unbiased default — fixed to map to "technical" (where most quick facts live) with a regression test that asserts every intent's hint resolves to a real bank label; (2) `domain_redirect` accepted an unconstrained `reason: str` with no digit guard — fixed with a boundary assertion + regression test pinning the contract.
- [x] Adapt agent response shape to question intent (skip forced thesis on quick-fact prompts) — QNT-149
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-74 manual testing — the chat panel rendered the same heavy four-section thesis whether the user asked "should I be cautious about META?" or "what's the RSI right now?". The graph forced every input through `plan -> gather -> synthesize -> Thesis`; the user's `message` only nudged plan selection, not output shape. Net effect: rigid, ignores the question, every answer looks the same. The fix turns the plan-stage shape contract into a runtime decision: a `classify` node lands in front of `plan` (so the topology is now `classify -> plan -> gather -> synthesize`) and picks one of two response shapes per run. Two-layer classifier (cheap heuristic short-circuits the obvious cases; LLM-fallback via `with_structured_output(IntentDecision)` resolves the ambiguous middle), bias-to-thesis on every failure mode (LLM exception, malformed shape, observability-stack crash) so the QNT-67 hallucination + QNT-128 golden-set contracts cannot regress because of a misbehaving classifier. New `QuickFactAnswer` Pydantic schema (answer + cited_value + source) parallels `Thesis` and travels through the same structured-output path; the synthesize node branches on intent. Plan prompt bias also flips: thesis over-fetches, quick-fact narrows to the one report that answers the question (live: "What's the RSI right now?" → plan gathered `technical` only, skipping `fundamental` + `news`, finishing in 779 ms vs ~2 700 ms for thesis runs). API surface: two new SSE events — `intent` (one-shot routing preamble fired right after classify so the panel can pre-empt layout) and `quick_fact` (full QuickFactAnswer payload mirroring the existing `thesis` event); the thesis card hides when the run has no `thesis` payload, and a new compact `QuickFactCard` renders the short answer + monospaced cited-value chip when `quick_fact` arrives. Eval harness extended to render either `Thesis.to_markdown()` or `QuickFactAnswer.to_markdown()` so the hallucination/judge/cosine scorers see a real string regardless of shape; `prompt_version` hash widened to cover both system prompts so a regression on either path is observable in `evals/history.csv`. Live golden run (`20260501T162326Z-41e742`): 3/3 hallucination_ok, 3/3 tool_call_ok, judge=9 on the new `nvda-quickfact-rsi` golden vs judge=7 on the thesis goldens — clean signal that quick-fact-shaped questions get a tighter answer once they're routed to the right path. Reviewer-agent caught two structural issues that pre-merge: `classify_node` originally lacked the `BLE001` exception guard the other LLM-calling nodes wrap their calls in (a Langfuse SDK fault would have killed the run instead of biasing to thesis); and a bare `price` heuristic token would have silently mis-routed "price target" / "price action" questions to `quick_fact` against the bias-to-thesis contract — both fixed in the same PR with regression tests pinning the corrected behavior.

    - QNT-141 — News ingest migration (Yahoo RSS → Finnhub `/company-news`); lands the schema columns (`publisher_name`, `image_url`, `sentiment_label`) that QNT-72/73 news cards consume. Per ADR-015.
    - QNT-131 — **Deferred 2026-04-28 to Backlog.** Classifier scoped to FinBERT (local CPU inference, no LLM coupling) when revisited. News cards in v1 ship without the `pend` chip. Trigger: UX evidence the chip is load-bearing, or thesis-eval signal that per-article sentiment moves the needle. See ADR-015 §"Revision history" (post-QNT-141, alongside QNT-142). The `sentiment_label` column from QNT-141 stays in place defaulted to `'pending'` for the future revisit.
    - QNT-132 — ✓ **Done 2026-04-28.** `/api/v1/health` provenance block (gates the bottom strip on QNT-73). **Trimmed 2026-04-28** to `sources` + `jobs.next_ingest_local` only. SENTIMENT/AGENT rows dropped — sentiment is `null` post-QNT-131 deferral; agent runtime is a constant. The remaining 2-line strip still carries the "no hardcoded UI strings" architecture signal on the values that actually flip (vendor swap, schedule shift). Suffix derived from the schedule's `execution_timezone` (single source of truth) — change the schedule, the strip flips.

- [ ] Generate TypeScript types from FastAPI's `/openapi.json` via `openapi-typescript` (`make types`) — do not handwrite types in `lib/api.ts`
- [x] **Public-chat abuse prevention: rate limit + per-IP cost cap + auth model + CORS lockdown** — QNT-161 **[gates QNT-75; landed before the public deploy because the Hetzner chat endpoint becomes an availability-bomb the moment the URL leaks]**
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-75 (Vercel deploy) makes `POST /api/v1/agent/chat` reachable to anyone who lands on the deployed frontend. Pre-QNT-161 the endpoint had no rate limit, no auth, no per-IP token budget, a permissive `*.vercel.app` CORS regex, and only the QNT-156 4000-char message cap as a guard. The threat model isn't a runaway monthly bill (Groq is free tier) — it's demo uptime. A scraper that exhausts Groq's daily TPD = the agent stops working = every subsequent recruiter sees a broken demo until quota reset = portfolio bounce. ADR-017 commits the project to **option (a) truly public** — no API key, no signup — because any auth wall destroys the one-click recruiter flow. Defense-in-depth instead: SlowAPI per-IP rate limit (`5/min, 30/hr, 100/day` with 429 + `Retry-After`), in-memory per-IP daily Groq token budget (~10K tokens/IP/day) + global TPD circuit breaker (~50% of model TPD) — both with UTC-midnight reset, both surfacing a deterministic conversational-redirect SSE event on exhaustion (no graph invocation, no LLM cost). Token tracking via a `contextvars.ContextVar`-bound `TokenUsageTracker` that the agent's `get_llm()` reads and attaches as a LangChain callback — propagates through `asyncio.to_thread` automatically. CORS allowlist tightened from open `*.vercel.app` regex to a project-pinned origin set + `CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGIN_REGEX` env (so leaked previews for unrelated Vercel projects can't drive traffic). Prompt-injection input filter (Pydantic field validator) rejects C0/C1 control chars and overlong-token (>500 char) runs. Frontend chat panel surfaces a small `demo: ~30 queries/hour per visitor; powered by Groq free tier` hint so the cap is set as expectation BEFORE 429s land; 429 path serves the SlowAPI JSON detail string verbatim. Sentry burst-alert hooks (`record_burst_alert` / `record_breaker_trip`) wired ahead of QNT-86 — minimal `sentry_sdk.init` guarded by `SENTRY_DSN`; without DSN, alerts log at WARNING. **FAIL CLOSED contract** locked by `tests/agent/test_litellm_fail_closed.py`: walks `litellm_config.yaml`, audits every chat-reachable alias + their fallback chain, asserts only Groq / Gemini / Google providers — a future contributor adding an Anthropic alias trips a CI failure. 33 new tests (27 in `test_security.py`, 5 in `test_litellm_fail_closed.py`, plus 4 patches to existing tests for the tightened CORS) covering: per-IP budget exhaustion → conversational redirect, global breaker trip → redirect + Sentry alert, redirect doesn't charge tokens (avoids billing-the-apology), 6th request in 60s returns 429 with friendly body, control-char rejection (NUL/BEL/ESC/DEL × 4), overlong-token rejection, newline/tab allowed, CORS regex allows pinned project + denies unrelated, burst alerter dedup + per-IP isolation, token tracker integration (post-run debit by observed spend), Sentry capture falls back to log when DSN unset. **Code-reviewer-ediff caught 3 BLOCKING issues pre-merge** — fixed in the same PR with regression tests: (1) `slowapi.util.get_remote_address` returned Caddy's container IP behind the reverse proxy (collapsed every visitor into one rate-limit + token-budget bucket), replaced with custom `client_ip()` reading `X-Forwarded-For` (leftmost) → `X-Real-IP` → `client.host`; (2) the LiteLLM config audit's permit-`groq/openai/` filter used `text.find("openai/")` once globally, suppressing any `anthropic/` violation when a single `groq/openai/` token existed elsewhere — switched to `re.finditer` with per-match position check; (3) `set_token_tracker` ran before the outer `try/finally`, so a `build_graph` crash mid-construction left a stale `contextvar` bound to the request task — moved inside the try with a `runner_task` None-guard in finally. End-to-end manual verification on real uvicorn: 100 reqs no XFF → 5 × 200 + 95 × 429; 10 reqs with distinct XFF → 10 × 200 (each treated as a separate IP, locking the per-IP fix).
- [x] **Deploy frontend to Vercel** — QNT-75 **[Phase 6 deploy ticket; ADR-018 commits the project to a free Cloudflare quick tunnel over a paid named-tunnel domain]**
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-71 (Next.js scaffold) and QNT-161 (public-chat abuse prevention) both Done — the gating prereqs cleared. Original Phase 6 plan assumed buy-a-domain + Caddy + Let's Encrypt for HTTPS termination on the FastAPI side, but for a portfolio piece the ~$10/yr ongoing cost and DNS-management overhead were cost-without-benefit. ADR-018 picks Cloudflare's free quick-tunnel mode instead: `cloudflared` runs on Hetzner with `--url http://api:8000`, makes an outbound connection to Cloudflare, and Cloudflare assigns a `*.trycloudflare.com` HTTPS hostname that the Vercel frontend reads via `NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL`. Net effect: end-to-end HTTPS for $0, FastAPI port :8000 closed to the public internet (bound to `127.0.0.1` only), free Cloudflare WAF + DDoS protection sit in front of the API. The single trade-off: trycloudflare hostnames rotate on every cloudflared restart — with the image pinned to `2026.3.0` and `restart: unless-stopped`, rotation in practice happens 1-2× a year (kernel reboots, deliberate version bumps). Recovery runbook in `docs/guides/vercel-deploy.md` is ~5 min: read new URL from `docker logs cloudflared`, paste into Vercel env, redeploy. Caddy retained under a dormant `prod-caddy` profile so the named-tunnel + own-domain upgrade path stays one-command activatable. **Code-reviewer-ediff caught 3 BLOCKING issues pre-merge** — fixed in the same PR: (1) cloudflared image was `:latest` (floating tag would silently rotate the URL on every deploy + risk breaking-change pulls), pinned to `:2026.3.0` matching the litellm pin pattern in the same compose file; (2) `restart_if_changed "Caddyfile" caddy` in `deploy.yml` would silently no-op after the profile move (compose `--profile prod restart caddy` doesn't see services in `prod-caddy`), removed with a comment explaining the dormant-profile rationale; (3) `docker compose --profile prod up -d --build` was missing `--remove-orphans`, so the existing caddy container would have lingered indefinitely after the profile move — added the flag, eliminating the manual ssh cleanup step the deploy guide originally documented. CORS infra inherits from QNT-161 with no code change required (allowlist + project-pinned regex already in `packages/api/src/api/security.py`); the `.env.example` documents both `CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS` and `CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGIN_REGEX` for the prod env file. Reviewer's advisory items deferred as non-blocking: cloudflared in `docker compose ps` could surface false DOWN alerts (recovers fast in practice); `depends_on: service_healthy` semantics on container recreate are best-effort (acceptable in steady state); trycloudflare URL is in docker logs (acceptable, docker group is restricted on prod). Operational shape — the four ACs are all post-deploy verifications the user owns: Vercel project link, env var, CORS allowlist edit in `.env.sops`, browser-side dashboard check.
- [x] **Cross-cutting**: Ticker list is sourced from `GET /api/v1/tickers` across every page (watchlist, detail-page switcher, chat-panel selector) — never hardcoded. Inherits QNT-78's ⏳ PENDING AC; hardcoding the list anywhere defeats the endpoint's purpose. Phase 3 lesson. **Verified 2026-05-02 via prod walkthrough**: watchlist server-fetches from `/api/v1/tickers`; chat-panel selector pulls the same list; no hardcoded ticker arrays in `frontend/src/`.
- [x] Verify: Watchlist renders 10 tickers + SPY with sparklines; ticker detail shows quote header / chart / technicals / fundamentals / news / provenance strip with all data; chat panel streams tool calls in real time and renders structured thesis; provenance strip values flip when a config value changes (QNT-132 verification). **Verified 2026-05-02 in prod** via https://equity-data-agent-ynr2.vercel.app — all surfaces render with live data; CORS preflight returns the Vercel origin; SSE chat streams tool calls + structured thesis end-to-end.
