### Phase 7 — Observability & Polish
**Scope**: Tracing, alerting, and production hardening.

- [x] Observability stack: Dozzle logs UI + Prometheus/Grafana/cAdvisor metrics — QNT-103 **[unified log/metrics dashboards on top of the per-IP rate-limit and breaker-trip alerting that QNT-161 already wired in Phase 6; QNT-86 (Sentry) lands first — see Phase 6 retro phase-review notes for the dependency ordering]**
    - **Triggered by**: Apr 19 2026 retro — unified logs UI + resource trend visibility are the observability surfaces missing from the current setup. Enables diagnosing slow leaks before they become outages.
- [x] Integrate Sentry for FastAPI error tracking (`sentry-sdk[fastapi]`, uses `SENTRY_DSN` from `.env`) — QNT-86
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-161 wired the abuse-control hook surfaces (`record_burst_alert` / `record_breaker_trip`) and a minimal `sentry_sdk.init` guarded by `SENTRY_DSN` ahead of this ticket, leaving release tagging, chat-stream error capture, and PII-scrub verification to land here. Phase 6 retro (2026-05-02) re-scoped the AC away from a greenfield init toward COMPLETING what QNT-161 stubbed: `release=settings.GIT_SHA`, `traces_sample_rate=0.1`, `auto_session_tracking=True`, `send_default_pii=False`. Chat SSE error paths from QNT-150 now forward via a new `sentry_capture_exception` helper — graph crashes are captured with the original exception object (preserving the worker-thread traceback that FastAPIIntegration's auto-capture middleware never sees), timeouts are captured as a synthetic `TimeoutError` so they cluster in the same Sentry issue keyed by ticker + budget. Added `/api/v1/_debug/sentry` verification endpoint gated on `settings.ENABLE_SENTRY_TEST` in prod (default off so a scraper looping on the path can't burn the 5K errors/mo free-tier quota; flip to 1 for one deploy when verifying, then revert). The `cors_aware_exception_handler` was extended to forward to Sentry explicitly because a registered `Exception` handler can short-circuit FastAPIIntegration's auto-capture on some sentry-sdk paths — Sentry dedups by stack-trace fingerprint so the redundant call is harmless. Promoted `GIT_SHA` from raw `os.environ.get(...)` to `Settings.GIT_SHA` and swept the existing `_health_payload` callsite for consistency. 12 new tests covering init kwarg shape (release / sample rate / session tracking / PII scrub), debug endpoint gating (404 in prod without override; raises in dev), `_sentry_capture_exception` no-op when DSN unset + DSN-set forwarding + SDK-failure swallow, and the chat SSE error → Sentry forwarding contract (graph crash → original exception forwarded; timeout → synthetic TimeoutError forwarded). Code-reviewer-ediff caught 2 blocking issues pre-merge fixed in the same PR: (1) raw `os.environ.get(...)` for `GIT_SHA` and `ENABLE_SENTRY_TEST` violated the "all config via shared.Settings" rule — promoted both to Settings fields and swept the existing `_health_payload` callsite; (2) a redundant test registered a permanent `/_test/cors_handler_forwards` route on the shared `main_module.app` instance, leaking into every later test — deleted the test since the same code path is covered by `test_debug_sentry_raises_in_dev`.
- [x] Add Dagster alerting on asset materialization failures — QNT-62
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-125 retro (2026-04-24 outage) — 200/200 Dagster runs failed at dequeue for ~20h while host/container alerts stayed silent (queue-drop is a runtime failure mode, not a container or host signal). QNT-125 added the CI guard against env-var drift; QNT-62 closes the sibling alert gap by wiring a `run_failure_sensor` to the existing `DISCORD_WEBHOOK_URL` (originally added by QNT-101 for `docker-events-notify`). Sensor fires once per terminal RUN_FAILURE — op-level `DEPLOY_WINDOW_RETRY` and run-level `DEPLOY_WINDOW_RUN_RETRY_TAGS` both transparently absorb intermediate retries before reaching the sensor. Dedup via `instance.get_run_records` with `(job_name, partition, status=FAILURE, updated_after=cutoff)` filter — current run's own FAILURE is included by Dagster's transition-before-dispatch ordering and excluded explicitly to avoid self-suppression. Dedup window 10 min, query `limit=100` for 10× burst headroom (worst case is one failure per ticker partition). Scope is `(job, partition)` not `(asset, partition)` — equivalent for this repo's jobs (each is single-asset or a tightly-coupled multi-asset group failing as one unit), and multi-asset jobs intentionally produce one alert per stuck partition rather than N. Discord message format mirrors `docker-events-notify.sh` (`[ASSET FAILURE] job=`x` asset=`y` partition=`z` step=`w`` header + fenced exception block + run URL) for visual consistency in the same channel. Settings additions: `DISCORD_WEBHOOK_URL` (shared with QNT-101) and `DAGSTER_BASE_URL` (default `http://localhost:3000` — prod webserver is private SSH-tunnel-only so localhost works for the operator clicking the run link). 11 unit tests cover message shape, dedup query (current-run-exclusion + only-current-run boundary), webhook helpers (truncation / HTTP error / non-2xx swallowing), and sensor integration against `DagsterInstance.ephemeral()`. Code-reviewer-ediff initially returned `FIX FIRST` flagging (1) (asset, partition) vs (job, partition) scope drift, (2) `limit=10` pagination edge if >10 failures land in one window, and (3) dedup test bypassing the real query path via monkeypatch — addressed in the same PR by documenting the (job, partition) scope as intentional, bumping limit to 100 with explicit headroom rationale, and documenting the two-layer test strategy (helper unit-tested directly with stub instance, sensor end-to-end against ephemeral instance for the no-dedup branch).
- [x] Implement retry logic for flaky external API calls (yfinance, news APIs) — QNT-63
    - **Triggered by**: Phase 7 audit found three remaining gaps after the Phase 6 retry surfaces (ClickHouse OperationalError loop, Qdrant transient handler, asset-level RetryPolicy) had landed: (1) yfinance 429 path string-matched the exception message and ignored Retry-After, (2) `fetch_company_news` was single-shot HTTP — a transient 5xx burned a full asset retry slot when the next attempt would have succeeded, (3) `Backoff.EXPONENTIAL` had no jitter on the three external-fetch assets. New `retry_helpers.py` parses Retry-After as either delta-seconds or HTTP-date (RFC 9110 §10.2.3), clamped to a 300s ceiling so a hostile / mis-formatted header can't sleep the asset for hours, and walks `exc.response.headers` defensively so any library that attaches the original 429 response (httpx, requests) flows through the same path — yfinance's `YFRateLimitError` discards the response so the existing fixed-delay fallback still applies there. `fetch_company_news` gains an intra-attempt retry loop (max 2 retries within one asset op = 3 total tries) that retries 429 + 5xx, honors Retry-After when present, falls back to 1s/2s exponential otherwise, and bubbles 4xx auth/bad-symbol errors immediately so the asset doesn't burn budget on permanent failures. All three ingest assets (`ohlcv_raw`, `fundamentals`, `news_raw`) switched from `Backoff.EXPONENTIAL` to `Backoff.EXPONENTIAL + Jitter.PLUS_MINUS` matching `DEPLOY_WINDOW_RETRY`'s pattern. 29 new tests: 18 in `test_retry_helpers.py` cover the parser (delta-seconds, HTTP-date, past-date clamp-to-zero, ceiling clamp, garbage, bytes input, case-insensitive headers, plain-dict fallback, missing-response fallback, plain non-HTTP exception); 11 in `test_external_fetch_retries.py` cover the asset call sites (yfinance 429 with Retry-After sleeps the header value before re-raising, yfinance 429 without header re-raises immediately for the asset RetryPolicy to handle, non-429 failures skip silently per pre-existing behavior, Finnhub single 5xx survives without burning asset retry, three consecutive 5xx bubble to caller, 4xx does not retry, 429 Retry-After drives sleep duration in fetcher, 5xx without Retry-After uses exponential base delay) plus a structural pin on the jittered RetryPolicy on all three assets. Code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP with 5 advisory items (test hygiene around `_make_handler_sequence` bounds + `_disable_finnhub_intra_sleep` autouse footprint; minor RFC divergence on `Retry-After: 0` falling to base delay; per-sleep cap × retry count interaction; pre-existing fundamentals quarterly/annual blocks still swallow 429 — explicitly out of scope per ticket). Out of scope per ticket: ClickHouse and Qdrant retries (already covered in Phase 6).
- [x] Load test FastAPI endpoints (confirm response times under 10 tickers) — QNT-65
    - **Triggered by**: Phase 6 surfaced (and Phase 7 retro confirmed) that demo uptime depends on the QNT-161 abuse-prevention path (rate-limit / per-IP token cap / global Groq TPD breaker / LiteLLM fail-closed), not on endpoint CPU/IO. Two re-scopes followed: (1) Phase 6 swap from generic latency probe to demo-protection load test, then (2) Phase 7 swap from real-TPD-burn to lowered-cap behavioral re-trip. Re-scope #2 (2026-05-06) audited `tests/api/test_security.py` (751 lines) and found every demo-protection AC already covered by unit tests — re-tripping the same code path under load shape adds no signal. Final scope shrunk to a one-off p50/p95/p99 baseline for the 5 read endpoints × 10 tickers loop. Implementation: `scripts/load_test_baseline.py` (asyncio + httpx driver, semaphore concurrency, linear-interp quantiles, latency-on-200-only with err column as canary, >5% error rate exit-non-zero) staged via `scp` to Hetzner `/tmp` then `docker cp`'d into the api container — eliminates SSH + Caddy hops, leaving FastAPI + ClickHouse query latency only. Run record at SHA `6e9ad60` on Hetzner CX41 (2026-05-06): 500 reqs / 0 errors / 14.1 s; quote p50 597 / p95 1112 ms (slowest, stitches OHLCV + 30-bar avg vol + TTM P/E); ohlcv 408/703; indicators 496/711; fundamentals 495/915; news 390/817. None hit p99 < 500 ms — acceptable for current ISR + Vercel deploy-hook architecture (most page loads serve build-time-pinned responses). Demo-protection (`tests/api/test_security.py`) and TokenBudget/SlowAPI race-condition probes documented as out-of-scope with rationale. Code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP with 5 advisory items addressed pre-merge: tightened "no network hop" to "eliminates SSH + Caddy hops" (loopback round-trip still exists), comment on TICKERS divergence from `shared.tickers` + meta-JSON drift detection, clarified warm-up scope (50 reqs, not 500), added latency-on-200 interpretation note, explicit /tmp transient SCP disclaimer per `feedback_prod_hotfix_scp.md`.
- [x] Write integration tests for critical paths (ingestion → calculation → report → agent) — QNT-64
    - **Triggered by**: closes the QNT-148 mock-only coverage gap that surfaced as a prod 500 (`ClickHouse ILLEGAL_AGGREGATION` on a CTE alias collision) — mock-only API tests can't catch CTE alias collisions / `ILLEGAL_AGGREGATION` / GROUP BY scope errors by design. Phase 6 retro (2026-05-02) added an explicit AC: at least one integration test per API router (logos, quote, ohlcv, fundamentals, news, search, agent_chat) that exercises the real ClickHouse client against a fixture-loaded test DB, not a mock. Implementation covers all four critical paths in dedicated test files: Path 1 (ingestion → CH) verifies `ClickHouseResource.insert_df` round-trips for OHLCV / fundamentals / news + `ReplacingMergeTree` idempotency on replay; Path 2 (raw → indicators) runs `compute_indicators` against the committed AAPL fixture, persists, and asserts the snapshot matches expected values at `rtol=1e-6` plus warm-up `Nullable` round-trip; Path 3 (FastAPI) exercises every router via `TestClient` + real `api.clickhouse.get_client` against fixture-loaded data covering reports (×4), data (ohlcv/quote/fundamentals/indicators/news/dashboard), tickers, logos no-key fallback, search Qdrant fallback, health, and agent_chat unknown-ticker SSE — plus a concurrent-query smoke test pinning the `autogenerate_session_id=False` fix; Path 4 (agent → tools → API) monkeypatches `agent.tools.httpx.get` to forward through `TestClient`, covering all `default_report_tools` plus `search_news` end-to-end. Conftest applies `migrations/*.sql` idempotently on session start (so CI runs without a separate `make migrate` step), refuses to run if `equity_raw.{ohlcv_raw,news_raw,fundamentals}` has rows (tunneled-prod safety gate, bypassed by `CI=true`), auto-truncates between tests, and stubs `_fetch_logo_data_url` session-wide so daemon prewarm threads can't race the logos test's `FINNHUB_API_KEY=""` monkeypatch. 35 new integration tests + 2 existing pass in 11.7 s (well under the 5 min AC); full suite (587 tests) passes in 22.2 s. Code-reviewer-ediff caught 2 advisory issues fixed pre-merge: (1) prod-data safety gate originally only scanned `ohlcv_raw`, missing the "fresh prod with news/fundamentals but no OHLCV" bypass — extended to scan all three; (2) `api.qdrant.get_client` `lru_cache` wasn't cleared between integration tests, letting a polluted client from one search test leak into a sibling test's `QDRANT_URL` monkeypatch — added cache-clear to both Path 3 and Path 4 autouse fixtures.
- [ ] Verify: End-to-end run on all 10 tickers, review Langfuse dashboard, confirm no orphaned errors in Sentry

### Post v1 Improvements
**Scope**: Targeted upgrades to the v1 surfaces (agent grounding, report quality) once the core stack ships and feedback starts to land. Each item is incremental — no new phases, no new infra.

- [x] Resolve company names to tickers in the chat parser (not just symbols) — QNT-257
    - **Triggered by**: user testing — "what's the thesis of micron / google / tesla" routed to the clarify node ("Which ticker did you have in mind?"), while the same ask with the symbol ("MU / GOOGL / TSLA") worked. Root cause: every ticker reference in the agent flows through one function — `extract_tickers` (`intent.py`), whose regex was built only from the literal symbols in `TICKERS`, so a plain company name resolved to nothing and the ambiguity gate (`_detect_ambiguity`) returned `needs_ticker`. A recall gap, not a wrong answer — the registry already held every name. Fix adds a conservative `TICKER_NAME_ALIASES` map in `shared/tickers.py` (company + common short name only — Nvidia/Apple/Microsoft/Google+Alphabet/Amazon/Meta+Facebook/Tesla/Micron/Advanced Micro Devices/Intel; deliberately NOT exec names or product brands, which over-resolve in prose — that's why it's separate from `NEWS_RELEVANCE.aliases`) with an import-time coverage assert mirroring `_validate_metadata_coverage`. `extract_tickers` folds name matching into one combined symbol-or-name regex (case-insensitive, alpha word boundary, longest-first alternation, set-deduped), so the WHOLE resolution pipeline — single-ticker, comparison, and the clarify gate — benefits from one change; the old symbol-only `_TICKER_BOUNDARY_RE` is removed (orphan-free). Symbol+name collapse to one entry ("compare Micron and MU" → `["MU"]`); first-occurrence order preserved. **Accepted trade-off (pinned, not fixed)**: a company short name that is itself an English/unit word resolves to the ticker ("tesla coil"→TSLA, "apple juice"→AAPL, "sub-micron"→MU) — inherent to plain-name resolution without context-aware NER (out of scope); the alpha-only boundary is intentional, since blocking hyphens would also drop legitimate "Micron-based"/"Tesla-built". `docs/guides/ticker-lifecycle.md` + CLAUDE.md updated from "three registry structures" to four. code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST → 2 blockers addressed pre-merge: case-insensitively deduped the alternation (the suggested `set()` wouldn't have caught the one real meta/META redundancy), and documented + pinned the common-word false-positive surface (the AC4 word-boundary claim was under-tested). AC7 verified live in dev /chat (tunnel up): each of the three asks, anchored to a DIFFERENT URL ticker (NVDA), drove all tool calls to the NAMED ticker (MU / GOOGL+TSLA / INTC) with zero clarify — proving the name overrides the URL anchor. Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, full `uv run pytest` green (+ new name-resolution, collision-guard, accepted-collision, and alias-coverage tests). Out of scope: exec/product-brand aliases, fuzzy/typo matching, `NEWS_RELEVANCE` changes, clarify-node copy.
- [x] Eliminate duplicate frontend mounts and redundant ticker-page fetches — QNT-246
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #15 and #16. `MobileSectionTabs` now mounts either the active <xl tab content or the >=xl three-card grid, never both; the root layout renders one `Watchlist` through `AppShell` across mobile menu, tablet drawer, and xl rail; client GETs are deduped while in flight so the ticker page emits one daily OHLCV request and one daily indicators request per load. Verified at 390, 820, 1280, and 1536 with browser request counts and screenshots.
- [x] Non-data states: landing market overview + chat empty-state + loading skeletons — QNT-250
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #17 (landing middle pane a vast empty void — "Select a ticker" alone in ~50% of the screen), #21 (chat empty-state suggestions floating in dead space at every size ≥md), #7 (bare "Loading…" lines + empty chart frame while data is in flight). First ticket of the Post-V1 Frontend Enhancement milestone (audit tickets QNT-246–253) to land. (1) Landing (`app/page.tsx`): the lone centered line is replaced by a Market overview — Top gainers / Top losers (top 4 each) derived from `/api/v1/dashboard/summary`, each row a `Link` into the ticker. Stays `force-static`: the fetch uses the apiFetch default (`cache: "force-cache"`), the same URL the layout's Watchlist fetches, so both prerender at build and share Next's force-cache Data Cache entry — no per-request fetch added, and `next build` confirms `/` is still ○ Static. (2) Chat empty-state (`chat-panel.tsx` `EmptyState`): `justify-center` → top-anchored `flex-col gap-4 py-6` under a "Research <ticker>" blurb + "Try asking" label, so the four suggestions read as the opening of a conversation instead of a centered cluster with dead space above and below. (3) Loading skeletons: `technicals-card` (9 rows mirroring the `dl` grid incl. the 2xl decoration column) + `fundamentals-card` (as-of bar + 11 rows) replace "Loading…"; `price-chart` gets a pulsing `absolute inset-0` overlay over the still-mounted canvas (avoids re-initialising lightweight-charts on every ticker swap; CLS stays zero — the canvas already reserves h-[300px]/h-[400px]). Built on Tailwind `animate-pulse`; the existing `prefers-reduced-motion` block was extended to neutralise it. Code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST: fixed a gainers/losers overlap when <8 tickers carry a non-null `daily_change_pct` (`slice(Math.max(4, len-4))` + empty-column guard) and matched the technicals skeleton's 2xl 3-column geometry; the branded focus-ring on the movers links was deferred to QNT-251 (a11y baseline, audit #1) to keep the focus affordance consistent with the existing watchlist convention rather than introduce a one-off. AC1–AC3 verified live in the browser by the user (1280 + 390; skeletons observed under DevTools network throttling). AC5: `node --test` 27 passed, eslint + tsc clean. Out of scope: new backend endpoints, chart-library / SSG-deploy-hook changes.
- [x] Recalibrate responsive breakpoints so technicals/fundamentals cards stop clipping — QNT-248
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #18 + #22 (both measured live in Playwright). Same root-cause family: the dense card-layout tier was gated on Tailwind's default `2xl` (1536px), but the middle-pane card column is only ~264px wide there — so the dense tier turned on before the column was wide enough. #22: at 1536 the technicals decoration chip ("NEGATIVE") overflowed the card by 18px and rendered "NEGATI"; the 2xl onset simultaneously flipped on the 3rd chip column AND the long tab labels (DAILY/WEEKLY/MONTHLY). #18: in the narrow xl column (~1280px, a 195px card) the fundamentals value + delta clipped the card's right edge ("215.94B +65.4" cut, "65.3% (T" cut mid-word). Fix is a single custom breakpoint: `--breakpoint-wide: 110rem` (1760px) defined once in `globals.css` `@theme` as the source of truth for the dense tier. Every dense gate in both cards (technicals chip column + 3-col grid + skeleton 3rd track, both cards' long tab labels + fundamentals YoY/yield suffix) moved from `2xl:` → `wide:`, so the clean 2-col short-label view holds from 1280 to ~1759 and the dense chips+labels appear only on genuinely wide (≥1760) 24"/27" monitors. #18 also needed a structural fix beyond the breakpoint: the value and its delta-pill were separated only by an `ml-1.5` margin — not a line-break opportunity — so "18.0%+16 bps" was one unbreakable run that clipped even with `white-space:normal`. Made the value cell a `flex flex-wrap items-baseline justify-end gap-x-1.5 min-w-0` row so the delta drops to a 2nd right-aligned line under pressure; `gap-x-1.5` reproduces the old 6px spacing when both fit. AC1–AC3 verified live in Playwright on TSLA at 1280/1536/1760 with rect measurements (1280: anyClip=false on annual+quarterly; 1536: chip column hidden, no overflow, 2-col, D/W/M; 1760: chips fit 17px inside the edge, DAILY/WEEKLY/MONTHLY + Quarterly/Annual/TTM, 3-col grid). AC4: zero ad-hoc `min-[1760]`, one `--breakpoint-wide` referenced via `wide:` (8× technicals, 4× fundamentals). AC5: `node --test` 27 passed, eslint + tsc clean. Notable dev-env gotcha (not a code defect): Turbopack's `.next` cache did NOT invalidate when the new `@theme` breakpoint was added — the `wide:` utilities silently failed to compile until `.next` was wiped and dev restarted; prod `next build` compiles from scratch so Vercel is unaffected. Code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP with one actionable advisory (stale "hides below 2xl" comment) fixed pre-merge. AC2 design note: the AC said "chip renders fully inside at 1536", but per the ticket Scope the chip is instead gated off below 1760 — at 1536 there's no chip (clean 2-col), and it returns in full at ≥1760; #22's overflow is gone either way. Out of scope: the chart, card metrics/content, mobile (<xl) layout, the duplicate-mount issue (QNT-246). Unblocks QNT-253 (shared TabStrip refactor — same tab markup).
- [x] Mobile polish sweep: footer wrap, chart label clip, touch targets, reduced-motion scroll — QNT-249
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #23, #19, #20, #12, #11 — surfaced from a real iPhone screenshot + Playwright at 390px. Shared theme: the desktop-dense chrome doesn't tighten enough for a ~390px column. Five fixes across three components. (1) #23 Provenance footer (`provenance-strip.tsx`) wrapped to 2 rows (51px) at 390px; below `md` the "Sources"/"Jobs" prefix words are hidden (`hidden md:inline`), `gap-x-6`→`gap-x-3`, `py-2`→`py-1` — measured 24px single row at 390px, desktop labelled two-column layout unchanged. (2) #19 Chart first time-axis label "May" was clipped to "ay" at the left edge on every viewport. Empirically confirmed the scope's "container padding" idea is inert — lightweight-charts draws the label on the canvas bitmap and self-clips at x<0, so outer padding can't recover it; the working fix is the `timeScale: { fixLeftEdge: true }` create-option, which pins the first bar inside the pane. Dropped `fixRightEdge` to stay surgical (clip was left-only). Smoke-tested MAX/1M/weekly+5Y — clean, and the sparse-data case (range wider than history) now fills the pane instead of leaving left whitespace. (3) #20 Bar-interval "M" pushed off-screen at 390px — the left toolbar group (`flex items-center gap-3`) → `flex flex-wrap items-center gap-x-3 gap-y-1` so the D/W/M group drops to its own row. (4) #12 Toolbar buttons + overlay chips were <44px tap targets; a shared `touch` class (`inline-flex items-center justify-center min-h-[44px] min-w-[44px] md:min-h-0 md:min-w-0`) raises every button to 44×44 below `md` and resets to the dense padding-only look at ≥md (measured 44×44 at 390px, 23px at 1280px). (5) #11 Chat auto-scroll (`chat-panel.tsx`) always used `behavior:"smooth"`; now gated on `matchMedia('(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)').matches ? "auto" : "smooth"`. AC1–AC4 verified live in Playwright at 390px (footer 24px, "May" full, M 44×44 on its own row) and 1280px (dense reverts, prefixes restored). AC6: `node --test` 27 passed, eslint + tsc clean. Code-reviewer-ediff returned no blocking code issues (the FIX-FIRST verdict was an evidence gap it couldn't see — measurements live in the sanity-check comment); its one correctness flag (fixLeftEdge × setVisibleRange on sparse data) was smoke-tested clean. Out of scope: chart/desktop-toolbar redesign, empty-states (QNT-250), breakpoint clipping (QNT-248). Frontend-only diff — prod path is Vercel, not Hetzner.
    - **Post-merge follow-ups** (same ticket, real-device feedback): AC4 (the #12 touch-target work) was **reverted** — on the actual 390px device the `min-w-[44px] min-h-[44px]` enforcement turned every toolbar chip into a boxy 44×44 square (PR #389). Per user preference, mobile now uses the same dense toolbar as desktop; **this intentionally re-opens audit finding #12** (sub-44px tap targets), revisitable later with a taller-only `min-h` (no `min-w`) approach. Then the bar-interval group (D/W/M) was still wrapping onto its own row at 390-430px because dates + gap + interval overflowed the row by ~6px (premature wrap, empty space beside the presets); tightened the mobile-only spacing (`gap-x-2`, divider `pl-2`, date/interval buttons `px-1.5`, all restored at `md:`) so dates + D/W/M share row 1 and the chips take row 2 — clean 2-row toolbar at 393/414/430, desktop unchanged (PR #391). Net surviving fixes from the ticket: AC1 footer single-row, AC2 fixLeftEdge label, AC3 M-reachable (now on the dates row, not its own), AC5 reduced-motion.
- [x] Chat streaming a11y live region + memoize RunBlock for token-level render perf — QNT-247
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #2 (a11y) + #3 (render perf), both in `chat-panel.tsx`, folded into one PR. #3: `RunBlock` was un-memoized, so every streamed token (`narrative_chunk` / `prose_chunk`) re-rendered ALL runs in the tape (up to `MAX_RUNS=20`), not just the streaming one — O(runs) reconciliation per token. Fix: wrap `RunBlock` in `React.memo`. The enabling change was making its props referentially stable across a token update: `run` already keeps identity (`updateRun` maps-and-replaces only the matching id), but `onSuggestion` was passed as an inline arrow `(q) => startRun(q)` that minted a new function every render and would have defeated memo entirely — changed to pass the stable `startRun` useCallback directly (the ticket flagged this "verify"; it needed the fix, not just a check). #2: the streamed agent ANSWER (`NarrativeBubble` / `ProseBlock` / cards) rendered into a plain `<article>` with no live region, so a screen-reader user heard the tool rows + the `role=alert` error path but never the answer. Fix: a single visually-hidden `role=status` / `aria-live=polite` / `aria-atomic` region in `ChatPanel`, fed the most-recent run's answer through a 600ms trailing `useDebounced` so the token storm collapses into one settled announcement (not one utterance per token); the error rail keeps its own assertive `role=alert`, and the `sr-only` region has no `tabIndex`/`autoFocus`/`.focus()` so it never steals focus. New pure helper `announceableAnswer(run)` (precedence narrative → prose → quick_fact answer) split into `chat-run.ts`, unit-tested (6 cases). **The live runtime check earned its keep**: driving a real quick_fact query ("What is AAPL's RSI?") through Playwright against the prod API showed the QuickFactCard render the answer while the live region stayed EMPTY — quick_fact skips narrate (QNT-232 #3) and streams no prose, so my first narrative+prose-only helper left that shape silent to a screen reader (the exact audit-#2 failure, for the card-only path). Added the `quickFact.answer` fallback + a regression test; re-verified live, the `status` node then carried "AAPL's RSI-14 is 44.0, which is neutral (source: technical)." AC2 evidence is that accessibility-tree snapshot. code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST on one BLOCKING claim ("conversational announces nothing") — triaged to a FALSE POSITIVE with backend evidence: `agent_chat.py:1120-1124` (and the fallback redirect at :1173-1176) splits `conversational.answer` into `prose_chunk` deltas, so `proseChunks` IS populated and the prose branch announces it; no fix applied. Its `?? ""`-is-dead-code advisory was also wrong (optional-chaining short-circuit returns `undefined` when `quickFact` is null, so the coalesce is load-bearing). AC4: `node --test` 33 passed; eslint + tsc clean. Frontend-only diff — prod path is Vercel, not Hetzner. Blocks QNT-253 (chat-panel split into card components + shared TabStrip).
- [x] Correctness cleanup: SSG relative news dates + tool_result binding — QNT-252
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #8 + #14, two small correctness items folded into one PR. #8 (the higher-value bug): `NewsCard` is a server component baked into the `force-static` ticker page (refreshed only by the Vercel deploy hook), so `formatNewsDate`'s relative bucket ("Today" / "Yesterday" / "Nd ago") was computed against `new Date()` at BUILD time and froze — an article built as "Today" still read "Today" days later. Fix: drop the relative bucket in the SSG path and render absolute-only ("Apr 28"); rationale documented in `format.ts`. Chose absolute-only over a `"use client"` view-time clock because the news list is otherwise a pure server component and a hydration boundary + mount flash isn't worth a cosmetic prefix inside the 7-day window. Pinned by `frontend/src/lib/format.test.ts` (a 2020 article and an article that WOULD have been "Today" at build both render absolute-only). #14: the SSE `tool_result` was bound to its `tool_call` by first-unmatched-by-name (`row.name === ev.name && !row.result`), which mis-binds if two concurrent calls to the SAME tool are ever in flight. Fix: new pure helper `bindToolResult` (`chat-run.ts`) matches on `started_at`, wired in `chat-panel.tsx`; unit test covers two same-name calls completing out of order. AC3 required a minimal ADDITIVE backend change despite the ticket listing the backend out of scope — the `tool_result` SSE payload carried no correlation key, so `started_at` is now echoed on all three `_post` sites in `agent_chat.py` (and added to `ToolResultEvent`); no tool semantics changed. Backend test asserts each `tool_result` pairs to a `tool_call` by `(name, started_at)` — strengthened from a name-keyed dict after code-reviewer-ediff flagged that the original assertion would silently pass on a same-name collision. AC4: `node --test` 38 passed, eslint + tsc clean; backend suite 1117 passed. Frontend-only user-visible path is Vercel; the backend field rides the Hetzner CD. Out of scope: the SSG / deploy-hook freshness model, the news source/content.
- [x] Accessibility & semantics baseline: labels, color-scheme, skip-link, tab roles, focus ring — QNT-251
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` findings #4, #5, #6, #9, #1, #10 — a baseline a11y + semantics sweep, six small items in one PR. (#4) The chat composer `<textarea>` had only a placeholder, no accessible name → added `aria-label="Message the analyst"`. (#5) The app is fully dark but never declared it, so native form controls / scrollbar gutter / mobile URL bar rendered light → `html { color-scheme: dark }` in `globals.css` PLUS a Next 16 `viewport` export (`colorScheme: "dark"` + `themeColor: "#09090b"` matching the zinc-950 body). Read `node_modules/next/dist/docs/.../generate-viewport.md` first per the AGENTS.md caveat — the `Viewport` export is the correct Next 16 shape (not `metadata.themeColor`, which is deprecated). (#6) No skip-link — keyboard users tabbed the whole watchlist before main → a `sr-only focus:not-sr-only` skip link as the first child of `<body>` targeting `<main id="main" tabIndex={-1}>` (added the id + programmatic-focus target in `app-shell.tsx`, with `outline-none` so the skip destination doesn't ring the whole pane). Kept `focus:` (not `focus-visible:`) deliberately — a skip link should reveal on ANY focus, and it's keyboard-only reachable since it's clipped. (#9) `MobileSectionTabs` buttons had `role=null` → added `role=tablist`/`role=tab` + `aria-selected` + `type="button"`, mirroring the three existing tab groups (technicals/price-chart/fundamentals). (#1) The original code-only audit over-stated the focus-ring gap; the in-browser pass confirmed most controls keep the native ring, so only the three that stripped it (watchlist link, composer, the QNT-250 landing mover-links) got a branded `focus-visible:ring-1 ring-inset ring-emerald-500/60` — the `focus:` → `focus-visible:` swap keeps `hover:bg` for mouse and adds the ring only on keyboard focus. (#10) Composer placeholder `...` → the single ellipsis glyph `…`. **Every AC verified with a real browser** (Playwright + local axe-core@4.10 served same-origin from `public/`, since remote-CDN injection is blocked): theme-color `#09090b` + html computed `color-scheme: dark`; real keyboard Tab → skip link reveals (182×34) → Enter → `activeElement = main#main`, `#main` hash; `Section` tablist with 3 `role=tab` + correct `aria-selected`; second Tab to a watchlist link matches `:focus-visible` with computed `box-shadow: oklab(0.696 -0.162 0.051 / 0.6) 0 0 0 1px inset` (emerald-500/60). axe: **0 critical** on `/` and `/ticker/AAPL` — the only violations were a pre-existing `color-contrast` (serious) on muted zinc-500/600 text, explicitly out of scope ("no full WCAG/axe remediation beyond these items"). code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST on two claims, both triaged out: (1) "skip link should use `focus-visible:`" — rejected, `focus:` is the correct convention for a keyboard-only skip link and `focus-visible:` would regress programmatic-focus reveal; (2) "incomplete ARIA tab pattern (missing `aria-controls`/`role=tabpanel`/arrow-keys)" — explicitly out of scope per the ticket (arrow-key nav deferred), the three existing groups it was told to mirror also omit these, and the agent's prediction that axe would fail was empirically false (ran axe: 0 such violations; `aria-controls` is axe best-practice, not a required attr). AC8: `node --test` 38 passed, eslint + tsc clean; `ruff check` clean (no Python regressions). Frontend-only diff — prod path is Vercel, not Hetzner. Out of scope: full WCAG/axe remediation, ARIA tablist arrow-key nav (future ticket, possibly with the QNT-253 shared TabStrip), restyling controls that already have a native ring.
- [x] Split chat-panel.tsx into card components + shared TabStrip — QNT-253
    - **Triggered by**: `docs/frontend-improvement-v1.md` finding #13 — the last of the QNT-246–253 audit run, deliberately sequenced last so it didn't collide with the sibling tickets' edits. `chat-panel.tsx` had grown to 1,834 lines: 9 card renderers + the SSE consumer + the run tape + a pile of helpers in one file, with the QNT-247 `React.memo` boundary buried and the compact tab markup duplicated byte-for-byte across four tab groups. Pure structural refactor, zero behavior/visual/a11y change. (1) Extracted 16 presentational components + a `types.ts` (the `ChatRun`/`ToolRow`/`RunStatus` run model) into `components/chat/`: the 9 cards (Thesis, QuickFact, Comparison, LeanComparison, Conversational, FocusedAnalysis, Exploration, RetrievedSources, ComposingBubble) plus the shared sub-blocks (AspectBlock, ProseBlock, ToolCallRow, NarrativeBubble, PixelSpinner, SuggestionButton) and `RunBlock` itself — moving the memo boundary into its own `run-block.tsx` directly serves the ticket's "make the QNT-247 boundary obvious" goal and is what shrank the container from 1,834 → **650 lines** (−65%). `chat-panel.tsx` keeps only the container: SSE consumer, run tape, `Composer`, `EmptyState`. `ASPECT_LABEL_PILL` is exported from `aspect-block.tsx` and shared by the lean + focused cards; `chat-run.ts` (already-split pure helpers) and `lib/sse.ts` left untouched as instructed. (2) New generic `TabStrip<T extends string>` (`components/tab-strip.tsx`) replaces the duplicated `role="tablist"` pill markup in `technicals-card.tsx` + `fundamentals-card.tsx` (2 of 4 — the AC floor); `mobile-section-tabs` (full-width underline) and `price-chart` ChartToolbar (date pills) deliberately left alone since folding their different visuals in needs a variant prop = visual-change risk on a pure-refactor ticket. **No-visual-diff proven deterministically** rather than by sampling screenshots (no local backend; chat cards need live SSE): a substantive-line diff of the new file set against the original `chat-panel.tsx` on `main` (c80b68f) returned **0 missing lines** — every JSX/className/conditional/key is verbatim — and the `TabStrip` output is byte-identical to both inline blocks (role, aria-label, aria-selected, the short/long `<span>` pair, all class strings). code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP with one advisory actioned pre-merge: `tab-strip.tsx` carries `onClick` but lacked `"use client"`; added it to match the `mobile-section-tabs.tsx` convention (no-op today since it's only imported by client parents, guards a future Server-Component importer). AC1–AC4: `npm run lint` (eslint) clean, `npm run typecheck` (tsc) clean, `npm run test` (node --test) 38 passed, `npm run build` (next build) compiled OK with RSC client boundaries intact. Frontend-only diff — prod path is Vercel, not Hetzner. Out of scope: any logic/visual/a11y change (those were QNT-247/248/251), state-management re-architecture, the 2 untouched tab groups.
- [x] Mobile chat history lost when closing the chat panel — QNT-256
    - **Triggered by**: field-reported mobile bug (not part of the QNT-246–253 audit run) — on a phone, open chat from the hamburger, send messages, tap close (X) to return to the ticker view, reopen chat → the whole conversation was gone and a fresh session started. Desktop/tablet were unaffected. Root cause: chat history (`runs`) + the per-conversation `thread_id` are component-local state in `ChatPanel` (`chat-panel.tsx:353/373`), whose own docstring assumes the panel is mounted once and never torn down (ADR-014 anti-pattern #6). `app-shell.tsx` violated that on mobile by mounting `ChatPanel` at TWO sites: a persistent desktop/tablet rail (`hidden md:flex`, always mounted) AND a mobile overlay that was CONDITIONALLY mounted via `{mobilePanel === "chat" && <ChatPanel />}` — so `closeMobile()` set `mobilePanel = null`, React unmounted the overlay instance, and `runs`/`threadIdRef` were GC'd; reopening mounted a fresh empty one. Two live instances on a phone also meant divergent state + a duplicate `useHealthSources` fetch. Fix: collapse the two mount sites into ONE CSS-positioned node, mirroring the watchlist single-node pattern directly above it (`app-shell.tsx:154-172`) — on `<md` it's an absolute overlay gated `flex`/`hidden md:flex` (a CSS toggle, NOT a conditional mount); on `md+` it's the static grid rail (`md:static md:flex`, `xl:col-start-3`). The overlay moved from outside the grid (offset `top-10` to clear the 40px header) to inside the `relative` grid container, so it now uses `top-0` like the watchlist node — the grid area already starts below the header. One mounted instance ⇒ one `runs` + one `thread_id` ⇒ closing only hides it; the latent dual-instance divergence + duplicate `/health` fetch are eliminated as a side effect. Chose this over the heavier "lift state into a store/context" — the single-node CSS approach gives the same single source of truth with no new state plumbing. In-flight SSE on close: with no unmount the abort cleanup (`chat-panel.tsx:580-582`) no longer fires, so a mid-stream close keeps the stream running hidden and the answer is intact on reopen (the intended AC2 behaviour). **Every AC verified live in Playwright against the prod API** (`https://api.nusaverde.com`) at 390/900/1280px: AC1 — sent a real query, closed, reopened → the SAME article node persisted (identical ref = no remount) + a follow-up continued the same thread; AC2 — closed mid-stream, the request completed while hidden, both runs present on reopen, 0 console errors; AC4 — 1280 three-pane + 900 tablet-rail layouts unchanged. AC3/AC5: single mount confirmed in the diff; `npm run lint`/`typecheck` clean, `node --test` 38 passed. code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP, no blocking — two advisories (`flex-col` base class; whether `md:inset-auto` resets `top`/`bottom`) both non-issues: `md:static` makes inset values inert regardless, and the in-grid rendering was already proven live. Flagged for separate cleanup (not touched here): `mobile-chat-toggle.tsx` (`MobileNav`) carries the identical conditional-mount anti-pattern but is dead code — not imported anywhere since `app-shell.tsx` superseded it. Frontend-only diff — prod path is Vercel, not Hetzner.
- [x] Push deterministic eval scores onto prod Langfuse traces — QNT-182
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-09 — the local golden-set harness scores 22 records weekly with four scorers (`hallucination_ok`, `tool_call_ok`, `judge_score`, `cosine`), but real production chats produce Langfuse traces with latency / token metrics and **no quality signal**, so a prompt regression in prod is invisible until someone reruns the bench manually. Considered alternatives: Langfuse-managed LLM-as-a-Judge with Gemini Flash (deferred — at 5–10% sampling × ~200 obs/trace this would consume 45–90K Hobby units/month against the 50K cap; revisit if `hallucination_ok` rate trends down on real traffic), pushing `judge_score` from prod (re-introduces per-trace LLM cost), pushing `cosine` (no reference thesis exists outside goldens), goldens → Langfuse Datasets (~17K obs/month per weekly bench leaves no quota headroom). Picked the cheapest two scorers — both deterministic, zero LLM cost — and wired them into the existing `@observe(name="agent-chat")` parent trace via `langfuse.score_current_trace(...)`. New `agent.eval_scores` module with `compute_scores(state)` (pure: `(HallucinationResult, missing_planned_tools)`) + `push_to_current_trace(state)` (Langfuse-bound, safe no-op when keys are unset so eval bench runs that env-strip Langfuse stay untouched). Render dispatch matches the SSE handler's branch order (comparison > conversational > quick_fact > focused > thesis), NOT golden_set's order — the divergence is deliberate and documented: when intent picks thesis but synthesize falls back to a domain-redirect conversational, the user actually sees the conversational, so prod scoring scores that text. `plan_adherence` uses per-ticker (intersection) for comparison runs so partial gather (NVDA fetched fundamental, AAPL didn't) is flagged — the looser union model would silently pass. Failure comments: `hallucination_ok=0.0` carries the unsupported numeric tokens via `HallucinationResult.reason()`; `plan_adherence=0.0` carries `missing: <tool1>, <tool2>` so prod debugging doesn't require a log lookup. Score push wrapped in `try / except + logger.warning` matching the `_UsageCallback` pattern in `agent.llm` so observability outages cannot break the SSE response. Code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST with one BLOCKING (dispatch-order docstring claimed to mirror `golden_set` but was deliberately SSE-matched; rewrote docstring with rationale) and three ADVISORIES actioned pre-merge: per-ticker plan adherence for comparison runs, `comment` field on `plan_adherence` failures listing missing tools, dead `stub_graph` fixture parameter dropped from happy-path test. Quota math: 2 score calls × ~150 prod chats/day = ~9K Langfuse units/month, comfortably under 50K. Local bench unaffected — eval `__main__.py:29-30` env-strip remains and `agent.evals` does not import `eval_scores`; verified with `uv run python -m agent.evals --only NVDA` (5 records, history.csv row written, `judge_score=n/a` because LiteLLM wasn't running locally — the harness handled connection-refused gracefully and continued). Smoke verified post-deploy: prod chat trace `e6c1c7ec0ff57f83ca49a3afa438f7da` carried `hallucination_ok=1.00` and `plan_adherence=1.00` in the Langfuse UI within minutes of merge. Out of scope: Gemini-managed judge, judge_score on prod, cosine on prod, dataset experiments — re-evaluate per the deferral notes above.
    - **Post-merge follow-up** (same ticket, new commits — per "don't split trivial follow-ups on the same feature"): two filterability gaps surfaced once the score data started rendering in the Tracing list. (1) The Provided Model Name column showed `equity-agent/default` — the LiteLLM alias — instead of the upstream provider/model. LangChain only sees the alias because we pass `model=alias` to ChatOpenAI, and LiteLLM echoes the alias back in the response; the underlying `groq/llama-3.3-70b-versatile` was unreachable from the trace UI. (2) No way to filter the Tracing list by answer shape — "show me only conversational redirects" required parsing the SSE event stream. Two-part fix: (a) static `_RESOLVED_MODEL_BY_ALIAS` map in `agent.llm` kept in sync with `litellm_config.yaml` plus a `current_model_info()` helper; SSE handler stamps `metadata={"alias","resolved_model"}` via `propagate_attributes` so every observation in the trace carries it. Unmapped aliases resolve to `"unknown"` rather than raising — telemetry-stamping must never break a request, and the `unknown` value is itself a filterable drift surface in the Langfuse UI when someone adds a litellm_config entry but forgets the map. Doesn't catch fallback fires (when `equity-agent/default` falls back to `equity-agent/fallback-llama4scout` on Groq TPD exhaustion, the trace still shows the configured default not the actual upstream); detecting that needs LiteLLM response inspection and is filed as a separate follow-up. (b) `intent:<value>` trace tag added after `graph.invoke()` succeeds so the Tracing list is filterable by shape (thesis / quick_fact / comparison / focused / conversational). Implementation note: Langfuse v4 has no public `update_current_trace(tags=...)` (`propagate_attributes` is set-once at context entry, but intent isn't decided until classify_node has run inside the graph). Used `langfuse._create_trace_tags_via_ingestion(trace_id=..., tags=[...])` with the trace_id resolved from the active `@observe` context — private API, mild upgrade risk, but the failure mode (no intent tag) is benign and wrapped in try/except. 5 new tests: 2 unit on `current_model_info` (default-provider resolution + unknown-alias drift), 3 integration on the ingestion path (happy path, intent-missing skip, ingestion-failure swallowed). Second post-merge follow-up extended the tag list with `model:<resolved>` alongside `intent:<value>` so the Tracing list filters via the same "Tags any of" mechanism for both axes -- one tag chip per dimension. Provided Model Name column intentionally still shows the LiteLLM alias (it's the literal request payload; rewriting it via callback hacks would make the Langfuse trace lie about the actual HTTP call).
    - **Deferred follow-up — fallback-fired tag (optional, NOT ticketed; Linear free tier capped at issue limit, parked here as the audit trail)**: when LiteLLM's fallback chain fires (e.g. Groq TPD ceiling trips, traffic re-routes to `equity-agent/fallback-llama4scout`), the QNT-182 metadata + tags still show the *configured* default `groq/llama-3.3-70b-versatile`, not the *actual* served model. Per-trace fallback attribution is missing in Langfuse UI; LiteLLM container logs (`docker logs equity-data-agent-litellm-1 | grep -i fallback`) carry the truth but require SSH and aren't filterable. Indirect signals already cover detection: `hallucination_ok` rate dip on the Scores dashboard (Scout produces different-quality output), Groq console TPD utilization curves. **Not currently ticketed** because (a) zero observed fallback fires in trace data so far, (b) the indirect signals provide adequate detection of the *aggregate* phenomenon, and (c) shipping the tag means inherently soak-pending prod verification (real fallback fires happen on Groq TPD exhaustion, can't be triggered on demand). **Promote to a real ticket when**: (i) you start publicly demoing and want bulletproof "this trace ran on the model I claimed" provenance, OR (ii) `hallucination_ok` rate ever shows a sustained dip without a corresponding prompt change (likely Scout substitution), OR (iii) a user reports an answer that looks Scout-shaped and you need per-trace attribution to confirm. **Effort estimate**: 30 min if LangChain's `response.response_metadata.model_name` already exposes the resolved model that LiteLLM returns (10 min recon to verify, then wire into the existing tag push); 2.5 hr if not (custom `BaseCallbackHandler` capturing `on_llm_end` → `ContextVar` propagated through `asyncio.to_thread` like `TokenUsageTracker` → diff against alias post-graph, append `fallback-fired` + `actual_model:<X>` tags). Multi-call edge case: graph fires 3 LLM calls (classify, plan, synthesize); tag policy would be "fires if any call fell back; `actual_model:<X>` reports the synthesize call". Tests stay mock-only (forced-fallback in dev via `litellm_config.yaml` edit if needed); prod AC inherently soak-pending until first natural fire.
- [x] Enrich news report + add company knowledge tool — QNT-175
    - **Triggered by**: two adjacent gaps surfaced once the v1 agent went live: (1) the news report template still rendered the Phase-3 "sentiment scoring pending Phase 4" placeholder even though Phase 4 had populated `sentiment_label` + `body` on every `news_raw` row for months — the data was in ClickHouse, never plumbed into the agent-facing report; (2) `TICKER_METADATA` only carried `name`/`sector`/`industry`, leaving the synthesize step with no static context about what each company does, who it competes with, or which metrics matter — so qualitative thesis claims had to lean on LLM prior knowledge (the QNT-67 hallucination scorer's exact failure mode). Implementation bundled both: the news template now selects `sentiment_label` + `substring(body, 1, 120)` from `news_raw FINAL`, prints a body snippet + `Sentiment: <label>` line under each headline, and computes a real distribution (`N bullish / N neutral / N bearish across N scored of N headlines -- net bullish/bearish/balanced`) in plain Python; legacy Yahoo-RSS rows whose `sentiment_label='pending'` render as `Sentiment: N/A` and the SIGNAL line names the un-scored state explicitly so a single Finnhub article doesn't read as net-bullish off a feed of un-scored ones. The new `packages/api/src/api/templates/company.py` is a static report builder (no DB query — keeps the tool available when the warehouse is unreachable) backed by extended `TICKER_METADATA` carrying `description` / `key_competitors` / `key_risks` / `watch` for all 10 tickers; `GET /api/v1/reports/company/{ticker}` exposes it. The agent picks it up as a fourth tool: `default_report_tools()` registers `company`, `REPORT_TOOLS = (company, technical, fundamental, news)`, `_TOOL_LABELS` adds "Reviewing company" so the SSE chat panel renders the tool row, and `_parse_plan` enforces the plan-prompt bias as code (thesis + comparison force-include `company` even if the plan LLM omits it; quick_fact strips it — a single-metric ask doesn't benefit from a description / competitor list). The Pydantic source Literals in `agent.thesis` / `agent.quick_fact` / `agent.comparison` were extended to match `REPORT_TOOLS` so the system prompt's `(source: company)` citation actually validates at structured-output parse time — code-reviewer-ediff caught the schema/prompt drift pre-merge (Pydantic would have null-coerced or rejected company citations, silently dropping grounding evidence). 9 new tests pin the surfaces: news sentiment + body-snippet rendering, pending-as-N/A, company report shape + 10-ticker coverage (so a future TICKER_METADATA edit can't strand a ticker on `(none recorded)`), `_parse_plan` force-include / strip behavior across all three intents, and a schema-Literal vs REPORT_TOOLS guard so the next tool-add can't drift the structured-output boundary again.
    - **Post-merge follow-ups** (4 PRs over the same evening, all responding to issues surfaced by the first prod thesis runs against the new 4-tool plan — none big enough for their own ticket but each targeting a measurable thesis-quality regression):
        - **PR #240 — chat trace stitching + token-budget bump.** Two unrelated cleanups bundled: (a) `agent_chat._runner` was missing the `@observe(name="agent-chat")` wrapper that the CLI had on `agent.__main__.analyze`, so each graph node's `@observe` decorator opened its own root trace in Langfuse. The chat path's classify / plan / gather / synthesize spans appeared as four separate top-level traces, while the CLI ran under one parent. One-line wrapper restored topology parity. (b) `CHAT_TOKENS_PER_IP_PER_DAY` 10K → 30K and `CHAT_TOKENS_GLOBAL_PER_DAY` 50K → 200K. Old global cap was 50% of just the primary's 100K TPD, sized before the LiteLLM auto-fallback to Llama-4-Scout (500K TPD) existed; effective ceiling is 600K TPD combined and 50K left ~550K of permanent unused headroom. New per-IP cap supports ~7-10 thesis runs/visitor; new global cap is ~33% of combined ceiling, reserves ~150K for daily ingest + own eval sweeps. Also bumped `mako` 1.3.10 → 1.3.12 in the same commit because pip-audit started failing CI on every branch (CVE-2026-44307; transitive dep, unrelated to QNT-175).
        - **PR #241 — thesis fetches every tool deterministically.** Prod sweep showed plan-LLM noise: same prompt, "Give me a thesis on NVDA" → all 4 tools, "Give me a thesis on AAPL" on the next request → only [company, fundamental, news] (technical dropped). The plan-prompt bias text already said "include every report that is even marginally relevant" but the LLM was narrowing under its own steam. Fix: skip the plan-LLM call entirely for `thesis` + `comparison` — `plan = list(available)` is deterministic. Quick_fact KEEPS the plan-LLM call because narrowing to the single relevant report is the whole point of that path. Drops ~250 tokens per thesis run (no plan call) and removes a real source of variance the QNT-175 force-include for `company` only half-fixed. 5-ticker post-deploy sweep confirmed 4/4 tools fired on every run.
        - **PR #242 — bullets cite underlying metrics, not the SIGNAL line + decimal-preservation.** Two prompt-layer tightenings driven by direct screenshot review of the first NVDA thesis: (a) bull/bear bullets were citing each report's `## SIGNAL` aggregate verdict ("the technical report indicates a BULLISH signal with 2/3 indicators agreeing") instead of the underlying metrics that drove the verdict (RSI 60.8, MACD posture, P/E vs threshold, revenue YoY %). The SIGNAL line is meta-summary the stance field already conveys; bullets exist to show their work. New rule + counter-example added to both bull and bear sections of `SYSTEM_PROMPT`, naming SIGNAL-line bullets as "non-bullets". (b) The first NVDA thesis rendered `SMA-50 (187.72)` from the technical report as `SMA-50 level of 18772` in the verdict action — a $187.72 support level became a fictitious $18,772 target by stripping the decimal. Added byte-for-byte format-preservation rule to the `verdict_action` description, careful to stay digit-free in the prompt body (the QNT-136 regression guard `test_system_prompt_contains_no_multi_digit_literals` would have failed on a `187.72` example). Same NVDA prompt post-fix produced underlying-metric bullets (`Revenue +73.21% YoY (source: fundamental)`, `P/E of 42.06, indicating a rich valuation (source: fundamental)`) and `SMA-50 (187.72)` correctly preserved.
        - **PR #243 — encourage news citation when headlines bear on the question.** Post-#242 prod sweep: only 2 of 5 thesis runs cited news (NVDA, TSLA); AAPL / META / JPM omitted news entirely despite each having 10 fresh on-topic headlines. Root cause: the model was cherry-picking fundamental's numerical metrics (easy to cite verbatim) and treating news as decoration. Without an explicit rule, "no number to cite verbatim" became "skip the source". Fix: a dedicated paragraph in the bull/bear sections naming news's role (catalyst evidence: partnerships, analyst notes, regulatory actions, product launches, demand signals, recalls, guidance, lawsuits) and saying the thesis "should cite at least one in either bull or bear" when news has on-topic content. The only valid opt-out is "no news headline materially bears on the question", not "fundamental has more numbers to cite". Kept rule 1 (no padding) precedence so off-topic news can still be skipped. Same 5-ticker post-deploy sweep: 5/5 cited news, AAPL/META/JPM all surfaced real catalysts (MP-Materials/Pentagon deal, multibillion-dollar tax benefit, Ripple/Mastercard tokenized Treasury settlement); TSLA correctly split news across bull (Optimus production) and bear (camera recall) — exactly the bull-or-bear allowance the rule was written for.
    - **Pattern lesson**: this five-PR fan-out matches `feedback_backend_pack_consumer_loop` — adding a backend surface (4th tool + new endpoint) needs the first downstream consumer to actually exercise it before the rough edges show up. Three of the four follow-ups (#241 plan-LLM noise, #242 bullets-cite-SIGNAL, #243 no-news-citation) were prompt-layer regressions only visible once a real thesis ran against the new 4-tool plan; none were detectable from unit tests. PR #240 was infra noise (trace topology + token-budget sizing) that surfaced from the post-deploy verification, not the thesis content. Next time a tool is added to the plan, plan to ship the consumer fixes in the same cycle.

- [x] Focused-analysis intents + composer cleanup — QNT-176
    - **Triggered by**: two adjacent gaps in the chat shape after the v1 4-tool plan landed. (1) The classifier had four intents (`thesis` / `quick_fact` / `comparison` / `conversational`) but no clean path for "give me a technical analysis of NVDA" or "what's the news sentiment on META?" — those questions either defaulted to `thesis` (over-fetched every report and produced a four-section card the user did not ask for) or got clipped to `quick_fact` (one cited value, too short for a real read). (2) The composer in `chat-panel.tsx` exposed `tools` and `cite` toggle buttons that had become footguns: `tools_enabled` was wired but every useful chat answer needs tools, and `cite_sources` had been a no-op on the backend since QNT-149. Hiding the synthesis contract (ADR-003: every numeric claim cites a source) behind a toggle taught the wrong mental model. Both gaps were small individually but both touched the same composer + intent surface, so bundled.
    - **Implementation**: Three new intents (`fundamental` / `technical` / `news_sentiment`) added to `agent.intent.Intent`. Plan node narrows DETERMINISTICALLY to `[company, <matching_report>]` — no plan-LLM call (the user named the domain explicitly; nothing to disambiguate). Heuristic triggers explicit phrases ("fundamental analysis", "technicals", "TA on", "chart setup", "news sentiment", "what is/'s the sentiment", "news read") with a mutual-exclusivity guard: if the user names multiple focuses in one breath ("triangulate technicals AND fundamentals"), the focused branch defers to thesis. New shared Pydantic class `FocusedAnalysis` with `summary` / `key_points` / `cited_values` and a `focus` discriminator — one class covers all three shapes, synthesize node re-asserts the focus value defensively against an LLM that emits the wrong literal. New SSE event `focused`; new `FocusedAnalysisCard` React component with a coloured pill per focus (sky / emerald / amber). Composer cleanup dropped `tools_enabled` / `cite_sources` from `ChatRequest`, the React composer JSX, and the SSE request body; backend unconditionally calls `default_report_tools()`. Schema-pin test (`test_chat_request_rejects_legacy_toggle_fields`) blocks silent re-introduction.
    - **Eval coverage**: three new golden records (`jpm-fundamental-deepdive`, `v-technical-analysis`, `unh-news-sentiment`) bring the suite to 22 records; new `test_every_intent_has_at_least_one_golden` regression guard iterates `get_args(Intent)` so a future intent addition lands with a golden alongside it (or fails the test loudly). Backfilled `expected_intent: quick_fact` on the previously unpinned `nvda-quickfact-rsi` record. `_prompt_version` now hashes `FOCUSED_SYSTEM_PROMPT` so prompt edits to the focused path are visible in `history.csv` as a different version.
    - **In-flight scope cut**: section C (markdown rendering via `react-markdown` + `remark-gfm`) was rolled back during sanity-check. The LLM does not currently emit markdown markers in its prose — structured Pydantic fields (`bull_case`, `key_points`, etc.) already carry list-shaped content, and the system prompts do not ask for `**bold**` / `inline code` / `- bullet` emphasis. Adding a renderer for markup that never appears violated CLAUDE.md ("don't add features beyond what the task requires"). Both deps were uninstalled and `ProseBlock` reverted to plain spans. If a future prompt-tuning ticket adds markdown emphasis to the synthesis prompts, re-add the renderer alongside that change.
    - **Review finding**: `code-reviewer-ediff` flagged the `"sentiment on"` and `"headlines on"` heuristic tokens as over-broad — phrases like "market sentiment on the sector" or "headlines on the bond market" would fire `news_sentiment` with no ticker present. Tightened to drop both; remaining tokens all carry "news" or "sentiment" in unambiguous focused-ask context. Regression test added.

- [x] Chat empty-state suggested questions + header cleanup — QNT-178
    - **Triggered by**: post-QNT-176 visual review of the empty chat panel — the page burnt vertical space on a single placeholder line ("Ask a question to start a research session. Active ticker: TSLA.") with zero discoverability for the answer shapes the agent supports. The QNT-176 focused-analysis intents (fundamental / technical / news_sentiment) shipped invisible; a visitor had to know to type "technical analysis of NVDA" to find them. Two adjacent footguns alongside it: the active ticker was repeated three times (header pill + empty-state body + composer @ticker chip), and the header carried decorative `LangGraph` / `Cited` pills that read as internal jargon for a portfolio site without telling the user anything actionable.
    - **Implementation**: new `EmptyState` component renders 4 ticker-parametrised suggestion buttons (one per main intent shape: thesis + the three QNT-176 focused intents). Click prefills the composer textarea + focuses, doesn't auto-send — gives the user a chance to edit before pressing Send (distinct from `ConversationalCard` suggestions which auto-send mid-conversation; same visual via a shared `SuggestionButton` component, different parent click contracts). Composer was lifted to a controlled component (`value` / `onChange` / `focusKey` props) so external clicks can prefill. `focusKey: number` is bumped by the parent and watched via `useEffect` to call `textareaRef.current.focus()`; skips the `focusKey === 0` initial render so opening the page doesn't steal focus from the rest of the layout. Header pills (`LangGraph`, `Cited`) dropped — the subheader trust line ("demo: ~30 queries/hour per visitor · powered by Groq free tier") is the canonical advertisement and was already there. Redundant "Active ticker: TSLA" body line removed; the @ticker chip in the composer carries it.
    - **Review finding**: `code-reviewer-ediff` flagged a cross-ticker leak — clicking "Technical analysis of TSLA", then navigating to /ticker/AAPL without sending, would leave "TSLA" in the composer with @AAPL chip; one accidental Send away from running a TSLA question against the AAPL run path. Pre-lift, `Composer` owned its own state but the same scenario existed (the panel stays mounted across route changes); the prefill button just makes hitting it much easier. Fixed via React's "adjust state during render" pattern (https://react.dev/learn/you-might-not-need-an-effect#adjusting-some-state-when-a-prop-changes): track `prevTicker` in state, conditionally `setComposerInput("")` during render when it shifts. Avoided the setState-in-useEffect anti-pattern (ESLint flagged on the first attempt) and avoided lifting the input even further into a `key={ticker}` wrapper.

- [x] Regime-polarity rule for Bull/Bear bullets + comparison-shape mirror — QNT-183
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (samples 2 UNH, 4 NVDA vs AAPL) — model treated regime-labeled metrics as ordered scalars, surfacing overbought RSI as a bull bullet because the technical SIGNAL aggregate printed BULLISH, and reading "AAPL higher RSI" as "stronger momentum" despite RSI 75.9 being overbought. Root cause: SYSTEM_PROMPT told the model to cite underlying metrics but never stated that a metric's polarity depends on its regime bucket. Fix: regime-polarity rule added to Bull/Bear sections of SYSTEM_PROMPT ("Regime labels override raw ordering … an overbought RSI reading is never a bull bullet even if the technical SIGNAL aggregate prints BULLISH"); regime mirror added to COMPARISON_SYSTEM_PROMPT differences paragraph ("Regime labels in either section trump raw ordering … A higher RSI is not 'stronger momentum' once it is past 70"). Two golden records (tsla-overbought-rsi-regime, nvda-msft-rsi-regime-contrast) and two test_prompts.py assertions pin the new rules. make eval target added to Makefile.

- [x] Strengthen anti-SIGNAL rule in FOCUSED with paired counter-example — QNT-184
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (sample 5b TSLA focused-technical) — FOCUSED_SYSTEM_PROMPT had a one-line anti-SIGNAL rule buried in the key_points description with no counter-example; model wrote "The overall signal is bullish, with 3/3 indicators agreeing (source: technical)" in violation. Thesis prompt had the same rule with a paired BAD/OK example and did not commit this violation. Fix: promoted the rule to a standalone block with BAD/OK examples in FOCUSED_SYSTEM_PROMPT; added defensive rule 6 to QUICK_FACT_SYSTEM_PROMPT; added forbidden_substrings mechanism to the eval harness so regression tests can assert the model doesn't produce the "indicators agree" phrase; new golden record tsla-focused-technical-no-signal-quote pins the rule as a hard gate.

- [x] Prior-session momentum-delta rule for Bull/Bear and focused-summary bullets — QNT-185
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (sample 1 NVDA thesis) — model cited only the current RSI bucket ("RSI-14 is neutral at 64.7, indicating a potential for further growth") without reading the prior-session delta (76.7 → 64.7, down 12.1). An equity analyst would say "RSI cooling from overbought" — mean-reversion in progress. Root cause: SYSTEM_PROMPT never instructed the model to use the prior-session delta the report already prints. Fix: momentum-delta rule added to Bull/Bear section of SYSTEM_PROMPT and mirrored in FOCUSED_SYSTEM_PROMPT; Bear Case addendum references the rule. New golden record nvda-rsi-momentum-delta pins forbidden_substrings: ["potential for further growth"]; record count band bumped to 15-30; test_prompts.py test pins the rule on both prompts.

- [x] Heuristic-token expansion for intent classifier (natural-language focused triggers) — QNT-186
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (sample 5 TSLA) — "Walk me through TSLA technical setup" routed to `thesis` because the heuristic only fired on "technical analysis", "technicals", "ta on", "chart setup" — none match that phrasing. Fix (AI Engineering roadmap B-5): added natural-language phrasings to all three focused token lists (`"technical setup"`, `"overbought"`, `"oversold"`, `"what do the charts say"` for technical; `"valuation read"`, `"what does the balance sheet say"`, `"expensive"`, `"fundamental picture"` for fundamental; `"what's the news say"`, `"how is sentiment"`, `"any catalysts"` for news_sentiment) and updated `_CLASSIFY_PROMPT` examples to keep the LLM fallback consistent. Pairs with QNT-189 (classifier_source trace tag) for measurement.
- [x] Verdict-action direction post-check (first deterministic tripwire) — QNT-193
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (sample 1 NVDA) — verdict cited "potential target of SMA-20 at 210.30" when close was already 225.32. Hallucination scorer passed (numbers real); semantic relation to close was wrong. Introduces `post_checks.py` with `check_verdict_direction()` — extracts price levels from `verdict_action`, splits on clause boundaries, checks directional framing (target/resistance vs support/defend) against the technical report's close. Pushes `verdict_direction_ok` Langfuse score via `eval_scores.push_to_trace_id()` for every thesis trace; Discord alert on >= 3 mismatches/hour. ADR-012 pattern: deterministic post-graph assertion, not a prompt rule. First instance of the post-check category (B-4 in AI Engineering roadmap); QNT-194 extends same module.
- [x] Verdict-action trigger-shape rule + post-check extension — QNT-194
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-18 analyst-quality assessment (samples 1 NVDA, 2 UNH, 5 TSLA) — every `verdict_action` described the present state ("Close above SMA-50") instead of specifying a future trigger. Extends `post_checks.py` (from QNT-193) with `check_verdict_shape()` — asserts at least one conditional verb (trim, add, hold, exit, defend, watch, reduce, accumulate, stop) or explicit escape hatch appears in `verdict_action`. Pushes `verdict_shape_ok` Langfuse score via `eval_scores.push_to_trace_id()` for every thesis trace. - [x] RSI momentum polarity misclassification fix — QNT-198
    - **Triggered by**: 2026-05-19 NVDA prod thesis — RSI-14 at 61.7 "trending down from 64.7" appeared in the bull case despite being a bearish momentum signal (declining RSI at any level → bear). QNT-183's regime-polarity rule covered overbought RSI only; QNT-185's prior-session-delta rule characterised direction but did not enforce case placement. Adds two prompt rules: (1) declining momentum delta belongs in bear only, (2) no indicator may appear in both bull and bear. Pins both with a golden record (`nvda-rsi-neutral-trending-down`, `forbidden_bull_substrings: ["trending down"]`) and two new test functions in `test_prompts.py`.
- [x] Structured-output retry on synthesize nodes (measure-first, then with_retry) — QNT-196
    - **Triggered by**: AI Engineering roadmap reliability gap — Phase-1 Langfuse measurement (30-day sample, 24,093 traces) found 2.7% overall fallback rate and 5.5% on the thesis branch specifically, dominated by Gemini returning malformed tool-call JSON that raises `OutputParserException` or `ValidationError`. All 5 synthesize branches now chain `.with_structured_output(Schema).with_retry(stop_after_attempt=2, retry_if_exception_type=(ValidationError, OutputParserException))`; WARNING logs include `type(exc).__name__` + branch name for Langfuse-parseable diagnostics.
