The brand-emerald vs gain-emerald overlap was reviewed and **deliberately KEPT** (green == "up" is a terminal convention a green brand reinforces; decision recorded in-code), diverging from the AC's literal "separate the hue" wording — substance over letter. **Verification**: changes are static frontend, so the Hetzner SHA / Dagster-graph ship gates are N/A; verified by building + serving against the **prod API** (`NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL=https://api.nusaverde.com`, all 10 tickers prerendered) and screenshotting the real states at 1440px (AC1) and on a live NVDA thesis (AC2). **code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP**; of its two advisories, the `md:p-10 md:pt-20` shorthand/longhand concern was dismissed (Tailwind v4 orders the `pt-*` longhand after the `p-*` shorthand deterministically, and the 1440px screenshot confirmed correct top padding), and the 9px-chip WCAG-AA contrast flag was actioned per a user decision — held the chip at `zinc-400`/`10px` (borderless is what de-noises it; ~5.9:1 clears AA) rather than the dimmer/smaller tier that fell to ~3.8:1. AC1/AC2/AC3 dev-execution-verified live. Out of scope: the flat single-surface elevation system (logged as a follow-up candidate), any change to the ticker detail pages (already strong).

- [x] De-duplicate consecutive source citations across all intents (keep the chip, drop the repeats) — QNT-287
    - **Triggered by**: a live read of the QNT-286 result — borderless chips were quieter but the residual distraction was REPETITION: within one answer the same source tags nearly every clause (a News aspect block, already titled "News", tagged 3 lines `NEWS`; the synthesis bubble tagged `FUNDAMENTAL` 3x). The eye tracks repetition, so chip styling had hit a ceiling. **Decision (with the user): keep the chip mechanism (not footnotes), surface a citation only when it adds information.** **The fix**: collapse CONSECUTIVE same-source citations to the first occurrence at the SHARED parse layer, so it covers every intent automatically. `parseInlineChips` (every non-rich card) and `parseProse` (the narrate bubble) gained a `DedupeState` carrier + `pushChip` that emits a chip only when its normalised source differs from the last EMITTED one — a same-source RUN collapses to one chip regardless of distance, a TRANSITION (news → fundamental → news) shows all three. The synthesis bubble de-dups across its own paragraphs via an internal carrier; the thesis **aspect blocks needed a SHARED carrier** (`AspectBlock` owns one, threaded through its summary + each support/challenge `ProseBlock`, which render in order) because each bullet is a separate `ProseBlock` — per-text de-dup alone wouldn't collapse the cross-bullet repetition the user pointed at. Also trims one trailing space when a duplicate drops (`oversight (source: news).` → `oversight.`, not `oversight .`). Pure parser logic, deterministic, no model/prompt change. **code-reviewer-ediff returned SHIP**; it scrutinised the render-time carrier mutation (carrier created per `AspectBlock` render, mutated by children rendering in source order) and confirmed it safe — StrictMode double-invoke recreates a fresh carrier each pass, concurrent restart re-runs the body, `ProseBlock` is not memoised; took one advisory (a test for the back-to-back-chips no-intervening-text edge). AC1–AC4 code (pinned by 7 `prose-parse.test.ts` cases: consecutive-collapse, transition-preserved, case/space-insensitive, orphan-space-trim, back-to-back, cross-paragraph, shared-carrier). **AC5 (live render screenshot) deferred** — the prod demo rate-limit (Groq free-tier daily cap) was exhausted, so the live visual confirm is a post-deploy check once the cap resets; user authorized shipping on the deterministic unit tests. Out of scope: footnote/superscript markers (rejected — keep the chip), chip styling (QNT-286), any change to how the agent emits `(source: …)`.

- [x] Restore a subtle boxed pill for inline citations (borderless reads as noise) — QNT-295
    - **Triggered by**: a live read of the QNT-287 result — with the repetition gone, the user preferred the **subtle boxed pill** look of the classification badges (`INLINE` / `DOWNTREND` / `NEUTRAL`) over QNT-286's borderless dim text, which read as *unstyled noise* rather than a designed element. The key insight: the original problem with boxed pills was REPETITION (a box on every clause = ransom-note), and QNT-287 already fixed that by collapsing consecutive same-source citations to one chip — so the box is viable again and now looks intentional. **The fix (one line + comment)**: `prose-block.tsx renderSegment` chip case goes from borderless back to a subtle boxed pill — `rounded border border-zinc-700/60 bg-zinc-900/50 px-1 py-px` — kept deliberately MUTED (dimmer border + faint fill) vs the tone-coloured classification badges so a source citation reads as secondary to a classification label; tone held at `zinc-400`/`10px` for WCAG AA. No parser/de-dup change (QNT-287 stands); one chip per source-run, transitions still shown. Verified live (thesis on prod-API build, 1440px): News aspect → one `NEWS` box, synthesis → `FUNDAMENTAL → TECHNICAL → NEWS` as three subtle boxes (transitions), no repeats. Out of scope: the de-dup logic (QNT-287), how the agent emits `(source: …)`.

- [x] Contextual RAG query rewriting: self-contained retrieval query from the classify call — QNT-289
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-2) — both RAG fire points (`gather` node) passed the RAW user question as the retrieval query. On a warm thread a targeted follow-up is often elliptical ("what about the buyback?" after an NVDA thesis turn): the classify LLM correctly sets `needs_news_search`/`needs_earnings_search` from history (QNT-216/QNT-280), but the string that reaches Qdrant is the bare ellipsis — no ticker, no topic noun — so hybrid + BM25 RRF + Cohere rerank (QNT-262) can't rescue it. Same invisible-failure class as QNT-280: no error, just a quietly worse answer while a directly relevant hit sits in the corpus. **The fix**: a `search_query` field added to the EXISTING classify structured-output call (`IntentDecision`, `intent.py`) — zero extra LLM round-trips, the classify call already runs on every turn and already reads history. Threaded `classify_intent_with_source` (now a 5-tuple; ~18 test call sites rippled, mirroring the QNT-280 tuple-arity precedent) → `classify_node` → `AgentState.search_query` → `gather`, which resolves `state.get("search_query") or question` at both fire points — an empty/rejected rewrite falls back to the raw question (today's behaviour), so the change can only ADD recall, never regress it. **Guardrails** (`sanitize_search_query`): length cap mirroring `agent.tools._QUERY_MAX_LEN`, and a hallucinated-entity guard — a ticker-shaped token (2-5 uppercase letters, common finance acronyms excluded) not in `shared.tickers.TICKERS` rejects the whole rewrite rather than searching on a ticker outside coverage. **AC2/AC3 measured live** on a new 20-fixture labeled warm-thread golden set (`goldens/search_query.yaml`, 8 elliptical / 6 cold_targeted / 6 generic) + harness (`search_query_eval.py`): flag layer 20/20 (100%), query layer elliptical 6-7/8 (75-88%, small-model variance run-to-run) / cold_targeted 6/6 / generic 6/6; no intent drift vs the QNT-280 trigger set re-verified live (`routing_eval` 26/26, `news_search_eval` flag 20/20, both 100%). Live retrieval comparison: rewritten-query hit-rate 92% (12/13) vs raw-question 77% (10/13), 0 regressions, 2 elliptical cases moved miss→hit (NVDA buyback, AAPL lawsuit). **AC4 live transcript**: a two-turn AAPL thread (thesis, then "is there any update on the lawsuit?" naming no ticker) — server log confirms the rewrite `AAPL lawsuit` reached the search tool verbatim, surfacing "Apple (AAPL) Faces £3 Billion UK iCloud Lawsuit As Class Action Moves Ahead" as the top retrieved source. **code-reviewer-ediff returned FIX FIRST on two items, both fixed pre-merge**: (1) the free-text classify prompt's long-standing history disclaimer ("do not use it to... infer a ticker that the user changed") directly contradicted the new field's "resolve the ticker from history" instruction in the SAME LLM call — added an explicit carve-out plus a dedicated `search_query` prompt paragraph, pinned by a new regression test, re-verified live with no drift; (2) the eval's `is_failing` gate only checked false-positives/regressions, leaving the load-bearing elliptical query-accuracy an eyeball-only metric — added `ELLIPTICAL_QUERY_ACCURACY_FLOOR` (mirrors `routing_eval.ACCURACY_FLOOR`), pinned by 3 offline unit tests on synthetic outcomes. Also dropped dead acronym-guard entries (`Q1`-`Q4`, `B2B`, `B2C`) that could never match the letters-only guard regex. AC1 code (pinned by 9 `test_intent.py` + 2 `test_graph.py` unit tests); AC2/AC3 code + dev-execution-verified live; AC4 dev-execution-verified live (LiteLLM + tunnel + API + Qdrant Cloud, no prod deploy needed — pure agent-runtime change). Out of scope (per ticket): widening WHICH intents can fire retrieval (QNT-290, blocked by this ticket), retrieval-layer changes (hybrid/rerank/floor unchanged), multi-query decomposition/HyDE-style expansion.

- [x] Let followup turns fire RAG retrieval: close the warm-thread recall gap — QNT-290
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-3), unblocked by QNT-289 the same day. The followup path reused the prior turn's checkpointer-hydrated reports verbatim and never visited `plan`/`gather` — `_classify_router` short-circuited every followup straight from `classify` to `synthesize` (a QNT-215 latency optimization). Correct for "explain that verdict again," but wrong when a followup pivots to a NEW targeted event ("and what did the CEO say about it?"): the classifier's `needs_news_search`/`needs_earnings_search` flags fired (intent-independent by design, QNT-222/280) but the signal was thrown away — no error, no empty panel, just a quietly worse answer, same invisible-failure class QNT-280 fixed for cold turns. **The fix**: `_classify_router` now special-cases `intent == "followup"` before the short-circuit set, routing to `plan`→`gather` when a new `_followup_fires_news_search`/`_followup_fires_earnings_search` predicate pair says yes (mirrors `_NEWS_SEARCH_INTENTS`/`_EARNINGS_SEARCH_INTENTS`, now including `"followup"`, plus a tool-wired check so CLI/eval runs without a search tool keep the cheap path). `plan_node` still returns an empty plan for followup (the out-of-scope report re-fetch never happens); `gather_node`'s followup branch fires `search_news`/`search_earnings` with the QNT-289 rewritten query and folds hits onto the hydrated `reports` copy via new shared helpers `_fold_news_hits`/`_fold_earnings_hits` (also used by the refactored cold-turn path, no behavior change there). `narrate_node` gained a block that feeds the freshly-folded report into the narrator's substrate on a flagged followup (gated on this turn's `retrieved_sources` corpus tags, not just report presence, so a zero-hit search doesn't pad the prompt). **AC2 dedupe**: new `_strip_retrieved_block(text, heading)` replaces (not stacks) any prior fold before re-folding onto the same hydrated dict, so a chained followup can't grow the persisted report unbounded. **Found and fixed pre-merge (by me and independently by the `code-reviewer-ediff` subagent)**: `_strip_retrieved_block`'s boundary heuristic assumed a retrieved block never contains an internal blank line, but `_truncate_body` only `.strip()`'d body/chunk text — an 8-K chunk with an embedded blank line would fool the boundary on the *next* chained fold, silently leaking a stray fragment into the persisted "base" (reproduced live: `Management guided Q2 revenue...\n\nThe company also announced a new buyback...` truncated wrong). Fixed by collapsing internal whitespace in `_truncate_body`; pinned by `test_strip_retrieved_block_survives_embedded_blank_line_in_hit_body`. Also fixed: `_followup_fires_search`'s docstring claimed it was shared with `gather_node`, but `gather_node` re-derived the same three-part condition inline (drift risk) — split into `_followup_fires_news_search`/`_followup_fires_earnings_search`, called directly by both sites. Also fixed (found via the live AC4 transcript): a flagged narrative-only followup showed `citations_count: 0` in the SSE `done` event despite `retrieved_sources` rendering and the narrative citing them — same gap QNT-281 fixed for the sibling focused-card-dropped case, now extended to followup. AC1 (flagged followup fires search + folds; unflagged gathers nothing, existing tests unchanged) code, pinned by `test_followup_with_needs_news_search_fires_search_and_folds_hits` + `test_followup_without_search_flags_gathers_nothing`; AC2 (chained-followup dedupe) code, pinned by `test_chained_flagged_followups_do_not_duplicate_retrieved_block`; AC3 (retrieved_sources + corpus tags on a flagged followup) code, pinned by `test_retrieved_sources_event_emitted_on_flagged_followup`; AC4 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API, no prod deploy needed — pure agent-runtime change): a 3-turn META thread — thesis (4 tool calls), flagged followup ("...Meta getting into the cloud business?": 1 `news_search` call with the QNT-289 rewritten query `"META cloud business"`, 5 hits, `retrieved_sources` all `corpus: "news"`, narrative citing `(source: news)`), pure followup ("why that verdict?": zero tool calls, no `retrieved_sources` event). Out of scope (per ticket, respected): query rewriting itself (QNT-289), re-gathering the full report plan on followup, any change to cold-turn retrieval gating.

- [x] Declarative per-intent routing policy table — consolidate scattered intent frozensets — QNT-288
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-1). `graph.py`'s 9 intents had their behaviour scattered across six-plus parallel frozensets/dicts (`_FOCUSED_REPORT`, `_NEWS_SEARCH_INTENTS`, `_EARNINGS_SEARCH_INTENTS`, `_TICKER_REQUIRING_INTENTS`, `_SHORT_CIRCUIT_INTENTS`, `_COMPACT_COMPANY_INTENTS`, `_DEEP_HISTORY_INTENTS`) that had to be kept mutually consistent by hand — QNT-263 caught the exact failure mode when `quick_fact` was missing from the earnings-search set. **The fix**: a single `IntentPolicy` dataclass (`focused_report`, `rag_corpora`, `history_budget`, `company_variant`, `requires_ticker`, `short_circuit`, `suggestion_hint`) held in one `INTENT_POLICIES: dict[Intent, IntentPolicy]` table; the legacy frozensets/dicts are now dict/set comprehensions DERIVED from the table rather than hand-maintained, so callers (`plan_node`, `gather_node`, `_classify_router`, `_hint_from_intent`, `_history_budget`) see identical values with one place left to edit. Pure refactor, zero behaviour change — every derived view hand-verified to compute to the exact same membership as the literal it replaced. One wrinkle: `_history_budget` had a live test pinning deep-history behaviour for the string `"clarify"`, which is not an `Intent` literal member (a routing-node name, never a live `AgentState['intent']` value) — preserved via a small `_DEEP_HISTORY_EXTRA` set kept outside the table rather than folded into a fake Intent entry. AC1/AC2 code (pinned by `test_every_intent_literal_has_a_fully_populated_policy`, strengthened post-review to also validate every `suggestion_hint` against `agent.conversational._SUGGESTION_BANK`); AC3 code (full repo test suite green — 1365 passed / 53 deselected / 1 xfailed — zero fixture edits; `routing_eval` untouched by construction, it only imports `agent.intent`). `code-reviewer-ediff` returned SHIP (no blocking; one advisory — `_hint_from_intent`'s direct dict indexing raises `KeyError` instead of the old chain's implicit `None` fallback on an out-of-domain string — left as-is since it's unreachable given the `Intent` type contract and adding a `.get()` fallback would be defensive code for an impossible scenario). Out of scope (per ticket): any behaviour change to routing (QNT-289/290), the exploration keyword trigger lists, moving nodes out of `graph.py` (QNT-294).

- [x] graph.py code health — node module split + discriminated-union answer payload — QNT-294
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-7; second-pass `_structured_call` dedup and output-structure C-6 folded in). `graph.py` had grown to 3,341 lines with every node (classify/plan/gather/synthesize/narrate/clarify/exploration) a closure inside `build_graph`, so most agent tickets paid a rising navigation + test-targeting tax; `AgentState` carried eight optional answer slots (`thesis`/`quick_fact`/`comparison`/`comparison_lean`/`conversational`/`focused`/`exploration`) with an "exactly one populated" contract enforced only by convention (every consumer re-implemented the branch ladder); the structured-output ladder (`with_structured_output` + `with_retry` + BLE001 + `_coerce_*` + fallback) was duplicated across the seven `_synthesize_payload` branches plus `clarify_node`; and `Thesis.to_markdown`/`ComparisonAnswer.to_markdown` duplicated the aspect loop and disagreed on the challenges glyph (`· ` vs `- `). Sequenced AFTER QNT-288/289/290 landed to avoid a big-bang-move-into-in-flight-behaviour rebase. **The fix**: (AC1) nodes became module-level functions in `agent/nodes/{classify,plan,gather,synthesize,narrate,clarify}.py` taking `(state, config, deps)` — unit-testable without compiling a graph — with build-time wiring threaded via a frozen `GraphDeps` (`tools`/`event_emitter`/`compact_company_tool`/`comparison_metrics_tool`/`active_retrievals` + `effective_tools`/`run_retrievals`/`followup_fires_search`); pure helpers moved to `agent/policy.py` (the QNT-288 `INTENT_POLICIES` table + derived views + types), `agent/structured.py` (the `_linked_invoke`/`_coerce` primitives + plan-prompt builders + `_PROMPT_VERSION`), and `agent/support.py` (planning/parsing, confidence, tool gather, `RetrievalSpec` + search formatting/folds, ambiguity detection, ticker/history resolution, transcript surfacing). `graph.py` dropped 3,341 → 678 lines, keeping `AgentState`, `_structured_call`, the runtime-grounding cluster, and `build_graph`'s wiring (topology **byte-identical** to `main` — same 7 nodes, same conditional-edge targets). (AC2) a single discriminated-union `answer` field replaces the eight optionals: `agent/answer.py::project_answer` is the SOLE multi-slot writer (sets `answer` + derives exactly one legacy slot from the payload's concrete type, clears the rest), so double-population is impossible by type; `_assistant_surface`, synthesize's early card emit, `narrate_node`, and the SSE wrapper read the union. (AC5) one `_structured_call(schema, prompt, config, prompt_name, *, llm=None, linked=True)` owns the ladder with the retry policy defined exactly once; the generic `_coerce[T]` replaced the seven `_coerce_*` helpers; `with_structured_output` greps to one pipeline call site. (AC6) a shared `render_aspect_block` used by both `to_markdown`s; challenges glyph normalized `· ` → `- `. **Two coupling constraints drove the design** (surfaced during the split, not guessed): (1) *checkpointer* — the followup path structurally reads the prior turn's `thesis` from a separately-hydrated channel WHILE writing this turn's answer, and old SqliteSaver threads persist the 8-key shape, so the eight legacy answer slots were kept as deprecated read-compat channels (`answer` is the write source of truth; the SSE wrapper falls back to a legacy slot only when `answer is None`, gated so a followup's hydrated prior card can't leak in); AC3 pins this with `test_old_shape_checkpoint_hydrates_and_followup_works`, which seeds a genuine pre-`answer` checkpoint and drives a warm followup. (2) *monkeypatch* — 56 tests patch `graph_module.get_llm` (plus `build_narrate_prompt`, `_runtime_grounding_check`, `RETRIEVAL_SPECS`, `classify_intent_with_source`), so every node module references `agent.graph` helpers via the `graph` module object (attribute access at call time, not by-value import) and `graph.py` re-exports the moved names — zero test edits, all patches honoured. Also fixed two latent typing gaps found while here (`_structured_call`/`_linked_invoke` prompt param widened to `list | str` since the planner passes a `str`; `answer_slot` widened to `object`). AC4 code — full offline suite green (1580 passed / 53 deselected / 1 xfailed), `_PROMPT_VERSION` unmoved (`eba1dde080`, computed from the same two builder functions), and both LLM evals re-run live against a brought-up LiteLLM proxy + API + tunnel: `routing_eval` 26/26 (100%, 0 misses, 0 false positives), golden set hard contracts `hallucination_ok 41/41` + `tool_call_ok 41/41` (exit 0; the judge *composite* aggregate was throttle-degraded on the shared proxy and the eval flagged it as provider-pressure, not a code regression). The 41/41 hallucination pass empirically confirms the glyph normalization is scorer-neutral (the scaffold-strip only removes leading list numerals, never bullet glyphs). `code-reviewer-ediff` + a self-pass returned SHIP (no blocking; one real find fixed pre-merge — the extraction script had prefixed `logger` → `graph.logger` in the node modules, behaviour-identical since both resolve to the same `getLogger("agent.graph")` singleton but leaving each module's own logger dead, cleaned up). Two advisories left as follow-up candidates (not regressions — both faithfully preserve pre-refactor behaviour): `narrate`'s `thesis or answer` vs `_assistant_surface`'s `answer or thesis` payload-pick precedence divergence; and a guardrail test enumerating synthesize/clarify return dicts to catch a future branch copying the narrow-projection pattern instead of `project_answer`. Out of scope per ticket: any behaviour change (routing, prompts, payload contents all identical), the `prompts` package, and the non-answer `AgentState` fields.

- [x] Pay down the QNT-294 compat surface — retire legacy answer slots + record the monkeypatch decision — QNT-307
    - **Triggered by**: QNT-294 shipped the single discriminated-union `state['answer']` field but kept two deliberate compat surfaces to land the split with zero test churn: (1) the seven legacy `AgentState` answer slots (`thesis`/`quick_fact`/`comparison`/`comparison_lean`/`conversational`/`focused`/`exploration`) as deprecated read-compat channels, and (2) the `graph.py` re-export block + `graph_module` monkeypatch seam. Both were meant to be paid down once the migration settled. **The fix (slots — AC1/AC2)**: `project_answer` now writes only `answer`; the seven `NotRequired` slots are dropped from `AgentState`; the SSE `_card` legacy fallback in `agent_chat.py` collapses to a bare `isinstance(answer, cls)`; and every reader migrated to the union — `synthesize`/`narrate`/`support._assistant_surface` (the followup path), `eval_scores._render_answer`, `golden_set.run_record`, `agent/__main__.py`, plus two readers the ticket scope missed that a whole-repo sweep caught (`dialogue_eval._render_payload`, `rag_impact_eval._answer_text`, both looping the 7 keys). The followup path used to lean on the legacy `thesis` slot surviving across turns (followup returns never cleared it, non-thesis `project_answer` calls nulled it); it now reads a dedicated `prior_answer` channel snapshotted at `classify_node`, gated to carry **only a Thesis** so it reproduces the retired slot's lifetime exactly (a non-thesis intent nulls it, a narrative-only followup preserves it) — carrying any-shape would feed a non-thesis payload into `build_followup_prompt`'s "earlier thesis" section, an out-of-scope synthesis change. `clarify_node` and the synthesize narrow-returns, which previously wrote slot keys directly, now write only `answer` (a returned key for a retired channel is silently dropped by LangGraph). AC2's back-compat is real, not assumed: verified empirically that LangGraph **ignores** the stored value for a channel the current graph no longer declares (`update_state` with a legacy `thesis` key does not raise; the key is absent from hydrated state), so a pre-refactor SqliteSaver thread loads clean, `answer` reads as None, and the warm followup degrades gracefully off the still-hydrated `reports` — the round-trip test `test_old_shape_checkpoint_hydrates_and_followup_works` was rewritten to assert this. **The fix (monkeypatch — AC3)**: DEFER, recorded in **ADR-024**. The re-export/`graph_module` seam is a working test seam (56 `get_llm` patches + 27 direct imports across 16 files); decoupling it is ~80 edits of pure test-mechanics churn for zero runtime change (the AC itself notes "not a runtime need"), and the dominant `graph.get_llm` seam can't be migrated by simply patching `agent.llm.get_llm` — it's the same indirection shape pointed at a different module. The slot retirement is the debt worth paying; the seam is not, this cycle. **`code-reviewer-ediff` caught two blocking bugs my own pass missed, both fixed + pinned pre-merge**: (1) `online_eval._extract_generated` collapsed the 7 per-shape trace keys into one `answer` key and tried each class in order against it — but a `QuickFactAnswer` dict `{answer, cited_value, source}` validates as `ConversationalAnswer` (only `answer` required, pydantic ignores extras), so every quick_fact prod-eval trace mis-rendered as conversational and lost its cited value; fixed with exact field-set matching (`keys == model_fields`, disambiguating since all five shapes have distinct field sets), pinned by a new `tests/dagster/test_online_eval.py`. (2) `prior_answer` originally carried the last non-None answer of ANY shape (a followup after a comparison/quick_fact turn fed that payload where the old code passed `None`) — an unflagged synthesis behaviour change the ticket puts out of scope; fixed by the Thesis-only gate above, pinned by two new cross-intent followup tests (`test_prior_answer_carries_original_thesis_across_followup_chain`, `test_prior_answer_is_none_after_non_thesis_turn`). AC1 code (pinned by the migrated `test_graph.py`/`test_agent_chat.py` suites + a whole-repo slot-read sweep returning empty); AC2 code (pinned by `test_old_shape_checkpoint_hydrates_and_followup_works`); AC3 code (ADR-024 + a `graph.py` pointer); AC4 code — full offline suite green (1587 passed / 53 deselected / 1 xfailed), `prompt_version` hash unmoved (`eba1dde080`; 0 diff vs main in the prompt-defining modules). Net −86 lines. The two live evals (`routing_eval`, golden set) were NOT re-run (no TPD budget): `routing_eval` is orthogonal by construction (it calls `classify_intent_with_source`, untouched here, so routing cannot regress), and the golden-set reader migration is verified offline by `test_golden_set.py`. Out of scope per ticket: any behaviour change to synthesis/routing/answer-union shapes; the QNT-294 review advisories (payload-pick precedence + return-dict guardrail — QNT-309).

- [x] Harden the answer-projection contract — unify payload-pick precedence + return-dict guardrail — QNT-309
    - **Triggered by**: two QNT-294 review advisories deferred as follow-ups (siblings of QNT-307/308). (1) Divergent payload-pick precedence — `narrate_node` picked `prior_answer` first for followup while `_assistant_surface` picked `answer` first, disagreeing only on a followup-metric turn (narrate summarised the hydrated prior thesis, the transcript recorded this turn's quick_fact). (2) The narrow-projection convention was convention-only: the followup/clarify paths hand-write `{"answer": ...}` returns instead of routing through `project_answer`, uncaught by any type or validator. **The fix**: one shared `_pick_payload(state)` helper in `support.py` (`(prior_answer if followup else None) or answer`, exposed via the `graph` re-export) consumed by BOTH `narrate_node` and `_assistant_surface` — unified onto narrate's precedence (the documented, review-vetted "metric-ask followup narrates over the earlier thesis" design) so the user-visible narration is unchanged and only the transcript anchor converges. An AST guardrail (`test_no_new_narrow_projection_branch`) walks `_synthesize_payload` + `clarify_node`, collects every `return {…}` writing `answer` as an explicit key (correctly excluding `_answer`'s `**project_answer(...)` spread, whose unpack key is not an `ast.Constant`), and asserts the multiset matches a commented allow-list (3 synthesize + 2 clarify) — a new narrow branch fails it. **Both `code-reviewer-ediff` and my own pass caught the same missed second divergence**: my sanity-check "byte-identical for all non-followup turns" claim was false — the focused news/fundamental RAG-drop path (`{"answer": None}`, a non-followup intent) following a thesis turn previously borrowed the stale prior Thesis for the transcript anchor; the shared precedence returns None there instead, aligning the anchor with what narrate actually narrated (the report body, never a Thesis it never voiced). Corrected as intentional convergence, documented in `_pick_payload`, and pinned by `test_non_followup_answer_none_does_not_borrow_prior`. AC1 code (pinned by `test_followup_metric_substrate_is_prior_answer` + non-followup / narrative-only companions); AC2 code (pinned by `test_no_new_narrow_projection_branch`); AC3 code — full offline suite green (1591 passed / 53 deselected / 1 xfailed), `prompt_version` hash unmoved (no prompt text touched). Out of scope per ticket: the legacy-slot retirement (QNT-307) and re-export decoupling (QNT-308); any behaviour change beyond picking one precedence.

- [x] Unified tool registry contract — end bespoke RAG side channels per new corpus — QNT-291
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-4). Every retrieval tool that didn't fit the `Callable[[str], str]` plan surface had grown its own side channel — a typed alias, a `build_graph` kwarg, a `needs_*_search` `AgentState` flag, and a hardcoded `gather_node` branch (duplicated across the cold AND followup paths) plus an SSE instrument seam: `search_news` (QNT-222) and `search_earnings` (QNT-263) each paid this tax, and the ticket's own "next corpus" (a filings or transcript store) would pay it again. **The fix**: a declarative `RetrievalSpec` (name / classifier flag / corpus / fold fn / hit-noun) held in one `RETRIEVAL_SPECS` tuple; `gather_node` iterates it via a single `_run_retrievals` loop that replaces the four hand-written branches, gating each corpus with `RetrievalSpec.fires` → `_intent_reads_corpus` reading QNT-288's `INTENT_POLICIES[intent].rag_corpora` table (so the gate is sourced from the policy table, not a parallel frozenset). `build_graph` gains a name-keyed `retrieval_tools` mapping; the old `search_news_tool`/`search_earnings_tool` kwargs stay as deprecated shims that `setdefault` into it, so 15+ existing tests/eval callers passing them fire unchanged. The SSE seam in `agent_chat.py` wraps registry entries generically (`_RETRIEVAL_FETCHERS` + iterate `RETRIEVAL_SPECS`), reproducing identical `tool_name`/`hit_noun`. Behaviour-preserving: same tools fire on the same turns, same `[Rn]` provenance sequencing (news-first, earnings-offset, via registry order), same folds. **Scope decision (raised as a question before building; proceeded on no response)**: the registry unifies only the two retrieval-fold tools — the recurring pattern, and the one the "next corpus" joins. `compact_company` (a pre-gather slot-swap already driven by the QNT-288 `company_variant` field, never a gather branch) and `comparison_metrics` (comparison-topology-specific: fires only on the 3-4-ticker path, takes the whole ticker list, stashes JSON with no per-turn flag gate or provenance) stay out by design — folding them into a `(ticker, query)→fold` contract would be a mismatched abstraction, a `match` over unrelated dispatch modes rather than a real consolidation. **Orphan cleanup**: `_run_retrievals`/`_intent_reads_corpus` replaced the last callers of the derived `_NEWS_SEARCH_INTENTS`/`_EARNINGS_SEARCH_INTENTS` frozensets, so they were removed (the gate now reads the policy table directly) and every stale prose reference swept. AC1/AC2/AC4 code; AC3 code — a seam test (`test_registry_entry_alone_drives_gate_call_fold_provenance`) monkeypatches `RETRIEVAL_SPECS` to a single FAKE entry and drives gate→call→fold→provenance end to end, demonstrating that adding tool #4 is a registry entry + wiring the callable, nothing in `gather_node`. Full offline suite green (1567 passed / 53 deselected / 1 xfailed). Both `code-reviewer-ediff` and a self-pass returned SHIP (no blocking; advisories — the generic fold log line dropped the "targeted-"/"-release" wording; stale frozenset prose refs, swept pre-merge). Out of scope per ticket: native LLM tool-calling (ADR-007 determinism stands), any new tool/corpus (this makes the NEXT one cheap), the report-plan prompts.

- [x] Runtime numeric grounding for quick_fact turns — close the narrate-skip gap — QNT-296
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering review, second pass (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-8; C-4 folded in from the output-structure pass). QNT-232 #3 made `quick_fact` skip the `narrate` node on cost grounds (the `QuickFactAnswer` card is already analyst-voice prose) — correct on cost, but the runtime numeric-hallucination check and composite confidence (`_runtime_grounding_check` / `_composite_confidence`) lived INSIDE narrate's tail, so the quick_fact early return wrote none of `grounding_rate` / `grounding_unsupported` / `confidence`. Net effect: the one shape whose entire contract is "one cited numeric value" shipped with NO runtime numeric check and a coverage-only confidence chip, while every other analytical intent (thesis/comparison/focused/exploration/followup) got the check via narrate's tail. **The fix**: two new module-level functions in `graph.py` — `_quick_fact_grounding` (mirrors narrate's `_runtime_grounding_check`/`_composite_confidence` pair against the card's own `to_markdown()`) and `_quick_fact_cited_value_supported` (C-4: `cited_value`, when non-empty, must verbatim-match the report named by `source`) — called from inside `narrate_node`'s existing `intent == "quick_fact"` early-return branch, splatting the result dict alongside `narrative: None`. Logs the same clean/miss lines narrate's tail logs (same format string), so Langfuse/log analysis sees quick_fact grounding like every other shape. **Two correctness bugs found and fixed during self-review before the `code-reviewer-ediff` pass even ran**: (1) a numeric `cited_value` is embedded verbatim in `to_markdown()`'s `**Value:**` line, so it's already extracted and scored by the regex check — an unconditional `+1` to the denominator for every non-empty `cited_value` double-counted the same claim and skewed confidence upward in mixed-error turns (fixed via an `extract_numbers(cited_value) <= thesis_numbers` "already scored" guard; pinned by a regression test asserting the exact rate, 0.5 not 0.67). (2) a formatted `cited_value` (`"$1,234.56"`, a documented example shape from the field's own description) that fails C-4 was flagged using its RAW string alongside the already-present CANONICAL form in `unsupported`, double-penalising one claim and risking `grounding_rate` going negative (unclamped, unlike composite confidence) — fixed by flagging with the canonical numeric token(s) when the claim was already scored, the raw string only for a genuinely new non-numeric claim; pinned by a regression test proving the rate stays in `[0.0, 1.0]`. `code-reviewer-ediff` returned SHIP with one advisory, fixed pre-merge: the C-4 substring check (`cited_value in report`) was case-sensitive and not word-boundary-aware — false-positived on harmless case drift (`"Overbought"` vs. the report's `"overbought"`) and false-negatived on a garbled substring collision (`"sold"` inside `"oversold"` read as supported, exactly the invented-citation failure class C-4 exists to catch); fixed with a case-insensitive `(?<!\w)...(?!\w)` regex (not `\b`, which is undefined between two non-word characters like a leading `$`), pinned by two new tests. AC1 code (pinned by `test_quick_fact_grounding_clean_card_yields_full_confidence` + `test_quick_fact_grounding_fabricated_number_lowers_confidence`); AC2 code — traced structurally, not just asserted: the branch is gated on strict `intent == "quick_fact"`, and followup (which reuses `QuickFactAnswer` but keeps `intent="followup"`), conversational, and clarify all return earlier in `narrate_node`, so the new code is unreachable from those paths (full offline suite, 1370 passed, confirms no regression); AC3 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API, no prod deploy needed — pure agent-runtime change): a real NVDA RSI quick_fact turn's SSE `done` event carried `grounding_rate: 1.0, grounding_unsupported: [], confidence: 1.0` with `narrate` present in `intent_path`; AC4 code (pinned by `test_quick_fact_cited_value_verbatim_in_named_report_passes`, `..._absent_from_named_report_is_flagged`, `test_quick_fact_empty_cited_value_is_a_noop`, plus the two word-boundary regression tests added post-review). Out of scope per ticket: re-enabling narrate for quick_fact (QNT-232 #3 stands), blocking/retrying on a grounding miss (stays advisory, same as every other shape), detector scale-awareness (QNT-297).

- [x] Scale-aware numeric grounding: stop $5M passing as supported by $5B — QNT-297
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering review, second pass (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-9). The QNT-255 clean-window fix stripped a glued magnitude unit (`$2.5T` → `2.5`, `$14B` → `14`) in `_canonicalise` so a news report's `$14B` and the model's expanded `$14 billion` compared equal — correct, but it collapsed SCALE, so an answer's `$5M` counted as supported by a report's `$5B` (both → `5`). For a finance product a misquoted scale is the most screenshot-able numeric error the agent could ship, and unlike the sign/window blind spots it is a wrong magnitude, not idiom. **The fix** (following QNT-128's sharpen-don't-loosen precedent): `check()` now compares `(mantissa, scale)` pairs instead of bare mantissas. A spelled-out scale word immediately after a number (`$2.5 trillion`) is folded onto the mantissa (`_glue_spelled_scale`, `bn/tn/mn/k/m/b/t` + thousand/million/billion/trillion → `K/M/B/T`) before extraction so it still matches a report's compact `$2.5T`. Support rule: a claimed bare mantissa matches any report scale (preserves QNT-255); a report mantissa written bare (no glued unit) supports any claimed scale (no evidence of mismatch); only a *positive* conflict flags — the answer says `M` while every report occurrence of that mantissa says `B`. **Design deviation from the ticket's Scope wording** (flagged in the sanity-check + ship comments): the ticket suggested changing `extract_numbers` to return `(value, scale)` tuples, but its bare-`frozenset[str]` contract is depended on by `graph.py`'s subset comparison (`cited_numbers <= grounding_result.thesis_numbers`, `graph.py:939`), the `thesis_numbers`/`report_numbers` typing, `--explain`, and 6 existing extract tests — changing the return type would ripple destructively through all of them. Kept `extract_numbers` stable and added the scale layer as internal helpers (`_extract_pairs` → `(canonical_value, scale)` single-pass primitive; `extract_numbers` and `_extract_scaled` both derive from it), so all new behaviour lives in `check()` and the blast radius is one module. AC1 code (pinned by `TestScaleAwareGrounding` in `tests/agent/evals/test_hallucination.py` — `$5M` vs `$5B` flags, spelled `$2.5 trillion`/`$14 billion` match glued reports, bare `5` vs `$5B` unchanged); AC2 code (QNT-255 regression fixtures `TestMagnitudeUnit` stay green, plus a deterministic OLD-vs-NEW sweep over all 9 golden YAML fixtures / 1418 recorded strings and the 8 rag_impact planted-figure answer-vs-hit pairs showing zero new false positives — the honest caveat, noted in review, is that self-grounded strings can't produce a scale conflict by construction, so the scale dimension is carried by the unit tests + rag_impact cross-check, not the self-sweep); AC3 code (module docstring's "Scale collapse" removed from the accepted blind-spot list and replaced with a "Scale-aware support (QNT-297)" section stating it is NOT accepted; the sign-magnitude and window-idiom notes retained). `code-reviewer-ediff` returned SHIP (no correctness blockers — it independently traced the `bn/tn/mn` vs `b/t/m` mis-tag safety, sign+scale composition, and the no-op gluing guarantee); one advisory fixed pre-merge: `check()` originally ran `_prepare`+`_NUMBER_RE` four times per call (two texts × two views) on the runtime hot path — refactored to a single `_extract_pairs` pass per text (4 → 2), behaviour-preserving, all tests + sweep green. A second advisory (per-corpus rather than per-report bare-exempt narrows the real-world hit rate) is the exact support rule the ticket specifies and is covered by `test_report_with_both_bare_and_scaled_does_not_conflict` — left as-is. Out of scope per ticket: qualitative/entity claim checking (offline DeepEval owns it), where the runtime check runs (QNT-296), unit-aware arithmetic (ADR-003 — still string comparison), and the sign/window idiom blind spots (documented, still idiom).

- [x] Chat flow continuity: follow-up chips after analytical cards + plan-rationale status line — QNT-298
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 interaction-flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, items B-1 + B-2). Two conversation-continuity gaps: (1) follow-up suggestion chips only rendered on conversational/clarify cards (QNT-244/QNT-178) — after a thesis/quick_fact/comparison/focused/exploration card, the conversation dead-ended with no discovery path into the followup/comparison/exploration shapes the agent supports; (2) the thesis planner's analyst-voice `plan_rationale` (and exploration's `_exploration_rationale`) were computed but never left the process — narrate consumed them, but the gather->synthesize wait (the longest silent stretch of a turn) showed a bare spinner. Both fixes are deterministic, zero new LLM calls. **The fix**: (1) a new `followup_templates: tuple[tuple[Intent, str], ...] | None` field on the QNT-288 `IntentPolicy` table — each entry pairs a template (`{ticker}`/`{partner}` placeholders) with the intent a click on it would classify as; `analytical_followup_suggestions(intent, ticker, comparison_tickers)` in `graph.py` fills the templates (comparison uses the two actually-compared tickers; single-ticker intents use a new static `_COMPARISON_PARTNER` map for the `{partner}` slot) and re-validates every chip through the QNT-244 `is_answerable_suggestion` guardrail. `agent_chat.py` computes the list on the `done` SSE event, gated by a new `_analytical_card_present()` check so a synthesize-failure conversational fallback (which ships its own suggestions) never doubles up. Frontend renders a `SuggestionButton` row under the landed card, same prefill/auto-send contract as the existing conversational chips. (2) `plan_node` and `explore_supervisor_node` fire a new `plan_rationale` SSE event via the existing `event_emitter` callback the instant the rationale resolves (before gather's tool calls for a fresh thesis; right after them for exploration, which gathers inline in one node) — no event when `None` (quick_fact/focused/comparison plans carry none). Frontend renders it as a one-line italic status between the user prompt and the tool-call rows, hidden once any card lands. AC1 code (pinned by `test_suggestion_guardrail.py::test_analytical_followups_are_answerable_and_non_clarify`, parametrized over every covered ticker x every analytical intent, using `_detect_ambiguity` on each chip's target intent as the non-clarify proxy — same methodology the QNT-244 bank tests use); AC2 code (pinned by `test_graph.py::test_plan_node_emits_plan_rationale_via_event_emitter` / `test_plan_node_skips_emit_when_rationale_is_none` / `test_exploration_supervisor.py::test_explore_supervisor_emits_plan_rationale_via_event_emitter`; full offline suite green, 1456 passed); AC4 code (pinned by `test_plan_rationale_emission_fires_zero_extra_llm_calls`, asserting exact LLM call counts are unchanged with an `event_emitter` attached). AC3 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API + frontend, no prod deploy needed — pure agent/frontend runtime change): a real NVDA thesis turn's SSE trace showed `plan_rationale` firing immediately after `intent`, before the first `tool_call`; the `done` event carried `suggestions: ["What's the news angle on NVDA?", "Compare NVDA vs AMD", "What should I watch this week on NVDA?"]`; Playwright screenshots show the rationale line, thesis card, and chip row together, and clicking "What's the news angle on NVDA?" ran a full second turn end to end (new tool calls, new focused card, new chip row). `code-reviewer-ediff` returned SHIP (no blocking; advisory: `_COMPARISON_PARTNER` is a fifth ticker-keyed structure `docs/guides/ticker-lifecycle.md` doesn't list, though it fails loud via a completeness test rather than silently; the plan-rationale status line and the existing `ComposingBubble` spinner can render simultaneously during the gather->synthesize wait, a mild UX redundancy rather than a bug). Out of scope per ticket: LLM-generated suggestions (deterministic bank only), chips on the clarify/conversational paths (already shipped, QNT-244), any change to what narrate does with `plan_rationale`.

- [x] Warm-thread trust affordances: context-anchor chip + degraded-tool note + data as-of date — QNT-299
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 interaction-flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, items B-3 + B-4). Three invisible states erode trust on warm threads: (1) followups silently inherit `analysis_ticker` (QNT-245 rebase rules) with no visible signal of what the agent thinks "it" refers to; (2) optional-tool drops (news outage) ship a thesis with no apology, indistinguishable from "nothing worth citing"; (3) reports carry as-of dates internally but cards show none, leaving the `_composite_confidence` freshness factor stubbed at 1.0 since QNT-221 ("until report templates expose a uniform as-of date"). All three are deterministic surfacing of state that already exists — zero new LLM calls. **The fix**: a `format_as_of_footer()` helper appends a machine-parseable `AS_OF: YYYY-MM-DD` line to every report template (technical/fundamental/news/company), distinct from each report's existing human-readable "As of ..." header prose. `agent_chat.py` gained `_extract_data_as_of()` (regex-pulls the footer from this turn's gathered reports, returns the OLDEST date — the staleness bottleneck) and `_degraded_tools()` (bare tool names that hit a required-tool error or were silently dropped as optional), both surfaced on the `done` SSE event alongside `analysis_ticker` (the already-resolved chip source). Frontend: a `Context: <TICKER>` chip in the composer (click prefills "Switch to "), a muted degraded-tool note and "Data as of <date>" line under the landed card. Freshness-factor wiring into `_composite_confidence` deliberately deferred — the as-of plumbing landed, but picking a staleness-to-score formula is a design decision the ticket left optional, consistent with the prior "#6 freshness leg — dropped... not cleanly quantifiable" note in `docs/equity-analyst-improvement-v4.md`. **Two real bugs found by `code-reviewer-ediff` and fixed pre-merge**: (1) `_degraded_tools` read `state["errors"]` unconditionally, but `plan_node`/`gather_node` deliberately never touch `errors` on a followup turn (to avoid clobbering checkpointer-hydrated state) — a required-tool failure from an earlier turn rendered a permanent false "unavailable this turn" note on every later followup; fixed by skipping required-tool detection entirely when `intent == "followup"`. (2) For a rich 2-ticker comparison (exactly AC1's own example), the SSE-layer `reports` local is only the PRIMARY compared ticker's bundle — for "compare to AAPL" from /ticker/NVDA the primary is the NAMED ticker (AAPL), so NVDA's staleness/drops were invisible; fixed with a new `_report_bundles()` helper that scans `reports_by_ticker` (both compared tickers) when populated. Also hardened the AS_OF regex to anchor at end-of-body so a folded news headline can never be misread as the report's own footer. AC1 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API + frontend, screenshot attached to the Linear issue): a two-turn NVDA thread — thesis (chip: `Context: NVDA`), then a single-ticker rebase followup "what about AAPL now" (chip: `Context: AAPL`, fresh AAPL thesis card, 4 tools/15 citations) — confirmed comparison turns correctly do NOT rebase the chip (two subjects, not one) while a single-ticker followup does. AC2/AC3 code, pinned by `tests/api/test_agent_chat.py` (9 new tests incl. the two regression tests for the code-review catches) and `tests/api/test_templates.py` (7 new/updated AS_OF assertions); AC4 verified via `git diff --stat main...HEAD -- packages/agent/` returning empty. Out of scope per ticket: auth/thread-management UX (ADR-017 stands), retrying/alerting on degraded tools (ops), freshness-based answer refusal.

- [x] Output-contract hardening: verdict-vs-labels tripwire + normalizing enum validators — QNT-302
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 output-structure review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, items C-2 + C-3, folded — same contract-hardening domain). Two places where the output contract was documented but not enforced in code: (1) the Thesis Overweight/Underweight rule lived only in the `verdict` Field description, so a Thesis with unfavourable labels + an Overweight verdict validated and shipped; (2) enum looseness with a real frontend consequence — `AspectView.label` was `str | None` while the `AspectLabel` Literal sat exported-but-unused, and the frontend indexes its pill palette by the raw string (`ASPECT_LABEL_PILL[label]`), so an off-vocabulary label rendered a broken chip; `FocusedAnalysis` similarly accepted wrong-family verdicts (`focus=technical` + `verdict=Premium`) and news-only fields on non-news focuses. **Design rule: NORMALIZE, never raise** — a raising validator inside `with_structured_output` triggers the retry->fallback-redirect chain and turns a cosmetic mismatch into a lost answer. **The fix**: (AC1) `normalize_aspect_label` + a `mode="before"` field validator tighten `AspectView.label` and the `LeanComparisonRow` pill fields to `AspectLabel | None` (the exported Literal is now used; off-vocab/mis-cased -> the canonical spelling or `None`) — makes the backend honour the `AspectLabel | null` contract the frontend already assumed; (AC2) a `FocusedAnalysis` `model_validator(after)` nulls wrong-family verdicts and empties news-only fields on non-news focuses, logging one line per normalization, with `graph.py`'s focus re-assertion switched from `model_copy` to `model_validate` so the normalization tracks the corrected focus; (AC3) an advisory `Thesis` verdict-vs-labels tripwire (`verdict_matches_labels` + a logging `model_validator`) plus a `verdict_label_consistent` column wired into the golden runner (history.csv + summary line). Label semantics verified against `packages/api/src/api/templates/fundamental.py`: Premium = a valuation *caution* (multiple above own-history 75th pct / peer median), so favourable={Discounted, Uptrend}, unfavourable={Premium, Downtrend}. **Both reviewers (my own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) independently caught the same blocking bug**: `verdict_label_consistent` was inserted mid-list in `HISTORY_FIELDS`, which misaligns the ragged append-only `history.csv` on read (older rows are positionally shorter); fixed by appending at the tail, syncing the committed 51->52-col header, and pinning both the append-only invariant and the write->read roundtrip with tests. AC1 code (pinned by `tests/agent/test_thesis.py` case/junk/non-str + `test_lean_comparison.py`); AC2 code (pinned by `tests/agent/test_focused.py`, all three focus kinds + worst-case no-raise); AC3 code (tripwire + eval assertion `test_factory_fixture_thesis_is_consistent` + golden-wiring tests) — the **observed mismatch rate over the golden set** is deferred to QNT-258 (a full 41-record live run exceeds the free-tier Llama daily TPD; QNT-258 already runs the QNT-129 golden sweep on a clean window, so the rate rides along at zero marginal cost; folded via a QNT-258 comment); AC4 code (all four validators normalize/log only; 1503 offline tests pass, no new retry triggers). Out of scope per ticket: new verdict semantics, schema-shape changes (citation vocabulary is QNT-301), frontend palette changes, and nulling company/news labels in code (a review advisory — a *known*-spelling label on company/news doesn't break pill indexing; deferred as a follow-up).

- [x] Claim-anchored retrieved-source citations + tiered citation UX — QNT-301
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 output-structure + citation review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, items C-1 + C-5). Citation value is asymmetric and the design spent it evenly: retrieved RAG evidence (dated, external, verifiable news/8-K hits) folded INTO `reports["news"]`/`reports["fundamental"]` (QNT-263/276) and was cited as a generic `(source: fundamental)` with no linkage from any claim to the specific article, while the QNT-226 "Retrieved sources" list floated below the answer clickable-but-unanchored. **Direction: TIER the citation UX** — canned reports keep aggregate provenance (bar + quiet chips, unchanged); retrieved evidence gets claim-anchored citations. **The fix**: (AC1) `_format_search_hits`/`_format_earnings_hits` stamp each folded bullet with a stable `[Rn]` tag and `_parse_search_sources`/`_parse_earnings_sources` stamp the matching `id` on the `retrieved_sources` SSE rows; a `start_id` threaded through `_fold_*` and the two gather call-sites offsets earnings past the news hits so the combined list is `R1..Rn` gap-free across both corpora, aligned by construction (both format+parse iterate the same rows with identical skip predicates and the same `start_id`). (AC3) the API `_CITATION_PATTERN` accepts the `R\d+` tail; the hallucination detector is immune because the digit is glued to the `R` (its left-boundary lookbehind rejects it) — pinned by tests. (AC4) prompt-only, no schema field: the source `Literal`s are untouched and the id rides as a suffix inside the free-prose inline citation, keeping free-tier structured-output risk unchanged; no new LLM calls. Frontend: `prose-parse` recognises the `(source: news R1)` form and renders it as an emerald link-chip that scroll-highlights the matching `data-source-id` row (scoped per-run via `closest("article")`). **Two blocking bugs found in review, both fixed and re-verified live**: (1) my own pass — id-drift when a retrieved row has a null headline: `_format_*` used `row.get(k, "")` (returns `None` for an explicit JSON null → `str(None)` is the truthy `"None"`, keeping a row `_parse_*` skips), drifting every later `[Rn]` off its source id; fixed by unifying on the `or ""` extraction, pinned by `test_retrieved_ids_stay_aligned_when_a_row_has_no_headline`. (2) `code-reviewer-ediff` — the `[Rn]` tag is stamped for ALL retrieval-firing intents (thesis/quick_fact/fundamental/news/followup) but only the thesis prompt was taught it; **confirmed live** that the narrate voice (news/followup answers, which cite as `(publisher, date)`) appended a raw `[R1]` next to the citation. Two-layer fix: a shared `RETRIEVED_CITATION_ANCHOR_RULE` added to the quick_fact/focused/followup/narrate prompts (never quote the raw tag; carry its id into the citation — verified live that quick_fact now emits `(source: fundamental R1)`), AND a frontend render-boundary guarantee — `prose-parse` also recognises a BARE `[Rn]` token as the same anchor chip, so a raw tag can never reach the user regardless of model behaviour (verified live: the news narrate renders R1–R4 chips, no bracket text). AC1 code (pinned by `tests/agent/test_graph.py::test_retrieved_hit_ids_align_across_block_and_sources` + the null-headline regression); AC2 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API + frontend): a targeted NVDA thesis emitted `(source: fundamental R1)`/`(R3)`, the UI rendered the anchored link-chip and clicking it scrolled to + flashed the matching R1 retrieved-sources row (badged R1–R5); a canned-only quick_fact RSI ask fired no retrieval and rendered as before; screenshots attached. AC3 code (pinned by `test_count_citations_accepts_anchored_id_form`, `test_citation_anchor_id_is_not_a_number` incl. the bracketed form, `test_synthesis_prompt_instructs_anchored_retrieved_citation`, `test_retrieval_prompts_teach_id_anchor`); AC4 code (source Literals unchanged, no new `.invoke`; full offline gate 1509 passed). Out of scope per ticket: structured `{text, sources[]}` citations across all shapes (schema-fattening = free-tier structured-output risk; revisit only if the id form fails), canned-chip styling/dedupe (QNT-287/295 stand), retrieval behaviour (QNT-289/290 own that).

- [x] Senior-analyst voice v6: live-sample assessment across post-ADR-020 intents + supported rules — QNT-303
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 citation + voice review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, D-items). The voice work to date (ADR-020 persona, QNT-285 BLUF narrate, the v1 B-rules) was grounded in the 2026-05-18 assessment; the intents that shipped after it (exploration, lean comparison, followup narrative-only, clarify, QNT-276 retrieved-evidence news) had never had a voice audit, and six senior-analyst signatures (D-1..D-6) were hypotheses to confirm against samples, not pre-commitments. **Method (assessment-first, the thing that worked in v1)**: sampled 1,400 prod GENERATION observations over 45 days read-only from the Langfuse `/api/public/observations` API (ADR-019, GETs only), grouped by trace, bucketed by classify-node intent, and graded the `narrate` voice surface against a senior-analyst rubric → `docs/assessments/agent-analyst-voice-2026-07.md` (per-intent corpus table, D-1..D-6 scorecard, headline findings, verbatim samples, reproduction). **What the samples supported, and only that (AC2, no taste-only edits)**: (D-1 Falsifier) **0 of 63** recent narrations named what would flip the call — the strongest missing signature, confirmed universal; shipped `NARRATE_FALSIFIER_RULE` scoped to `_FALSIFIER_INTENTS={thesis, comparison}` (the two shapes that reliably print regime labels), anchored on a printed LABEL (Uptrend/Premium/RSI band) not a raw level so it stays ADR-003-safe. (D-6 Filler) 0 current hits but no deterministic guard existed → shipped `agent/analyst_voice.py::find_filler` + `_apply_deterministic_filler_gate` wired into `dialogue_eval.run_fixture`, capping the `voice_match` axis at 0 on any banned phrase regardless of the LLM judge — the no-regret twin of the QNT-156 conversational digit check (AC3). Also folded the narrate prompt (base + probe-close + falsifier) into the `prompt_version` hash — it was historically outside it, so a narrate voice edit had been shipping with an unchanged version; now the D-1 rule bumps it once. **Deferred with evidence**: D-2 (tension-naming already a strength in prod), D-3 (comparison bottom line — the narrate wrapper already emits a relative lean like "More cautious on NVDA relative to AAPL"; the structured card intentionally stays contrast-only, and the ticket requires explicit product approval to change it — asked, no response, applied the safe default of not shipping the card change), D-4 (quick_fact already pairs value+regime; the prior-session-direction grounding overlaps QNT-296, same shape), D-5 (no degraded-coverage narration existed in the 45d window to grade the failure against; pairs with QNT-299). **Latent bug caught by my own clean-window run**: an initial D-1 draft scoped to news made the model fabricate a "200-day moving average" no report printed, driving `msft-news-what-matters` to `non_hallucination=0.0` — fixed by narrowing the falsifier to thesis/comparison and anchoring on labels. **`code-reviewer-ediff` caught a blocking precision bug the fixtures missed**: the first "it's important to note" regex lacked a leading `\b`, false-firing on any word ending in "it" ("Deficit/Profit's/credit is important to note" → zeroed voice_match on legit prose); fixed with `\b` + regression fixtures, plus two advisories (dropped the low-precision "as mentioned" pattern; cleaned the rationale string). AC1 docs (`agent-analyst-voice-2026-07.md`); AC2 code (D-1→0/63, D-6→no-guard; `prompt_version` bump pinned by `test_changing_narrate_prompt_changes_version`; rules pinned by `tests/agent/test_analyst_voice.py`); AC3 code (`dialogue_eval.py::_apply_deterministic_filler_gate`, pinned by `test_filler_gate_zeroes_voice_match_on_filler`); AC4 dev-execution — before/after for thesis+comparison generated live (falsifier appears: "The read holds while the trend label stays Uptrend"), and a **paired clean-window run** (same 5 fixtures on main vs branch, judge via OpenRouter) showing every axis flat or up (voice_match +0.07, composite +0.034, non_hallucination 0.00) — no guardrail regression. Out of scope per ticket: citation UX (QNT-301), schema hardening (QNT-302), model/provider changes (QNT-292), report-template changes beyond a graded failure.

- [x] Citation-anchor integrity: drop hallucinated out-of-range retrieved-source ids — QNT-305
    - **Triggered by**: prod chat reports + 2026-07-03 Langfuse NVDA thesis traces — the QNT-301 anchor layer works, but in 2 of 4 recent anchor-citing runs the synthesis model **fabricated an out-of-range id**: the report fed to synthesis carried only `[R1]`/`[R2]` yet the answer cited `R5` and `R11`, pointing at no `retrieved_sources` row. The anchored chip then dangles (a silent `scrollToSource` no-op) and — worse — it is a **fake footnote**, undermining the one thing the citation layer exists to prove (ADR-003: the agent only quotes, never computes). Root cause is model invention, not a fold-numbering bug (the fold tagged R1/R2 correctly), so the fix is **deterministic at the render/emit boundary**, not a prompt-only nudge. **The fix**: a single Python source of truth — `agent/citations.py::strip_oob_anchors` (de-anchors `(source: name Rn)` → `(source: name)` and removes a bare `[Rn]` when `n` exceeds the retrieved-row count) + `strip_oob_anchors_in_obj` (recurses a card payload). (AC1/AC2 backend) every card dump in `agent_chat._stream` is stripped before the SSE emit, gated on `anchor_max = len(retrieved_sources) if "gather" in intent_path else 0` — mirroring the QNT-226 retrieved_sources emit gate exactly, so a stale-hydrated followup counts 0 rows. (AC2 frontend) the streamed **narrate bubble is not a card payload** (it streams as `narrative_chunk` deltas the backend can't cleanly strip), so `prose-parse.ts` de-anchors out-of-range ids client-side, wired from `run-block.tsx`; this reuses the QNT-301 bare-`[Rn]` precedent. Together the two boundaries cover all five anchor-citing shapes (thesis, quick_fact, focused, followup, narrate). (AC3 eval) `eval_scores.compute_anchor_integrity` flags any cited id past the (gather-gated) row count across card + narrate, pushed as the deterministic `anchor_integrity_ok` score on every prod chat — the standing regression guard and the live signal for the intermittent bug. (Secondary) the shared `RETRIEVED_CITATION_ANCHOR_RULE` prompt now forbids numbering past the largest printed id. **`code-reviewer-ediff` caught two blocking bugs my own pass missed**: (1) the frontend `maxAnchor` was fed `run.retrievedSources.length` live, but `retrieved_sources` is emitted post-graph — strictly *after* the narrate deltas stream — so for the whole live narration the count was `0` and **every in-range anchor was stripped** until the event landed (permanent on an aborted stream); fixed by gating on stream completion (`isStreaming ? undefined : length`) so the guard only fires once the final count is authoritative. (2) `compute_anchor_integrity` omitted the `"gather" in intent_path` gate the render boundary uses, so a stale-hydrated followup would let a fabricated id pass as `clean` on exactly the case the guard strips; fixed to the same gate, pinned by a stale-followup test. AC1 code (pinned by `tests/agent/test_citations.py` out-of-range + in-range control, and `prose-parse.test.ts`); AC2 code (backend strip pinned by `test_out_of_range_anchor_stripped_from_thesis_card_over_sse` threading a fabricated R5 through the real SSE thesis emit; frontend de-anchor pinned by `prose-parse.test.ts` card + narrate paths); AC3 code (`tests/agent/test_eval_scores.py` incl. the stale-followup divergence); AC4 dev-execution — deterministic before/after through the real emit-boundary fns on the reported R5/[R11]-with-only-R1/R2 case (R5→`(source: news)`, `[R11]` removed, R1/R2 untouched; detector flags `[5, 11]`), the natural live-SSE repro being non-deterministic (2-of-4) and observable via the new `anchor_integrity_ok` score. Out of scope per ticket: voice/D-items (QNT-303), chip styling / canned-chip dedupe (QNT-287/295/301), retrieval quality (QNT-289/290).

- [x] Turn hygiene: cancelled-turn checkpoint test + parallel report gather — QNT-300
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 interaction-flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, items B-5 + B-6, folded — same turn-hygiene domain). **B-5 (test-first, accept-and-document)**: the chat panel aborts the in-flight SSE run on a new message / unmount, and `agent_chat._stream` cancels the runner task on client disconnect — but the graph runs in `asyncio.to_thread`, and cancelling the asyncio task cannot kill the thread, so the worker finishes in the background and its checkpointer writes (reports, transcript, thesis) still land. `tests/agent/test_cancelled_turn.py` reproduces the exact endpoint mechanism (`create_task(to_thread(...))` → `.cancel()` → `shield` suppressing `CancelledError`) against a real `SqliteSaver` graph with one gated tool, and confirms the invariant: **a cancelled-but-completed turn commits its assistant transcript entry identically to a delivered one, and a follow-up on the same `thread_id` anchors on the turn the user never saw**. Decision: **accept and document** (not "mark the turn") — the worker thread has no cancellation signal at write time, and gating the transcript append on SSE delivery would require plumbing a delivery signal back into the checkpoint write across the thread boundary, exactly the turn-delivery infrastructure the ticket scopes out. The divergence is bounded (compact surface text only) and self-heals (a follow-up surfaces the referenced content to the user); rationale lives in the test module docstring, cheap future lever (API-side checkpoint deletion on disconnect) noted as race-prone and deferred. **B-6 (measure, then parallelise)**: `_gather_reports` drove the planned tools serially. Measured from the agent's side against a live API (`scripts/bench_gather_latency.py`, cross-checked with direct `curl` timings — `news` which hits Qdrant/CH is the *fastest* call and `company` which skips CH is among the slowest, so the cost is API-side per-request work, not tunnel/DB latency, making the numbers roughly prod-representative): per-call p50 367–1098ms, **thesis 4-serial ≈2937ms p50, comparison 8-serial ≈5878ms p50** — both far over the 300/600ms decision thresholds, and per-call is hundreds of ms so the "win is noise next to synthesize" case is ruled out. **The fix**: `_gather_reports` now fans the callable planned tools onto a bounded `ThreadPoolExecutor` (workers = `min(plan size, 4)`), assembling `reports`/`errors` in a second `plan`-order pass so the output is byte-for-byte identical to the old serial loop (retry / optional-drop / tool-not-registered / error-string contract unchanged; `_call_with_retry` swallows every tool exception so no future raises; the `with` block joins all workers, no leak). The comparison caller still loops tickers sequentially (two parallel batches, per the cap-4 note — not an 8-wide fan-out). End-to-end against the same live API: **thesis 2937→944ms (~3.1×), comparison 5878→1714ms (~3.4×)**. AC1 code (pinned by `tests/agent/test_cancelled_turn.py` — commit-survives-cancel invariant + follow-up-anchors consequence); AC2 docs (p50/p95 numbers recorded in the PR body); AC3 code (parallelisation in `packages/agent/src/agent/graph.py`, all 109 existing `test_graph.py` tests pass unchanged plus two new tests — `test_gather_reports_runs_tools_concurrently`, which uses a `threading.Barrier` that *deadlocks a serial implementation* so it genuinely proves concurrency, and `test_gather_reports_concurrent_preserves_optional_and_error_contract`). Both reviewers (my own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned no correctness blockers; one advisory fixed pre-merge (docstring clarified that the cross-ticker comparison loop stays sequential so a future reader doesn't read the 5.9s motivation as "comparison is fully parallel"). Out of scope per ticket: a visible stop-generation button (client abort already exists), parallelising the gated single-call RAG searches, and any per-thread concurrent-message queueing beyond the B-5 findings.

- [x] Gather node: parallel cross-ticker comparison gather + followup early retrieved_sources emit (v3 G-3/G-9) — QNT-321
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, items G-3 + G-9) — two surgical `gather_node` gaps left by QNT-300/QNT-305. **G-3 (perf)**: QNT-300 parallelised `_gather_reports` *within* a ticker but left the comparison caller looping tickers serially — a rich 2-ticker gather ran as two sequential parallel batches (~1.7s), even though QNT-300's cap is about *concurrent connections*, not batches. **The fix**: `_gather_reports_multi` (`agent/support.py`) fans every `(ticker, tool)` pair onto ONE `ThreadPoolExecutor(max_workers=min(len, 4))`, assembling `reports_by_ticker` + the ticker-prefixed `errors` map in a second `tickers × plan`-order pass so the output is byte-for-byte identical to the old serial per-ticker loop (same retry / optional-drop / `{ticker}.{tool}` error-tagging contract). The single shared pool holds the same max-4-in-flight bound while overlapping across tickers. **G-9 (bug)**: the QNT-290 followup RAG branch returned *before* the QNT-305 early `retrieved_sources` SSE emit that the cold path already had — so a warm-thread turn that fired RAG streamed `Rn` anchors with no row count until the post-graph emit, the exact mid-stream flicker the early emit was added to kill, alive on the one path that skipped it. **The fix**: hoisted the emit into a shared `_emit_retrieved_sources` helper (`gather.py`) called before returning on *both* the followup and cold branches; the post-graph emit in `agent_chat` stays as the idempotent safety net. AC1 code (pinned by `test_gather_reports_multi_matches_serial_per_ticker_loop` — diffs the two implementations directly — and `test_gather_reports_multi_caps_in_flight_at_four`, a counting fake tool asserting `peak ≤ 4`); AC2/AC3 code (followup SSE-order pinned by `test_followup_rag_emits_retrieved_sources_before_narrate`; cold-path order still guarded by the pre-existing `test_gather_emits_retrieved_sources_before_narrate`). **AC4 dev-execution** — live before/after on a rich NVDA-vs-AAPL comparison via a new `--gather-compare` bench mode (`scripts/bench_gather_latency.py`, QNT-300's method), through the SSH ClickHouse tunnel + local API: **BEFORE serial loop 1717.6ms p50 → AFTER shared pool 1316.0ms p50 (1.31×)**. The tunnel adds a fixed per-call SSH round trip to every call equally, which dampens the *ratio* (the overlap benefits only the variable API-work portion) — co-located prod trends toward the plan's ~0.9s; the BEFORE figure matched the predicted ~1.7s almost exactly. Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blocking issues. Out of scope: the 3-4 ticker lean-metrics path (QNT-224, single-call, unaffected), and any change to WHICH intents fire retrieval.

- [x] Paid inference primary for public launch: DeepSeek V4 Flash via OpenRouter + global breaker recalibration — QNT-258
    - **Triggered by**: the imminent public LinkedIn launch (~10–20 concurrent visitors). A load review found the Hetzner CX41 + async SSE path handle the concurrency fine — the binding constraint was the Groq free-tier daily token ceiling: at ~14K tokens/substantive chat the 200K global breaker tripped after ~15 chats, a silent quota wall on launch night. Compounded by Groq's 2026-06-17 decommission retiring the entire synthesize-capable free chain (scout 07/17, 70b 08/16; every survivor caps at 8000 TPM → 413 on a 9–12K synthesize), which also killed the "flip Groq 70b to paid" option. **The move**: promote the synthesize/narrate primary (`equity-agent/default`) off Groq llama-3.3-70b to the paid **DeepSeek V4 Flash via OpenRouter** ($0.09/$0.18 per M, ~$0.002/chat), removing the daily cap (ADR-025, extends ADR-021 / ADR-011). **Bench-gated promotion (quality before capacity)**: a 41-record golden sweep on a clean window showed DeepSeek meets or beats the llama-3.3-70b baseline on every hard gate — hallucination_ok 40/41 vs 39/41, judge composite 5.634 vs 4.293, cosine 0.431 vs 0.408, harness p50 15.3s vs 14.3s (parity), and a far tighter p90 tail (36.8s vs 128s — the exact throttled-tail failure mode ADR-021 targeted); routing_eval 26/26 (classifier flag preserved, no intent drift); verdict_label_consistent 4/41 vs baseline 0/41. **Key discovery (ticket premise was wrong)**: DeepSeek V4 Flash on OpenRouter defaults to **reasoning ON** (37–89 CoT tokens/call even at `reasoning_effort: low`), not "non-reasoning" as the ticket assumed — left on it produced a degenerate first bench (~30 min vs ~10 min), intermittent empty completions (CoT ate the token budget → `content: null`), and uniform ~0.9–0.96 narrate grounding-miss on every ticker; fixed by `extra_body: {reasoning: {enabled: false}}` on the `default` + bench aliases (verified `reasoning_tokens → 0`, also aligns the QNT-275 DeepEval judge with ADR-023). **Breaker recalibration (AC4)**: `CHAT_TOKENS_GLOBAL_PER_DAY` 200K → 20M — on a paid plan there's no free-tier TPD to proxy, so it becomes a pure runaway-cost/abuse breaker (~1,400 chats, ~$2.7/day worst-case ceiling), still fail-closed; the per-IP token budget (30K/day) + rate limit (5/min;30/hour;100/day) are unchanged and do the real anti-abuse work. AC5 was converted from a deferred live burst to a **deterministic** unit test (`test_paid_breaker_survives_30_chat_launch_free_tier_tripped_at_15`): 30 chats survive 20M, the old 200K trips at ~15. **Fail-closed safety invariant changed, not deleted** (`tests/agent/test_litellm_fail_closed.py`): "free-tier only" was impossible once the primary is paid, so it became "permitted providers only" (groq/gemini/google/openrouter) while still forbidding frontier providers (anthropic, direct openai, azure, bedrock, vertex, …) across the whole reachable chat chain, with the regex string-scan as a backstop that catches `anthropic/`/`openai/` even routed through OpenRouter; the runtime contract (a quota error degrades to a `ConversationalAnswer`, never propagates) is unchanged. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real blocker**: AC3's "working fallback anchor" had no liveness evidence in the durable artifact — verifying it live surfaced a real problem and changed the shipped config. Nemotron 3 Ultra (`nvidia/nemotron-3-ultra-550b-a55b:free`, 1M ctx, structured-outputs capable so it serves both synthesize and narrate) verified clean (`finish_reason=stop`) and kept as THE anchor; **Laguna M.1** (`poolside/laguna-m.1:free`), originally chosen as a second anchor, returned upstream 429s + empty completions on a live smoke test and was **dropped** — a known-flaky last hop only added retry latency before the deterministic fallback. Final chain: `default (DeepSeek) → fallback-nemotron-ultra → deterministic fallback (fail-closed)`. Free OpenRouter models are used ONLY in the fallback slot (user decision, ADR-025), overriding the ticket's "free = bench-only" for that slot alone — the primary stays paid, so train-on-prompts/rate-limit exposure is bounded to rare fallback events. AC8 ride-alongs recorded in the same window: post-QNT-307 golden green (single discriminated-union `answer` field renders live), routing 26/26, verdict_label rate 4/41. AC9 (QNT-303 narrate two-part-close A/B) deferred as a documented follow-up (QNT-303 owns narrate voice; no prompt change expected). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1593 passed; ADR-025 written + ADR-021/011 cross-linked; bench in `docs/model-bench-2026-07.md`. Out of scope: per-node tiering of cheap nodes (QNT-220), graph/fallback-topology re-architecture, a permanent paid multi-provider gateway (noted as launch-day insurance only), and the full Groq fallback + eval-baseline re-anchoring (follow-up — the `small` tier's Groq hop still dies 07/17). **Post-ship follow-up (folded in)**: a Sentry error (EQUITY-DATA-AGENT-8) surfaced within minutes of deploy — DeepSeek intermittently returns the `ConversationalAnswer` reply as **bare prose** instead of the JSON envelope (an inherently conversational task), tripping a `json_invalid` ValidationError that the `_structured_call` ladder recovers via the deterministic clarify fallback (handled, 0 users) but that Sentry still captures + costs 2 retries + loses model tailoring. Fixed by passing `method="function_calling"` to the two conversational `_structured_call` sites (clarify + conversational-prompt) so the structured data returns as tool-call args — a channel the model can't fill with prose — verified 14/14 valid live; the validated `Thesis`/synthesize path keeps the default json_schema method untouched. Test stubs' `with_structured_output` signatures widened to accept the method kwarg; pinned by `test_clarify_uses_function_calling_method`.

- [x] ADR: paid synthesis economics + the free-tier simplification dividend — QNT-292
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-5). QNT-258 shipped the *forced* paid primary (DeepSeek V4 Flash) under the Groq-decommission deadline and wrote ADR-025; this ticket is the deliberate follow-on that records the two things 258 deferred — the **economics** ADR-011 was always missing, and the **simplification dividend** now that the free-tier walls the architecture accreted around are gone. Docs-only: `docs/decisions/026-...md` (extends ADR-025, cross-links ADR-011/021/023) + the stale `docs/INDEX.md` ADR list backfilled (024/025/026). **AC1 economics (measured, not guessed)**: pulled synthesize/narrate token volume from Langfuse over an exact 14×24h window (2026-06-21→07-04, 148 `agent-chat` turns) via the metrics API. Per ADR-019 every generation is named `ChatOpenAI` (request-boundary CallbackHandler, no per-node spans), so the split is by served alias: the paid path (`equity-agent/default` + Scout fallback overflow + gpt-oss-120b terminal) = 842,723 in / 71,848 out ≈ **6.2K paid tokens/turn, input-dominated ~12:1**; `equity-agent/small` (classify/plan, 197K/13.5K) **stays free** and is excluded.
