Cost table × three providers → DeepSeek **$0.19/mo at 1× demo traffic, $1.90 at 10×** (alternates GPT-4o-mini $0.36/$3.63, Groq-70b — the decommissioned incumbent, illustrative — $1.19/$11.87), plus a 500-chat/day launch-burst reference (~$20/mo). Cost is not the constraint at any modelled scale; reliability is. **AC2 dividend**: a keep/remove/simplify verdict over all six free-tier layers named in Context — genuine removals are only two (the residual dead Groq fallback chain, and the newly-unlocked prompt-cache lever); the other four (per-IP fence, tail timeout, variance gating, served-model tracker) plus per-node tiering are provider-independent and stay. The measured 12:1 input skew is what reframes prompt caching (ADR-021 declined it as permanent on the free 8K-TPM wall) into the single biggest open cost lever. Each removal filed as a follow-up referencing the ADR: **QNT-317** (re-anchor + retire the dead Groq fallback chain — Scout dies 07/17, Todo + cycle) and **QNT-318** (revisit prompt caching). **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real omission**: the dividend table enumerated five layers but Context named six — per-node tiering (QNT-220 #7) had no verdict row despite being classified as a free-tier artifact; added as an explicit KEEP (gpt-oss-20b survives; free classify/plan saves cost regardless), plus two advisories fixed (window off-by-one — re-queried the exact 14×24h boundary, numbers identical; a $/turn display cell). Out of scope: the forced primary/fallback wiring + breaker recalibration (QNT-258 owns it), moving classify/plan off the small model (tiering stands), executing the deletions (each ships on its own follow-up).

- [x] Re-anchor + retire the Groq free-tier fallback chain before the decommission — QNT-317
    - **Triggered by**: ADR-026 (QNT-292) simplification dividend + the re-anchoring QNT-258 deferred. ADR-025/258 moved the paid primary to DeepSeek V4 Flash and collapsed default's chain to `default → nemotron-ultra → deterministic`, but deliberately left the residual Groq free-tier fallback machinery — which still pointed at models Groq is decommissioning (llama-4-scout + qwen3-32b die 2026-07-17; llama-3.3-70b + llama-3.1-8b die 2026-08-16). Deadline-driven: Scout's hop in the `small` chain dies 07/17. **The change (config + sync sweep, no behaviour rewrite)**: (1) re-anchored the `small` tier from `small → default → fallback-llama4scout → gpt-oss-120b` to just `small → default` — `default` is the paid primary (no daily cap) and litellm fallbacks are recursive, so `small` transitively inherits `default`'s own nemotron anchor; the dead Scout/gpt-oss-120b tail (ADR-026's REMOVE-residual verdict) is gone. (2) Deleted the `fallback-llama4scout` (Scout, retiring) and `fallback-groq-gptoss120b` (its downstream hop, survives but orphaned once Scout's chain was removed) model_list aliases. (3) Retired the three retiring bench aliases (`bench-llama4scout`, `bench-qwen3-32b` — 07/17; `bench-llama3-70b` — 08/16, the old production-default calibration line, superseded by `bench-deepseek-v4-flash`). **Sync sweep (broader than the YAML)**: the retiring aliases were also referenced in `agent/llm.py`'s `_RESOLVED_MODEL_BY_ALIAS` trace-tag map (kept 1:1 with the config) and `scripts/evals/token_summary.py`'s bench-alias list — both pruned — and two test overrides pointed `set_model_override` at `bench-qwen3-32b`, repointed to the surviving `bench-gptoss20b` (both tests still assert the judge stays pinned while a *non-judge* alias is overridden). Two stale fallback-fire comment examples naming the deleted Scout alias (llm.py docstring + agent_chat.py) updated to nemotron. **Fail-closed contract preserved** (AC2, `tests/agent/test_litellm_fail_closed.py` 6/6): the re-anchored chain still terminates on a real model (`default`, then nemotron), and `graph.py::_structured_call` (untouched) degrades a throttle to a deterministic ConversationalAnswer regardless of alias. AC1 code (grep-verified: no live `llama-4-scout`/`qwen3-32b`/`llama-3.3-70b`/`llama-3.1-8b` reference in model_list, fallbacks, or the map); AC3 code (ADR-026 REMOVE-residual verdict cited at every deletion site in `litellm_config.yaml`). Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blockers; one advisory swept (the agent_chat.py comment), two left with rationale (README.md / `system-overview.md` describe the pre-QNT-258 default chain — pre-existing 258 drift, out of AC scope which scopes doc reflection to config comments; `aggregate_bench.py` names `bench-llama3-70b` as accurate history of a real QNT-138 re-run). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1594 passed. Out of scope: prompt caching (QNT-318 owns it), the README/architecture-doc default-chain drift (pre-existing QNT-258 cleanup).

- [x] Revisit prompt caching on the paid synthesize call now the free-tier TPM wall is gone — QNT-318
    - **Triggered by**: ADR-026 (QNT-292) simplification dividend, which reframed prompt caching from "declined, permanent" (ADR-021 #11, killed on the free 8K-TPM per-request wall) into "the single biggest remaining cost lever" once the bill went paid + input-dominated (~12:1). **Outcome: ENABLED** via an ordered OpenRouter provider pin on `equity-agent/default` (ADR-027, config change). **The investigation had a false start worth recording**: the first pass *declined* on a two-call cold probe that showed `cached_tokens` 0 (unpinned) / flat 64 (DeepInfra) and concluded "privacy-compliant providers don't prefix-cache." That was an under-powered test — it stopped **before the provider's cache warmed**. The OpenRouter dashboard (aggregate hit rates Novita 83.5%, DeepInfra 54.5%, …) prompted a re-measurement that reversed it. **Corrected finding + evidence (2026-07-05)**: the blocker was never model capability — DeepSeek V4 Flash caches — but that OpenRouter serves it from ~16 providers **each with its own KV cache** and load-balances across them, so unpinned calls hop providers and never reuse a warm cache. Fix: pin an **ordered** provider preference (`extra_body.provider.order`) so routing sticks to the first provider and its prefix cache stays warm. Verified live (5× sticky Novita, 100% warm = 9,472/9,487) **and through the litellm SDK** (drop_params does NOT strip the `provider` block: sticky Novita, cached 2,432→8,192→8,192; even a fresh prompt's call-1 gets ~2.4K = the shared `SYSTEM_PROMPT` floor). **Config**: `order: [novita, deepinfra, gmicloud, deepseek, alibaba, baidu]` (top-6 by OpenRouter token share; **privacy-compliant three first**, data-retaining three last as deep resilience only), `allow_fallbacks: false` (stay in-set; litellm's nemotron anchor still backstops), `data_collection: allow` **scoped to this alias only** (user decision — the public-equity chat carries no PII and is already public/no-auth per ADR-017; account default stays strict so the DeepEval judge + other aliases are untouched). Cache reads bill ~0.2× input (≈80% off) on Novita/DeepInfra; strict improvement (caching + cheaper/deterministic serving) at the cost of provider concentration (mitigated by the ordered fallback set). **Deliverables**: ADR-027 rewritten (declined→enabled, with the same-day correction note preserved) and renamed `027-prompt-caching-enabled-via-provider-pin.md`; ADR-021 #11 note + ADR-026 dividend row (REVISIT→ENABLED) + revisit-trigger updated; `docs/INDEX.md`, memory, and this entry updated; `test_litellm_fail_closed.py` 6/6 still green (provider slugs aren't `model:` fields; no anthropic/openai string added). **No golden-sweep re-run**: prefix caching is a transparent KV optimization — served tokens + sampling are identical, so output can't regress (DeepSeek V4 Flash already gated in QNT-258). Prod steady-state `cached_tokens` to be confirmed in Langfuse post-deploy. Out of scope: relaxing the account-level data policy (per-alias is the surgical form); pinning the bench/judge aliases (a noted follow-up opportunity — the fixed-rubric judge would cache well too).

- [x] Smoke each pinned OpenRouter provider serves the structured output (reasoning-off) — QNT-319
    - **Triggered by**: ADR-027 (QNT-318) left a **Watch (deep-fallback parity)** note — QNT-318 pinned an ordered top-6 OpenRouter provider set on `equity-agent/default` for prefix caching but only exercised the three lead providers (novita/deepinfra/gmicloud); the three deep-fallbacks (deepseek/alibaba/baidu) were unverified on the `reasoning.enabled:false` + forced structured-output axis — the exact axis that produced the QNT-258 "DeepSeek prose `json_invalid`" regression. **Deliverable**: `scripts/smoke_openrouter_providers.py`, an opt-in dev-run smoke that pins each of the six providers individually (`provider.only`) through the litellm proxy and, reasoning-off, exercises three arms — `synthesize(Thesis)` (the real prod structured shape on this alias), the array-bounded `ThesisPlan` capability probe, and narrate — reporting per-provider pass/fail with `finish_reason` + schema-parse evidence over N attempts. **Finding: all six serve every arm** (`finish_reason=stop`, valid parse); the three deep-fallbacks are confirmed. Caveat is a **per-attempt prose-flake** (a provider intermittently returns prose instead of the JSON envelope — the known QNT-196 ~5.5% phenomenon), bounded in prod by `_structured_call`'s two-attempt retry + deterministic fail-close; the smoke runs N attempts and treats a provider as capable if it parses at least once, surfacing the flake ratio. **No config reorder** (AC2's "record" branch taken): no provider is categorically incapable, and the array-bounded `ThesisPlan` never runs on these providers in prod anyway (it runs on the Groq `equity-agent/small` alias). **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real omission**: the first cut tested only `ThesisPlan`, which does NOT route through `equity-agent/default` in prod (`plan.py` pins it to the Groq small alias) — so the actual risk surface (`Thesis` synthesize, `synthesize.py`) was untested and the ADR cited unreproducible ad-hoc `Thesis` numbers; fixed by adding the `synthesize(Thesis)` arm (now the numbers reproduce from the committed script) and rescoping the `ThesisPlan` arm's docstring to an honest capability probe. Two advisories sweeped (`--providers` typo validation → exit 2; `--attempts` clamped ≥1 to avoid an empty-results IndexError), one left (narrate `.invoke` vs prod `.stream` — the arm only asserts a clean completion). AC1 dev-execution-verified (6 providers × 3 arms × N=3, all PASS, exit 0); AC2 code/docs (ADR-027 Watch note resolved); AC3 code (opt-in script under `scripts/`, not collected by pytest `testpaths=["tests"]`, no CI/Makefile reference — CI makes no paid calls). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1594 passed. Out of scope: changing the provider order or caching config (QNT-318/ADR-027 owns it); adding the smoke to the default CI gate.

- [x] Tripwires: LiteLLM alias-map sync test + comparison RAG demand detector + small-alias liveness smoke (v3 G-13/G-14/G-15) — QNT-326
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, items G-13 + G-14, plus a G-15 small-alias sunset guard added the same day) — three zero-behaviour-change tripwires. **G-13**: `agent/llm.py`'s `_RESOLVED_MODEL_BY_ALIAS` (the alias→upstream-model map that stamps Langfuse traces, QNT-182) is hand-synced with `litellm_config.yaml`, and QNT-317 had to prune the dead Groq aliases by hand — a drift silently mis-attributes the served model on every trace. **The fix**: `test_resolved_model_map_is_in_sync_with_litellm_config` (`tests/agent/test_litellm_fail_closed.py`) asserts every map key exists in the YAML `model_list` and its value equals `litellm_params.model` (reuses the existing `_load_config`/`_models_by_alias` helpers); mutating one entry trips it (verified, reverted). **G-14**: comparison's `IntentPolicy.rag_corpora` is empty because `RetrievalSpec.fold` cannot address `reports_by_ticker`, so a targeted-event comparison ("compare NVDA and AMD on their antitrust exposure") silently discards the classifier's `needs_*_search` flags. Per the RAG-seams lesson (ship a detector with each deferral), NOT the per-ticker fold: `_comparison_rag_demand` (`agent/nodes/gather.py`) records the '+'-joined discarded corpora ("news"/"earnings"/"news+earnings") on state `comparison_rag_demand`, gather logs it, and `agent_chat.py` stamps a `comparison_rag_demand:<corpora>` Langfuse tag — a count on that tag is the demand signal for whether the fold is worth building. **G-15**: `equity-agent/small` (classify/plan every turn) still points at Groq `gpt-oss-20b` with no confirmation it survives the Groq sunset; a kill degrades silently (classify BLE001 → intent=thesis, `classifier_source="fallback"`, keyword-floor-only RAG, over-fetching planner) with nothing paging, and the QNT-319 provider smoke covers only the pinned OpenRouter providers. **The fix**: `scripts/smoke_small_alias.py`, an opt-in dev smoke (QNT-319 pattern) that fires one structured `ThesisPlan` call on the small alias — a sunset shows up as a red smoke run instead of silent `classifier_source="fallback"` drift. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real blocker**: the demand marker bled across turns — `AgentState` persists via the checkpointer and only gather's comparison branch writes the key, so a later followup/conversational/thesis turn (short-circuit intents skip gather entirely) inherited a prior comparison turn's "news" and stamped a false tag. **The fix**: `classify_node` resets `comparison_rag_demand: ""` at the turn boundary (classify runs first on every turn; gather overwrites within the same comparison turn); regression test `test_comparison_rag_demand_does_not_bleed_across_turns` uses a real `SqliteSaver` + shared `thread_id` across two invokes (verified: fails without the reset). Second review pass returned SHIP. AC1/AC2/AC3 code, AC4 docs (the v3 doc is gitignored — G-14 "Shipped" marker + new G-15 section written on disk). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1605 passed. Out of scope: building the per-ticker comparison RAG fold (deferred pending the G-14 demand signal), re-anchoring the small tier off Groq (G-15 posture is detect-not-preempt).
- [x] Graph flow: routing + narrate-substrate decisions written to state once (v3 G-1/G-2) — QNT-320
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 graph-flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, findings G-1/G-2) — the same cross-node drift class QNT-288's policy table killed for frozensets, re-formed for predicates re-derived between nodes. **G-1**: on the focused RAG-drop path synthesize returns `answer=None` and narrate re-derived the *identical* `needs_news_search`/`needs_earnings_search` predicate to pick its narrative-only substrate (the code comment literally said "the guards mirror the synthesize-side drop condition exactly") — two copies of one decision that QNT-263 (a hand-synced set missing `quick_fact`) shows how to break. **G-2**: `_classify_router` recomputed `_prior_turn_context` + `_should_route_exploration`, but `classify_node` already rewrites the intent to exploration when that predicate fires, so the router's re-check was dead code reading like a live path. **The fix (behaviour-preserving, byte-identical on every fixture)**: (G-1) synthesize writes a single `narrative_substrate` state key on *every* return path — `"news"`/`"fundamental"` (the folded report) on the focused drop, `"prior_answer"` on the narrative-only followup, `None` on every card-bearing path (via the shared `_answer()` helper + the one followup-metric bare-dict return); narrate reads the key and the mirrored predicate block is deleted. (G-2) `classify_node` computes the route once into a `route` state key via a new pure `_classify_route(intent, ambiguity_kind, followup_fires)`; `_classify_router` becomes `state.get("route", "plan")` with no predicate calls; `followup_fires_search` moved into classify (overlaying this turn's fresh `intent`/`needs_*_search` onto state for `RetrievalSpec.fires`); the dead exploration branch removed. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real blocker**: the first cut wrote `narrative_substrate` on only the two `answer=None` paths, leaving it checkpointer-stale on non-drop turns — masked *only* by the incidental fact that every current answer type's `to_markdown()` is non-empty (so narrate's `not payload_markdown` guard short-circuits). Shipping an anti-drift refactor that introduces a new staleness vector is exactly the class this ticket exists to kill, so the fix writes the key fresh on all 26 return paths (regression `test_card_bearing_path_clears_narrative_substrate` pins a card-bearing path clears it); the second review pass returned SHIP. One non-blocking discovery: removing the `partial()` wrapper on the router exposed its annotations to LangGraph's build-time `get_type_hints`, raising `NameError: AgentState` (a `TYPE_CHECKING`-only name) — fixed by spelling the router's hint `graph.AgentState` (the runtime-imported module), the only graph callable registered directly rather than via a deps-bound partial. AC1/AC2/AC3 code (pinned by `test_dropped_card_substrate_reads_from_state_key`, `test_no_new_narrow_projection_branch`, `test_card_bearing_path_clears_narrative_substrate`); AC4 dev-execution-verified (`make test` 1606 passed; `pytest tests/agent/` 1028 passed; `routing_yaml` 5 passed). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean. Out of scope per ticket: any behaviour change; G-4 turn-boundary state reset (separate ticket).
- [x] Graph flow: classify owns the turn boundary — explicit scratch-vs-durable state reset (v3 G-4) — QNT-323
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 graph-flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, finding G-4) — the same "convention distributed across nodes, enforced by comments" smell as G-1/G-2, but for checkpointer state lifetime. The `SqliteSaver` persists `AgentState` across turns on a warm thread, so any key a node leaves unwritten hydrates with the PRIOR turn's value. Which keys are per-turn scratch (must clear at the boundary) vs durable thread memory (`messages`, `prior_answer`, hydrated `reports` on followup) was a convention scattered across node return dicts: `plan_node`'s followup branch had to return ONLY `{"plan": []}` or it clobbered the hydrated reports; its conversational/no-tools branches had to spell out the empty resets or a warm thread's stale reports leaked into a fresh turn; `gather_node` + `explore_supervisor_node` repeated the dance per branch. The next node someone adds could break followup or leak stale scratch with an innocent return dict, and nothing fails until a warm-thread integration test happens to cover that path. **The fix**: `classify_node` (already the turn-boundary node — it resets `intent_path` via `_wrap_path`, snapshots `prior_answer`, appends the user message) now owns the WHOLE reset via `_turn_boundary_reset(intent)`, a single function declared as data next to `AgentState` (`_SCRATCH_RESET_BASE` + `SCRATCH_RESET_KEYS`). It clears every per-turn scratch key (`plan`/`plan_rationale`/`errors`/`reports_by_ticker`/`comparison_tickers`/`retrieved_sources`/`confidence`/`grounding_*`/`supervisor_iterations`/`comparison_rag_demand`, plus `reports` for non-followup intents) and preserves the durable set; `reports` is the one intent-conditional member (durable on followup, scratch otherwise). Downstream nodes drop their defensive resets/omissions and carry only keys they produce. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on two real leaks of the exact class the ticket eliminates**: the first cut omitted `plan_rationale` (only plan/explore write it; plan's followup branch returns only `{"plan": []}`, so a warm-thread followup fed the prior turn's rationale into `build_narrate_prompt`, which reads it unconditionally) and `supervisor_iterations` (only explore writes it; the SSE `done` event reports it every turn, leaking a stale count after any exploration turn). Fixed by adding both to the scratch set (and auditing all remaining `AgentState` keys — every other is already reset, written every turn, intentionally durable, or reset structurally via `_wrap_path`); pinned by `test_single_writer_scratch_keys_cleared_on_warm_thread`. One advisory swept (plan's conversational/no-tools branches simplified to `{"plan": []}`). AC1 code (single `_turn_boundary_reset`; nodes carry only produced keys); AC2 code (meta-test `test_no_node_resets_a_scratch_key_it_does_not_populate` — AST-walks every non-classify node's return dicts + a coverage guard that fails if a new node is added unchecked); AC3 dev-execution-verified (checkpointer round-trips: followup reuses prior reports with 0 tool calls; a fresh quick_fact on a warm comparison thread sees `reports_by_ticker=={}`/`comparison_tickers==[]`/`retrieved_sources==[]`). A side benefit: exploration previously merged prior-turn `reports` on a warm thread (it reads `state.get("reports")` and bypasses plan/gather resets) — classify's reset now clears it. Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1617 passed. Out of scope per ticket: any behaviour change beyond stopping cross-turn scratch leakage.
- [x] Retrieval query is first-class on every classify path (v3 G-10/G-11) — QNT-322
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, items G-10 + G-11) — a path asymmetry left by QNT-289's contextual RAG query rewrite, which protected only the `llm` classify path. **G-11**: the `heuristic` short-circuit (and the `fallback` path) always returned `search_query=""`, so when a keyword floor fired there (e.g. a followup-heuristic turn plus a "buyback" floor token) Qdrant received the raw elliptical question instead of a clean query. **G-10**: `sanitize_search_query` rejected ANY 2-5-uppercase ticker-shaped token outside `TICKERS`/the acronym list as a hallucination — so a legitimate user-supplied competitor (SK, TSMC, ASML) killed the whole rewrite, the exact warm-thread ellipsis loss case QNT-289 was built for (the entity lives only in history, the rewrite is the sole string that names it, and the raw-question fallback loses the topic). **The fix**: (G-10) the guard now rejects a ticker-shaped token only when it appears in NEITHER the raw question NOR the history string rendered to the classifier (`_token_in_context`, word-boundary + case-insensitive) — a competitor named anywhere in the thread survives, an invented token still dies; length cap unchanged. `sanitize_search_query` gained `question`/`history_text` kwargs, threaded from the LLM path (reusing the exact `_render_history_for_classifier` output the model saw). (G-11) new `_floor_search_query` composes a deterministic `ticker + matched-floor-token` query (the ticker from `extract_tickers`, the topic from the news/earnings token or the `_specific_news_qualifier_phrase` refactored out of the old bool helper) and is wired into ALL three no-LLM return points (heuristic + both fallbacks — the defect was symmetric, per the title, though Scope named only the heuristic). The composed query is non-empty IFF `_is_targeted_news`/`_is_earnings_search` is True (verified algebraically identical terms), so a caller can never emit a query while reporting both flags False; no LLM call added. **Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blockers**; two advisories patched inline pre-merge: (1) `_floor_search_query` skipped the tool-side `_QUERY_MAX_LEN` cap — a pathological punctuation-free qualifier run could push the composed string past 512 and silently degrade `search_news`/`search_earnings` to `"[]"` instead of the raw-question fallback; guarded with the same cap, pinned by `test_floor_search_query_over_length_cap_returns_empty`. (2) the G-10 docstring said "user-supplied" but `history_text` includes assistant turns (the new golden fixture relies on the entity being in the *assistant's* prior message) — reworded to "named anywhere in the thread". AC1 code (context-aware guard both directions — pinned by `test_sanitize_keeps_user_supplied_entity_named_in_the_question`/`_in_history` + `test_sanitize_rejects_invented_entity_absent_from_question_and_history` + `test_sanitize_without_context_preserves_rejection`); AC2 code (heuristic+floor → ticker+topic, empty only when no floor — pinned by `test_heuristic_path_composes_ticker_plus_floor_topic`/`_without_ticker`/`_empty_query_when_no_floor_fires` + `test_fallback_path_composes_floor_query`); AC3 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API): `python -m agent.evals.search_query_eval --retrieval` → warm-thread rewritten hit-rate 13/13 (100%) vs raw 10/13 (77%), 0 regressions, the new uppercase-entity ellipsis fixture `nvda-sk-hynix-ellipsis` (SK Hynix in the assistant turn only) query=ok/hits=5, cold_targeted all raw=5/rewritten=5 unchanged, elliptical query accuracy 78% ≥ 70% floor → `is_failing`=False. Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1625 passed. Out of scope per ticket: query rewriting itself (QNT-289), the per-ticker comparison RAG fold (QNT-326 G-14 demand signal owns it), changing WHICH intents fire retrieval.
- [x] Followup substrate: prior_answer generalized beyond Thesis to any analytical card (v3 G-5) — QNT-324
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, item G-5) — QNT-307 deliberately scoped the classify `prior_answer` snapshot to a Thesis only, reproducing the retired legacy slot's lifetime exactly. That cut was the main product gap in the flow: "which of those two looks stronger?" after a comparison, or "so what's the takeaway?" after an exploration scan, followed up over hydrated reports only — the card the user is literally pointing at was invisible to the followup prompt. **The fix (scope)**: (AC1) `ANALYTICAL_ANSWER_TYPES` (a tuple in `answer.py`, re-exported via `graph`) drives the classify snapshot — `isinstance(hydrated_answer, graph.ANALYTICAL_ANSWER_TYPES)` carries any of the 5 analytical shapes (Thesis / Comparison / LeanComparison / Focused / Exploration) across the turn boundary; `ConversationalAnswer` and `QuickFactAnswer` map to None (chit-chat is never substrate; a followup's own compact card is not a full analysis — this keeps the pre-existing "followup after a quick_fact turn carries no prior card" behaviour). (AC2) `build_followup_prompt` renames `prior_thesis`→`prior_answer` and renders the card under a **shape-labelled** heading ("your earlier comparison/focused analysis/exploration scan on this ticker") via a class-name→label map kept local to the schema-light prompts module. **The fix (grounding — surfaced during AC3 eval validation, beyond the ticket's stated "narrate needs no change")**: feeding a *comparison* card into a followup exposed a real grounding-check false positive — a comparison's second-ticker figures live in `reports_by_ticker`, which the turn-boundary reset (QNT-323) clears, so a followup faithfully re-quoting the card was flagged by the deterministic numeric checker as hallucinated (`non_hallucination` 0.0, composite 0.54). Fixed at the pattern level: `_runtime_report_texts` now folds the prior card's `to_markdown()` into the grounding substrate when `intent == "followup"` (the card was numerically grounded when produced); narrate's runtime check + both eval `_flatten_reports` copies (`dialogue_eval` + the `eval_scores` online-trace scorer) delegate to the one canonical assembler so runtime and offline checks agree. The fold is strictly additive to the supported-number set, so it provably cannot regress any fixture's non-hallucination score, and a followup inventing a number absent from card + reports is still flagged (pinned by `test_followup_fold_still_flags_invented_numbers`). **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on the grounding fold's masking risk** (no test proved it wasn't a blanket bypass) — addressed with the invented-number guard test above; its AC3 "missing evidence" blocker was a false positive (the agent sees only the diff, not the session's live eval receipts). AC1 code (pinned by `test_classify_snapshots_analytical_shape` (5 shapes) + `test_classify_drops_conversational_answer` + `test_classify_drops_quick_fact_answer` + narrative-only preservation); AC2 code (pinned by `test_followup_prompt_carries_prior_card` (5 shapes) + omits-when-none); AC3 dev-execution-verified live (tunnel + LiteLLM + API up): `python -m agent.evals.dialogue_eval --only <fixture>` → NEW `nvda-compare-then-stronger` [0.910] clean non_hallucination 1.00, NEW `tsla-explore-then-takeaway` [0.860] clean non_hallucination 0.95, existing `aapl-thesis-retail-followup` [0.910] / `tsla-technical-why` [0.600] unchanged and clean. Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1646 passed. Out of scope per ticket: any change to WHICH intents route followup, the per-ticker comparison RAG fold (QNT-326 G-14 demand signal owns it).
- [x] History-aware comparison ticker resolution (v3 G-12) — QNT-325
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, item G-12) — comparison resolution was history-blind while the QNT-289 search-query path already resolved ellipses from transcript, so the two resolution paths had diverged. `_detect_ambiguity` returned `needs_second_ticker` unconditionally when the question named no ticker, and `_resolve_comparison_tickers` read only the question + URL-context ticker — so a warm thread that just discussed NVDA and AMD, asked "now compare those two", got a clarify card for a question the transcript answers verbatim. **The fix (deterministic, no LLM)**: `_history_tickers` extracts the most-recent distinct tickers the USER named across recent transcript turns (newest first, user turns only so assistant valuation colour — "AMD trades at a discount to NVDA" — can't seed a false pairing); `_resolve_comparison_tickers` gained a `history` arg and fills the gap from it only when the question names <2 tickers (question-named > URL-context > history-fill priority, deduped, cap-at-2 early exit). The ambiguity gate now DELEGATES its comparison decision to the resolver (`len(resolved) < _MIN`), so gate and plan can never disagree — a warm two-ticker thread defers and proceeds; a cold "compare them" or a warm one-ticker thread still clarifies. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real blocker**: gate and plan re-derived history independently and diverged at the `HISTORY_TURN_LIMIT` boundary — classify computes the gate's history BEFORE appending the current user turn, then its return appends-and-re-trims `state["messages"]` to the 20-message cap, dropping the OLDEST turn; plan then re-derived from that window-shifted list and could see a shorter window than the gate (defer, then redirect on <2). **The fix**: `classify_node` resolves the pair ONCE from its pre-append `history` and forwards it via `state["comparison_tickers"]` (a shared `context_primary` local feeds the SAME `primary` to the gate call and the forwarding call); `plan_node` consumes it verbatim (keeping its `>_MAX_COMPARISON_TICKERS` redirect guard) instead of re-deriving. Regression `test_gate_and_plan_agree_at_history_cap_boundary` pads the transcript to exactly 20 messages and confirms the shifted-history re-derive would have seen only AMD, but forwarding preserves NVDA+AMD; second review pass returned SHIP (one advisory — gate/forwarding `primary` call-site asymmetry — swept inline via the shared `context_primary`). AC1 code (fill-only-when-short, most-recent-wins, dedupe — pinned by `test_resolver_fills_pair_from_history_gesture`/`_history_most_recent_wins`/`_dedupes_history_against_named`/`_ignores_history_when_two_named` + `test_history_tickers_ignores_assistant_only_ticker`); AC2 code (gate defers on resolved pair; cold + warm-one-ticker still clarify — pinned by `test_gate_defers_when_history_resolves_pair`/`_clarifies_cold_compare_them`/`_clarifies_warm_one_ticker_thread`); AC3 dev-execution-verified (real `classify_node`→`plan_node`: `uv run pytest tests/agent/test_history_comparison.py` → 14 passed, incl. warm-two-ticker→{NVDA,AMD} routes to plan + warm-one-ticker→clarify + the cap boundary). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1658 passed. Out of scope per ticket: the per-ticker comparison RAG fold (QNT-326 G-14 demand signal owns it), any change to WHICH intents route comparison.
- [x] Spike: fold thesis plan pick into the classify call — thesis 4→3 LLM calls (v3 G-6) — QNT-327
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-06 flow review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, item G-6) — the thesis path was four sequential LLM calls (classify → thesis-plan → synthesize → narrate), where classify and thesis-plan are back-to-back small structured calls to the same alias, costing one full proxy round trip on 100% of LLM-path thesis turns. `IntentDecision` had already absorbed orthogonal fields three times (QNT-222/263/280/289), so the precedent + guardrail pattern existed; the counter-pressure was a fatter schema degrading intent accuracy on the 20b model. Framed as an experiment, not a commitment (ADR-007), with a measured decline a valid outcome (ADR-021). **The fix (behind the ThesisPlan fallback)**: optional `report_picks` + `plan_rationale` on `IntentDecision`, produced ONLY for a `thesis` intent (double-gated: prompt instruction + `if decision.intent == "thesis"` in `classify_intent_with_source`, whose return grew 5→7-tuple, ~40 test stubs + 3 eval unpack sites rippled). `classify_node` forwards them via new per-turn-scratch state keys `folded_report_picks`/`folded_plan_rationale` (added to `_SCRATCH_RESET_BASE` so a warm-thread heuristic turn can't inherit prior picks; classify is the sole writer); `plan_node`'s thesis branch consumes them via new `support._tools_from_folded_picks` (filters to available, forces `company`, returns `None` on any <2-tool result → signals fallback) and SKIPS the dedicated `ThesisPlan` call when valid. Every other path (heuristic/fallback classify, non-thesis intent, empty/degenerate pick) runs the standalone planner unchanged, so correctness is preserved on every path — only plan QUALITY on thesis turns was at risk, which the eval gates. New instrument `agent.evals.plan_fold_eval` scores folded-vs-planner agreement (`AGREEMENT_FLOOR = 0.80`). **Decision: SHIP (measured favourably, not declined).** **AC2 measured live (2026-07-07, LiteLLM up, clean window, no contamination)**: `routing_eval` 26/26 (100%) on both `main` (5-field) and branch (7-field) — intent accuracy unchanged, 2 label drifts changed no routed corpus (small-model variance); `plan_fold_eval` 9/9 (100%) agreement (1 golden LLM-path-thesis fixture + an 8-ticker open-ended-thesis probe, since the golden set is thin on LLM-path thesis), every case folded==planner==all-four-reports; a live thesis turn (`qnt327-fold-thesis-trace`) counted exactly 3 LLM round-trips (classify→synthesize→narrate) with plan logging "skipped ThesisPlan call". **Both reviewers returned SHIP, no blockers**; one advisory addressed — a post-classify intent override (comparison/exploration reroute) can leave picks in state alongside a non-thesis intent, inert today but pinned by `test_non_thesis_intent_ignores_folded_picks_in_state`. **Surfaced + fixed a latent test-isolation gap**: `test_synthesize_node_invokes_llm_with_system_message` patched only `graph.get_llm`, not `intent.get_llm`, so its LLM-path question let classify escape to the live proxy — harmless before this ticket, but with picks now foldable a reachable proxy made classify fill `report_picks` → plan skipped the `ThesisPlan` call the test asserts; pinned to a heuristic-thesis phrasing so classify stays off the network. AC1 code (pinned by `test_folded_picks_consumed_and_skip_the_planner_call`/`_empty_folded_picks_falls_back_to_the_planner`/`_degenerate_folded_picks_fall_back_to_the_planner`/`_tools_from_folded_picks_filters_forces_company_and_signals_fallback`/`_non_thesis_intent_ignores_folded_picks_in_state` + 3 `test_intent.py` fold tests); AC2 dev-execution-verified live; AC3 docs (v3 doc G-6 marked SHIPPED with the numbers + caveats — gitignored personal doc; new eval documented in `evals/README.md` entry (g2)). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1667 passed. **Caveats (in the v3 doc)**: the fold only activates on the LLM classify path — thesis asks carrying an explicit token ("thesis"/"should I buy"/"bull case") short-circuit the heuristic and were already 3 calls, so the 4→3 saving lands only on open-ended thesis asks; agreement is ~trivially high because thesis skews full-picture (both resolvers pick all four), a latent simplification (a constant four-report thesis plan could replace both the planner call and the fold) noted for future hygiene. Out of scope per ticket: shipping without eval parity.
- [x] Turn-boundary reset: interludes and followup preserve thread substrate (v3 R-1/R-2) — QNT-349
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08 post-ship reassessment (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, findings R-1/R-2) — a re-read of the eight shipped v3 tickets hunting for interactions *between* the new pieces. Shared root cause: QNT-323's turn-boundary reset treats every turn as an analytical turn, but conversational and clarify turns are non-analytical INTERLUDES that pre-QNT-323 preserved thread state by omission (their routes skip plan/gather, which carried the only resets). **R-1 (user-visible regression)**: `_turn_boundary_reset(intent)` cleared `reports` for every intent except followup, so a conversational ("hi", route=synthesize) or clarify (route=clarify) interlude wiped `reports` and nothing repopulated them — a subsequent followup ("tell me more") then saw empty reports AND `prior_answer` None (pre-existing QNT-307 semantics) and fired synthesize's no-context redirect ("I don't have a prior turn on this thread to follow up on"), factually wrong with the transcript right there. The suite was green because no fixture ran a 3-turn thread with an interlude in the middle. **R-2 (advisory)**: `reports_by_ticker` was an always-reset `_SCRATCH_RESET_BASE` member with no followup exception, so once QNT-324 made the prior ComparisonAnswer (both tickers' numbers) the followup narrate substrate, a comparison→followup grounded the second ticker's figures against the PRIMARY ticker's `reports` only → false-flagged as unsupported, dipping grounding_rate / the confidence chip and polluting grounding_unsupported. Both tickets individually correct; the interaction is the bug. **The fix (one file, `graph.py`)**: `reports` + `reports_by_ticker` moved into a new `_SCRATCH_RESET_SUBSTRATE` (the durable thread substrate); `_turn_boundary_reset(intent, route)` clears them only when `not _preserves_thread_substrate(intent, route)`, where the predicate is `intent == "followup" OR route in {clarify, synthesize}` — the route arm covers the interludes, the followup arm covers a followup that fires a targeted RAG search (route=plan, not short-circuit). `SCRATCH_RESET_KEYS` reproduces the identical scratch set (base ∪ substrate) so the QNT-323 meta-test is unaffected; `comparison_tickers` stays always-reset (classify overwrites it every turn, no followup path reads it). `classify_node` passes the resolved `route`. **Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blockers**; two advisories: (1) `prior_answer` (the analytical CARD, a separate channel) is still nulled across a ConversationalAnswer interlude by pre-existing QNT-307 semantics — the ticket's explicit Out-of-scope, surfaced as a fast-follow candidate; (2) the R-1 fixtures use canned stub output so they pin structural claims (no redirect, `reports` preserved, zero re-fetch) not content grounding — patched inline with a scope note in the fixture docstring. All 4 new fixtures confirmed to FAIL on `main` with the exact regression signatures (interludes → no-context redirect; R-2 → `unsupported: 180`, grounding_rate 0.67) and pass after — genuine regression tests, not tautologies. AC1 code (route-derived reset — pinned by `_preserves_thread_substrate`/`_turn_boundary_reset`); AC2 code (3-turn fixtures — pinned by `test_conversational_interlude_then_followup_reaches_prior_reports[narrative-only|metric-ask]` + `test_clarify_interlude_then_followup_reaches_prior_reports`; existing 2-turn fixtures unchanged); AC3 code (`test_comparison_followup_grounds_against_full_bundle` — grounding_rate 1.0, `180` not in grounding_unsupported); AC4 dev-execution-verified (`uv run pytest tests/agent/ -m "not integration and not deepeval"` → 1079 passed; `tests/agent/test_turn_boundary.py` → 15 passed); AC5 docs (v3 doc R-1/R-2 marked SHIPPED — gitignored personal doc). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1672 passed. Out of scope per ticket: whether interludes should also preserve `prior_answer` (pre-existing QNT-307 semantics, a deliberate product call for a later ticket).
- [x] Prompt-layer hygiene: comparison disclosure alias miss + hardcoded ticker list + narrate prior-card label (v3 P-1/P-2/P-3) — QNT-350
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08 logic-layer review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v3.md`, findings P-1/P-2/P-3) — the first end-to-end read of `prompts/system.py`. The layer held up (injection defenses, constant-synced Rn anchor rules, eval-scoped falsifier); three small defects in one file were bundled per one-feature-one-ticket. **P-1 (user-visible)**: `build_comparison_prompt`'s "which tickers did the user name" check used an uppercase-symbol regex while upstream `extract_tickers` resolves company-name aliases — "compare nvidia and amd" resolved to [NVDA, AMD] but the regex saw only AMD, so the prompt falsely instructed the model to disclose NVDA "came from the current page or thread context" and that spurious sentence landed in the rendered differences paragraph. **The fix**: swap the regex for alias-aware `extract_tickers(question)` membership (function-local import to break the real `agent.intent → agent.prompts → .system` cycle); dead `import re` removed. **P-2 (drift)**: `CONVERSATIONAL_SYSTEM_PROMPT` hardcoded the ten covered tickers as prose (the exact hardcoding CLAUDE.md forbids and the ticker-lifecycle guide sweeps for) and the capability copy said "four answer shapes", omitting exploration (a real user-reachable shape). **The fix**: derive the covered-ticker sentence from `shared.tickers.TICKERS` at module load (prompt-version hash already fingerprints it), test-pinned to the registry; enumerate "five answer shapes" incl. exploration. **P-3 (mislabel)**: `build_narrate_prompt`'s prior-turn heading hardcoded "your earlier thesis" while QNT-324 generalized `prior_answer` to any analytical shape — a followup over a prior comparison fed the narrator a comparison card labeled thesis. **The fix**: extract the `_PRIOR_ANSWER_LABEL` lookup into a shared `_prior_answer_label` helper (also used by `build_followup_prompt`); `build_narrate_prompt` gains a `prior_answer` object param (label-only) and the narrate node forwards the hydrated card; a bare prior markdown with no card falls back to "thesis" (back-compat preserved). **Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blockers**; one advisory fixed inline — the "suggestions" field guidance three lines below the P-2 fix still hardcoded "ten covered tickers" and listed shapes without exploration (same drift class), swept by dropping the count and adding exploration. AC1 code (alias membership — pinned by `test_comparison_prompt_no_disclosure_when_alias_names_both_tickers` + `test_comparison_prompt_discloses_genuinely_context_filled_ticker`; existing "compare to AAPL" disclosure test unaffected); AC2 code (registry-derived list + exploration — pinned by `test_conversational_prompt_ticker_list_derives_from_registry` + `test_conversational_prompt_names_exploration_shape`); AC3 code (shape-labelled narrate heading — pinned by `test_narrate_prior_block_names_prior_card_shape` (4-shape parametrize incl. ComparisonAnswer) + fallback case); AC4 dev-execution-verified (`make test` → 1687 passed, 53 deselected, 1 xfailed; prompt-text-only, hash auto-computed so no manual bump, no golden-sweep — served tokens/behaviour unchanged). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean. Out of scope per ticket: building the per-ticker comparison RAG fold; any behaviour change beyond the three prose/label fixes.
- [x] Agent latency: deepseek-first provider pin, strict json_schema enforcement, synthesize verbosity cap — QNT-351
    - **Triggered by**: a 2026-07-08 Langfuse investigation into why the QNT-258 flip to OpenRouter DeepSeek V4 Flash quadrupled per-call latency (default-alias p50 1.1s→4.3s, p90 6.1s→13.1s vs the stable Groq weeks). The gap decomposed into slow decode, verbosity growth, tripled TTFT, and — the crux — the **QNT-318/ADR-027 prefix cache was not landing in prod** (27 of 33 structured calls `input_cache_read=0`; the only hits were back-to-back bursts). **The premise was wrong, not just under-realized**: OpenRouter endpoint metadata (`supports_implicit_caching`) reports FALSE for Novita and every pinned provider **except first-party DeepSeek (TRUE)** — a byte-identical back-to-back probe on Novita/others returned `cached_tokens=0` AND `cache_write_tokens=0`, so ADR-027's "Novita 100% warm" reading was a back-to-back burst artifact that never persists across organic minutes-to-hours gaps. **The corrected-assumption crux (surfaced mid-implementation, paused for a user decision)**: the ticket assumed the per-alias `data_collection: allow` already accepted in ADR-027 made first-party DeepSeek reachable; verified empirically it does NOT — a raw `only:[deepseek]` call 404s (*"No endpoints available matching your guardrail restrictions and data policy. Configure: openrouter.ai/settings/privacy"*) behind an **account-level** guardrail, and letting it fall back served a non-DeepSeek provider at `cached=0`. Reaching first-party DeepSeek required relaxing the OpenRouter **account privacy setting** (user decision, 2026-07-08), which **reverses ADR-027's explicitly-rejected "relax the account-level data policy" alternative** and widens routing eligibility account-wide (incl. the DeepEval judge). **The fix (config + smoke + ADR, `litellm_config.yaml`)**: (AC1) reordered the `equity-agent/default` provider pin to `deepseek → baidu → alibaba → novita → gmicloud → deepinfra` — DeepSeek leads as the only implicit-caching endpoint (p50 71 tok/s, 99.90% uptime, cache reads `0.0028/M ≈ 0.02× input`), the rest re-derived from live `throughput_last_30m`/uptime/price/quant (baidu fastest+cheapest reachable, deepinfra last as p50 17 fp4); (AC2) added `require_parameters: true` so OpenRouter routes only to endpoints that honour the request's `response_format`/`json_schema`; (AC5) `max_tokens: 1500` on the alias caps synthesize verbosity (payload median grew ~410→920 post-flip, range 390–2430; 1500 sits above the normal ceiling so normal payloads + narrate ~197 are untouched and the 1500–2430 slow-decode tail is cut — a truncated structured payload fail-closes via `_structured_call`, bounded blast radius, inherited harmlessly by the tiny small-alias fallback). **Receipts (`scripts/smoke_deepseek_cache_schema.py`, new)**: AC3 cache smoke — direct `only:[deepseek]` call 2 `cached=1536/1618` (cost $0.000227→$0.0000161, ~14× cheaper); proxy synthesize smoke call 2 `cached_tokens=4096/4893` → PASS. AC4 strict json_schema smoke — clarify + conversational shapes under `method="json_schema", strict=True`: **0/8 prose escapes** → strict enforcement holds, so reverting the QNT-258 `function_calling` workaround becomes a follow-up candidate (kept out of scope; needs its own per-shape receipts). (AC7) ADR-027 amended: Novita-premise reversal, new order, account-privacy reversal + a drift-watch note (the privacy toggle is non-declarative external state — AC6's post-deploy Langfuse check is the current detector, a standing cache-hit/fallback-rate alert the durable follow-up), strict-schema receipt, economics superseded to the ~0.02× DeepSeek figure. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST**; both blockers were ship-time PR-body / infra-template-AC responsibilities (raw AC3 receipt in the PR + CD-green/no-drift gates), not diff defects — carried into ship. Two advisories fixed (config comment discloses the small-alias fallback cap inheritance; ADR gains the drift-watch note); one left (adding `require_parameters` to QNT-319's smoke is that ticket's scope). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1687 passed. Out of scope per ticket: reverting the `function_calling` workaround (this ticket only produces the enforcement smoke that would justify it), changing the primary model or the Nemotron anchor (ADR-025 stands). AC6 (post-deploy Langfuse p50 + cache-hit rate vs the 07-04..08 baseline) is a prod-execution follow-up over a real traffic window.
- [x] Report confidence honesty: wire the freshness factor + surface fetch failures in the prompt — QNT-355
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08/09 report-pipeline audit (`docs/report-improvement-v1.md`, items H-1/H-2) — the composite confidence number was less honest than it looked. **H-1**: `_composite_confidence` multiplies `coverage × grounding × freshness` but hardcoded `freshness=1.0` with a docstring deferring "until report templates expose a uniform as-of date" — a precondition QNT-299 already met (every report ends in a machine-parseable `AS_OF: YYYY-MM-DD` footer whose own docstring names "the agent's freshness read" as the intended consumer), yet nothing folded it into confidence, so a 45-day-old fundamental scored identically to fresh data. **H-2**: `gather` moves tool `[error]` results into `state["errors"]`, but `_build_user_message` rendered only the supplied-reports line, so the LLM wrote "Not fetched for this question" for an aspect whose fetch actually *failed* — the user couldn't tell "chose not to look" from "the fetch broke" — and the `tools.py` module docstring falsely claimed the `[error]` string reached the synthesize prompt. **The fix (agent-only)**: (AC1) new `parse_as_of` owns the AS_OF regex; `_freshness_factor` applies a per-report-type decay (neutral within a 5-day cadence for technical/news, ~100-day for fundamental/company, then reciprocal `horizon/age` beyond it); `_reports_freshness` takes the STALEST gathered report as the cap (mirrors the SSE `data_as_of` oldest-date rule), folded into `_composite_confidence` at both the narrate tail and `_quick_fact_grounding`. (AC2) `_build_user_message` gains an `errors` param rendering a `Failed to fetch: <name>` line when non-empty (threaded through `build_synthesis_prompt`/`build_quick_fact_prompt` + `synthesize_node`), and both `SYSTEM_PROMPT`/`QUICK_FACT_SYSTEM_PROMPT` gained a rule to name a listed report as "unavailable this turn" instead of "not fetched". (AC4) stale docstrings in `graph.py` + `tools.py` fixed; H-1/H-2 marked SHIPPED in the gitignored working doc. **Correcting the ticket's H-1 premise**: it said the AS_OF footer is consumed by "nothing", but `agent_chat.py` already parsed it (`_AS_OF_PATTERN`/`_extract_data_as_of`) for the SSE `data_as_of` chip — so to honour AC1's "exactly two AS_OF readers" I did NOT add a third parser; I consolidated the regex into the shared `agent.graph.parse_as_of` and repointed the SSE layer to import it (net: one writer `formatters.format_as_of_footer` + one reader `graph.parse_as_of`, grep-verified). **Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no blockers**; one advisory fixed inline — `parse_as_of`'s `date.fromisoformat` was unguarded, so a pattern-matching-but-calendar-invalid footer (`2026-13-45`) would raise `ValueError` uncaught in the narrate freshness tail and the SSE `done` generator (new risk from the consolidation — the old raw-string capture never parsed); made total with `try/except ValueError → None`, pinned by a test. Second advisory recorded as an AC-bounded scope cut at ship time — the failed-fetch line covered thesis + quick_fact (the two intents using `_build_user_message`), not comparison/exploration (distinct prompt builders; comparison's per-ticker `{ticker}.{name}` error keys are their own rendering) or followup (stale carried-over `errors`) — then **folded in via the PR #511 follow-up below**. AC1/AC2 code (pinned by `test_reports_freshness_*`, `test_parse_as_of_reads_trailing_footer_only`, `test_build_synthesis_prompt_renders_failed_fetch_line`, `test_system_prompt_instructs_naming_the_failed_report`); AC3 dev-execution-verified (`test_backdated_reports_lower_composite_confidence_vs_fresh` + `test_required_tool_failure_reaches_synthesize_prompt` → backdated 400-day fundamental yields composite confidence < fresh; a failing required `fundamental` tool lands in `errors` and reaches the synthesize prompt as `Failed to fetch: fundamental`); AC4 docs. Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1699 passed. Out of scope per ticket: freshness-based re-planning/refetching (this only makes the score + narrative honest); report template changes (QNT-353/354). **Follow-up (PR #511, merged 2026-07-09, commit 7b736771)**: the failed-fetch line was extended to the two remaining report-consuming intents — exploration (bare error names, reuses the extracted `_failed_fetch_line`) and comparison (`{ticker}.{name}` keys grouped per ticker by `_failed_fetch_by_ticker`, rendered inside each ticker's reports block), with matching `EXPLORATION_SYSTEM_PROMPT`/`COMPARISON_SYSTEM_PROMPT` rules; followup stays excluded (stale carried-over `errors`).
- [x] Fundamental report: absolute SCALE block + margin-bps trajectory lines — QNT-354
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08/09 report-pipeline audit (`docs/report-improvement-v1.md`, items C-3/C-4/C-11) — the fundamental report rendered 100% ratios/percentages with no absolute scale numbers anywhere in the corpus, even though migrations 018-023 had shipped the columns and the Dagster asset populated them: they never reached `_RATIO_COLUMNS` in `api/templates/fundamental.py`. **C-4**: "what is NVDA's revenue / market cap" — among the most natural quick_fact asks — returned "not available in the supplied reports", and every thesis lacked size framing. **C-3**: the margin-trajectory phrasing the prompts push for ("net margin expanded 120 bps YoY") was impossible because the LLM is forbidden from subtracting the two percentages it can see (ADR-003), while the pre-computed `gross/net_margin_bps_yoy` sat unrendered. **C-11 (docstring half)**: `get_fundamental_report`'s docstring promised "earnings surprises" the report has never contained. **The fix (pure template + `_RATIO_COLUMNS` widening, no migration)**: (AC1) a `## SCALE` block rendered once at the top via `_scale_lines`, printing absolute revenue/net income/FCF from the latest TTM row's `revenue_ttm`/`net_income_ttm`/`fcf_ttm` (the only period_type carrying them) + market cap, all through the existing `format_currency` (`precision=0`); (AC2) `_margin_line` gained a `bps_yoy` param appending `; +120 bps YoY` to the gross/net PROFITABILITY lines (quarterly+annual only — the asset's emit scope), and a conditional EBITDA-margin line on TTM sections where `ebitda_margin_pct` is present; (AC3) the docstring rewritten to "valuation multiples, growth, margins, and absolute scale". **Corrected the ticket's "pure template" premise**: `market_cap` is NOT a `fundamental_summary` column (that table holds ratios + TTM absolutes only) — it lives in `equity_raw.fundamentals`, so the SCALE block needed one small extra parameterized query (`_fetch_market_cap`, newest `period_end`) alongside the widened summary fetch; kept within the template layer, no migration. **Both reviewers (own pass + `code-reviewer-ediff`) returned SHIP, no code blockers**; two advisories fixed inline — (1) `equity_raw.fundamentals.market_cap` is non-nullable and defaults to `0.0` when yfinance omits `marketCap`, and `format_currency` treats only None/NaN as missing, so a 0-sentinel would render a misleading "$0"; guarded to N/M per the formatters.py convention (pinned by `test_fundamental_scale_market_cap_zero_sentinel_renders_nm`); (2) added an invariant-lock assertion that the TTM PROFITABILITY section carries no `bps YoY` suffix. Two advisories left as noted tradeoffs — SCALE's market cap uses the raw stored snapshot (the ticket's specified source) which can drift from the `close×shares` market cap implied by the multiples (out of "pure template" scope), and `format_currency` on a negative net income prints `$-…` (cosmetic, shared formatter). AC1/AC2 code (pinned by `test_fundamental_scale_block_renders_absolute_figures`/`_nm_without_ttm_or_market_cap`/`_market_cap_zero_sentinel_renders_nm`, `test_fundamental_profitability_carries_bps_yoy_suffix`, `test_fundamental_ttm_section_renders_ebitda_margin`); AC3 code (`tools.py` docstring); AC4 dev-execution-verified — live curl of `/api/v1/reports/fundamental/NVDA` (tunnel + local uvicorn) rendered the SCALE block with cited values (Revenue $253,491,000,000 / Net income $159,613,000,000 / FCF $119,076,000,000 / Market cap $4,718,977,351,680), QUARTERLY/ANNUAL bps-YoY suffixes (`+2885 bps YoY`, `-392 bps YoY`), and the TTM EBITDA-margin line (`65.3%`); AAPL cross-checked; durable eval artifacts `nvda-quickfact-revenue` + `nvda-quickfact-market-cap` goldens added; AC5 docs (report-improvement-v1.md C-3/C-4 marked SHIPPED, C-11 docstring half ticked — gitignored personal doc). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1710 passed. Out of scope per ticket: estimates/surprises + dividends/buybacks ingestion (gated on trace demand); technical + news templates (QNT-353/356).
- [x] Forward calendar: next-earnings-date ingest + report line for dated catalysts — QNT-357
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08/09 report-pipeline audit (`docs/report-improvement-v1.md`, item C-10) — no table held any dated future event, and `EXPLORATION_SYSTEM_PROMPT` rule 4 explicitly forbade "watch next week" items *because* "the reports carry no dated catalysts" (a self-acknowledged hole), so "what should I watch" answers could not name the one real upcoming catalyst every analyst leads with. This is the single report-v1 member that breaks the milestone's "no new ingestion" clause; the milestone description was amended when the ticket was filed (demand is agent analytical quality, not the ingest code's phase). **The fix (new ingest asset + one report line + prompt relax)**: (AC1) new Dagster `earnings_calendar` asset reads `yf.Ticker(t).calendar['Earnings Date']` per ticker (iterates `shared.tickers.TICKERS`, RetryPolicy + 429 handling identical to `ohlcv_raw`/`fundamentals`), keeps the earliest still-future date, and upserts one row per ticker into the new `equity_raw.earnings_calendar` (migration 029, `ReplacingMergeTree(fetched_at)` ORDER BY ticker); a weekly `earnings_calendar_schedule` (Sun 20:00 ET, clear of every sibling schedule's window) + `earnings_calendar_job` wired into `definitions.py`; `EarningsCalendarRow` schema-of-record added (matches the 4 sibling declarative schemas — zero business-logic imports). (AC2) the company report `## CONTEXT NOW` block renders `Next earnings: <ISO>` verbatim (ADR-012) in both `full` and `compact` profiles via a new parameterized `_fetch_next_earnings_date`; rule 4 relaxed from "do not invent a forward calendar" to "only dated events the report states" (the earnings-date line may be cited to the user; inventing anything else still forbidden), prompt test added. (AC3) new asset check `earnings_calendar_date_in_window` bounds the date to `[today, today+120d]` (WARN), not just not-null. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST, one real blocker fixed inline**: `_fetch_next_earnings_date` read the stored date with no `>= today()` guard — because the table refreshes weekly while `today()` advances daily, a just-passed earnings date can sit in the row for up to a poll interval, and serving it verbatim (now citable to the user under the relaxed rule) would assert a *past* date as an upcoming catalyst; added `AND next_earnings_date >= today()` so a stale date degrades to N/A until the next weekly poll (verified live: guarded query returns AAPL's future date, a 2000-01-01 probe filters to count 0). Two advisories left as convention-consistent (`EarningsCalendarRow` "unused" matches all 4 siblings; `PARTITION BY ticker` matches `earnings_releases_raw`). AC1/AC2/AC3 code (pinned by `test_definitions_load`, `test_exploration_prompt_permits_dated_events_the_report_states`, `test_company_context_now_renders_with_data`/`_handles_missing_fundamentals`); AC4 dev-execution-verified — applied migration 029, materialized `earnings_calendar` for all 10 tickers (all RUN_SUCCESS, e.g. AAPL 2026-07-31 / NVDA 2026-08-27), boundary query for rows outside `[today, today+120d]` returned 0, live curl of `/api/v1/reports/company/AAPL` rendered `Next earnings: 2026-07-31` in CONTEXT NOW, and the live exploration eval case `aapl-watch-earnings-date` (real graph + judge) named the catalyst with a citation ("Apple's next major calendar event is its earnings release on 2026-07-31 (source: company)"), numeric_support_ok 1/1; AC5 docs (report-improvement-v1.md C-10 marked SHIPPED, milestone amendment confirmed — gitignored personal doc). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1723 passed. Out of scope per ticket: other calendar events (dividends/splits/conferences) and estimates/surprises ingestion (C-11), both demand-gated.
- [x] Technical report: surface shipped indicators + volume + 52-week range + window returns + trend consensus — QNT-353
- [x] News digest quality: 280-char snippet-budget parity + same-story dedup — QNT-356
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08/09 report-pipeline audit (`docs/report-improvement-v1.md`, items C-8/C-9) — two content-quality gaps in the canned news digest (`api/templates/news.py`). **C-8**: the digest truncated body snippets at 160 chars while folded RAG hits get 280 (`agent/support.py:_NEWS_BODY_MAX_CHARS`, the budget QNT-225 established as what disambiguates an event from a name-drop), so 160 often cut before the catalyst detail. **C-9**: 20 chronological slots with no same-story dedup — several outlets covering one wire story crowd out the window's second story, and coverage breadth is itself a materiality cue an analyst reads as story weight. **The fix**: (AC1) one shared `shared.retrieval.NEWS_BODY_SNIPPET_CHARS = 280`, consumed by both the digest SQL substring and the fold default so they cannot drift silently (pinned by `test_news_snippet_budget_pinned_to_fold`); (AC2) greedy token-Jaccard clustering (`_cluster_rows`) collapses near-duplicate headlines into one representative bullet with an "also covered by N sources" suffix counting distinct other outlets. **The corrected-assumption crux (caught during live AC3 execution)**: the ticket frames dedup as "five outlets covering one story" and keys the suffix on `source`, but `news_raw.source` is the Finnhub *feed label*, not the outlet — `uniqExact(source) = 1` per ticker over 14 days (only `finnhub`/`yahoo_finance`), so a suffix keyed on it would never fire. The real outlet is `news_raw.publisher_name` (Yahoo, Benzinga, SeekingAlpha, CNBC, ChartMill; 5 distinct/ticker, 100% populated), so the digest's outlet identity — bullet tag, breadth suffix, and SOURCES roll-up — was repointed to `publisher_name`. **Design decision**: C-9's benefit is that collapsing dupes "frees slots for the window's second story", so dedup runs over a 60-row fetch pool and renders up to `_MAX_HEADLINES` (20) *distinct* clusters — dedup after the SQL `LIMIT 20` would only shrink the digest, never backfill; rendered bullets stay capped at 20 so prompt cost stays bounded (pinned by `test_news_dedup_frees_slots_for_crowded_out_stories`). **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST, one real blocker fixed inline**: the initial Jaccard threshold 0.6 false-merged *distinct-but-similar* stories — "...Q3 2026 Earnings" vs "...Q4 2026 Earnings" (0.71) and a same-day "shares rise on strong..." vs "shares fall on weak..." reversal (0.60) both cleared 0.6 and would hide a materially different story under an "also covered by" suffix; verified the computation and raised the threshold to 0.8 (syndicated reprints score ~1.0, so no real merges lost; bias to precision over recall — a missed collapse is the benign failure), with adversarial fixtures (`test_news_dedup_keeps_distinct_but_similar_stories_separate`) locking both near-miss pairs apart. **Data reality**: scanned all 10 tickers — zero natural cross-outlet near-dupes in any current top-60 window (the free-tier feed is Yahoo-dominated; same-headline multi-outlet syndication is rare and pushed past the window), so the collapse+suffix behaviour is pinned by unit tests rather than shown live. AC1/AC2 code (5 news tests total); AC3 dev-execution-verified — live curl of `/api/v1/reports/news/MU` (MU = 518 articles/14d; local uvicorn over prod ClickHouse via tunnel) rendered 20 distinct stories with outlet tags + per-outlet SOURCES roll-up (Yahoo: 18, SeekingAlpha: 1, Benzinga: 1) and widened 280-char snippets; per-turn token delta +865 chars ≈ +216 tokens vs the 160-char baseline (9 of 20 snippets exceeded 160, well under the ~2400-char worst case), dedup collapses this window: 0; AC4 docs (report-improvement-v1.md C-8/C-9 marked SHIPPED — gitignored personal doc). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1720 passed. Out of scope per ticket: sentiment/event-type classification (needs a real classifier; demand-gated); the RAG fold path (already at 280 with its own dedup-by-retrieval).
- [x] Technical report: surface shipped indicators + volume + 52-week range + window returns + trend consensus — QNT-353
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-08/09 report-pipeline audit (`docs/report-improvement-v1.md`, items C-1/C-2/C-5/C-6/C-7) — the technical template trailed the warehouse. Migrations 015-017 shipped `sma_200`/`adx_14`/`atr_14`/`bb_pct_b`/`macd_bullish_cross` and the Dagster asset computed them, but `_INDICATOR_COLUMNS` in `api/templates/technical.py` still listed only the original nine; volume was selected and dropped; there was no 52-week range or multi-window return (so "how has AAPL done this year" was unanswerable without breaking ADR-003); and the multi-timeframe trend consensus was majority-rule *counted by the LLM* in two prompts (quasi-arithmetic ADR-012 says belongs in the report body). **The fix**: (AC1) widened `_INDICATOR_COLUMNS` and rendered SMA-200 (+ 50/200 golden/death-cross), ADX-14, ATR-14, %B, MACD-bullish-cross and a volume-vs-20-day-average line with canonical thresholds printed in-body; returns anchor on split-safe `adj_close`, 52-week on raw `high`/`low` to match a quote page and the shown raw close); these render on the DAILY section only; (AC3) a `_consensus_line` computes the multi-timeframe consensus in the template (majority rule, ties -> Sideways) and the majority-rule instruction was removed from `SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `FOCUSED_SYSTEM_PROMPT` + `focused.py` + one golden, replaced by a quote-the-consensus rule (pinned by `test_prompts_quote_consensus_line_not_majority_rule`). **AC4 dev-execution caught a real bug**: clickhouse_connect binds the date param as a String literal, which CH `toYear`/`subtractYears` reject — fixed with `toDate()`; live curl of `/api/v1/reports/technical/NVDA` then rendered every new line with real values (SMA-200 +5.98% golden cross, 52-week 161.61-236.54 close -14.27% from high, performance 1m -2.60 / 3m +10.39 / YTD +8.86 / 1y +24.66, volume 0.89x). **AC5**: the new YTD/52-week/1y quick_facts now answer with `(source: technical)` citations (NVDA YTD +8.86%, 52-week high 236.54, AAPL 1y +50.36%; a compact-technical variant built while chasing it was **reverted**). Root cause = comparison-output growth on main (QNT-350/355/303 prompt edits + QNT-354 SCALE block) vs the QNT-351 1500 cap; filed as **QNT-358**. `code-reviewer-ediff` caught one blocker fixed inline — the `_fetch_price_context` outer query lacked a `date <= anchor` upper bound, so `adj_now`/`high_52w`/`low_52w` could reflect a later raw-ingest bar than the report's shown close under ingest lag; bounded the outer `WHERE`. Kept two surgical report-design improvements from the investigation: extras render DAILY-only (SMA-200 needs 200 bars -> always N/M on weekly/monthly) and terser lines (%B folded onto the Bollinger line). AC1/AC2/AC3 code; AC4/AC5 dev-execution-verified (receipts above); AC6 docs (report-improvement-v1.md C-1/C-2/C-5/C-6/C-7 marked SHIPPED — gitignored personal doc). Verification: ruff/format/pyright clean, `make test` 1716 passed. Out of scope per ticket: fundamental + news templates (QNT-354/356); the 2-ticker comparison output budget (pre-existing -> QNT-358).
- [x] Eval harness spine: shared runner, history envelope, and gates across the eight suites — QNT-293
    - **Triggered by**: the 2026-07-02 AI-engineering architecture review (`docs/AI Engineering improvement plan v2.md`, item A-6). `packages/agent/src/agent/evals/` had grown to eight harnesses (golden_set, dialogue_eval, deepeval_eval, retrieval_eval, rag_impact_eval, rag_smoke_eval, news_search_eval, routing_eval), each with its own runner, output format, and env-gating — "did anything regress" was eight commands, and every cross-cutting change touched up to eight files. That drift already bit once: the prompt-version hash was hand-synced between `graph.py` and `golden_set.py` and silently diverged until QNT-230 unified it. **A shared spine, not a rewrite**: new `agent/evals/spine.py` owns the pieces that must stay identical — the **history envelope** (`HISTORY_PATH` + the 52-column ragged `HISTORY_FIELDS`, which had been *defined in golden_set.py and imported by the others*, the exact drift smell), the **run-identity** helpers (`git_sha` / `prompt_version`, the latter still lazy-importing `agent.graph` to avoid a cycle), and the **gating primitives** (`threshold_from_env` generalising the golden `EVAL_MIN_JUDGE` parser, plus a `SuiteResult(summary, failed, run_id, warning)` contract). **One CLI**: `python -m agent.evals` with no flag runs the golden set exactly as before (default), `--suite {golden,retrieval}` dispatches the ci.yml-gating pair through the spine via a `_SUITES` table (`retrieval` lazy-imports `ir_measures` so the golden path never needs it). **Minimal blast radius (the key decision)**: `golden_set.py` re-exports the envelope from spine under the historical names (`_git_sha`/`_prompt_version`/`HISTORY_FIELDS`/`HISTORY_PATH`/`fail_threshold_from_env`), so the four un-migrated suites (dialogue, deepeval, rag_impact) and every test import unchanged; only the two migrated suites (golden via the CLI, retrieval) point at spine directly — the other six fold in opportunistically when next touched. **Design decision — kept the wide committed `history.csv`**: the ticket sketches the shared schema as a `metrics`-as-JSON column, but the real `history.csv` is one wide CSV all eight suites append to (keyed by `eval_type`); converting it now would be the maximal cross-cutting change (rewrites read/write in all eight), risk the AC2 parity check, and discard the committed quality trend — directly against the ticket's own "do NOT big-bang" + "semantics frozen". So the shared *envelope* was extracted and the wide CSV preserved; the JSON-column shape is documented in `spine.py` + README as the eventual target once all eight fold. **Correction to my first read**: the CI retrieval gate is a pytest `-m eval` marker (`test_retrieval_eval.py` calls `compute_metrics`/`gate_failures` directly), NOT the CLI — so `ci.yml` needed zero change (AC3), and `--suite retrieval` is an additional offline entry to the same `score_offline` path. **`code-reviewer-ediff` returned FIX FIRST on one real issue**: the golden `EVAL_MIN_JUDGE` sub-threshold path emitted its `[fail]` line to stderr *before* `main()` printed the stdout summary, inverting the historical stdout-then-stderr order (AC1 "same output shape") — fixed by routing the diagnostic through `SuiteResult.warning` so `main()` prints stdout summary first, then stderr, locked by a CLI channel-split test; two advisories accepted (broadened exception scope — exit codes unchanged; AC2 evidence recorded in the PR body). AC1 code (default golden in `_SUITES`, stdout composition byte-identical; pinned by `tests/agent/evals/test_spine.py`); AC2 dev-execution-verified (old `python -m agent.evals.retrieval_eval` vs new `--suite retrieval` → identical stdout + exit 0, locked as a standing detector); AC3 code (`ci.yml` unchanged, `make test` 1570 passed); AC4 docs (`spine.py` docstring + README "Shared spine" section). Out of scope: changing any metric/threshold/fixture/judge (semantics frozen), folding the remaining six suites, the JSON-column history envelope, online/scheduled judged sampling (QNT-292).

- [ ] README factual-currency pass + repo metadata (partial ship 2026-07-08) — QNT-282
    - **Triggered by**: a hiring-manager README review, refreshed 2026-07-08 after the Groq-decommission arc (ADR-025/026/027) left the README asserting a stale provider/cost story.
